Shahadat — Testimony

6 min
Accepting Witnesses for Freedom Without a Claim
Discussion on accepting witnesses for freedom without a prior claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts witnesses for original freedom without a claim, and identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view.

Core Idea
In rights of Allah, a formal claim is not required; the prohibition of the womb suffices for accepting testimony.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a formal claim is a prerequisite for accepting testimony in matters of original freedom. The majority view holds that because the prohibition of marrying the freed person's mother is a right of Allah, witnesses are accepted without a claim. However, some Hanafi scholars require a claim due to hiddenness of lineage. We'll examine the proofs and analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
Read the passage to understand that the dispute is about whether a claim (daʿwā) is required for accepting witnesses in cases of original freedom (ḥurriyyat al-aṣl). Note the majority Hanafi position and the opposing view (qīla).
The majority view is that no claim is needed; the opposing view says a claim is required.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof: linking to rights of Allah
The Hanafi position rests on the principle that the prohibition of the womb (the right of Allah over the person) makes the matter fall under ḥuqūq Allāh, where daʿwā is not a condition. Trace how the text connects freedom to the prohibition of the mother's marriage.
The key phrase is 'ḥurmat al-farj' (prohibition of the vulva) as a right of Allah.
3
Examine the analogies (qiyas) provided
The author gives three analogies: (1) a slave-girl whose manumission is witnessed while she is silent, (2) a divorced woman (mukhtaliʿa) who brings evidence of triple divorce after khulʿ, (3) a mukatib who brings evidence of manumission after kitaba. For each, explain why the analogy proves the permissibility of accepting testimony without a claim.
All analogies share the element that the party may be unaware of the fact, and the master/husband has exclusive power to effect the change.
4
Analyze the opposing view and the Hanafi response
The opposing view argues that hiddenness of lineage (khafāʾ al-ʿulūq) may lead to contradictions if a person initially acknowledges slavery and later claims freedom. The Hanafi response is that such contradiction does not invalidate the claim because in these analogous cases, the party may have been unaware initially.
The text states: 'contradiction in matters where there is hiddenness does not prevent the validity of the claim.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢ . لتضمنه تحريم فرج الدم ، فإنَّ الشخص إذا كان حرَّ الأصل يكون فرج أمه حراماً على من يدعي أنها ملكه، وحرمة الفرج من حقوق الله الله، وفي حقوق الله الله لا يشترط الدعوى، فتقبلُ الشُّهودُ بغير بينة، وهذا كما أنَّ رجلين شهدا أنّ هذه الأمة أعتقها مولاه، وهي ساكتة ثبت حرمتها بدون دعواها ; لأنَّ الفرج حق الله تعالى. وقيل : الدعوى شرط في حريَّة الأصل أيضاً لخفاء العلوق، فإنّه قد يجلب عن دار الحرب صغيراً ولا يعلم حريَّة أبيه أو أمه فيقر بالرّق، ثم يعلم بحريَّة أُمه أو أبيه فيدعي الحرية، والتناقض فيما يجري فيه الخفاء لا يمنع صحة الدعوى. . وإن كان وضع المسألة في الحريَّةِ بالإعتاق ، فالتناقض لا يمنع صحة الدعوى ; لاستقلال المولى بالإعتاق فربّما لا يعلمُ العبد إعتاقه، ثم يعلم بعد ذلك، فصار كالمختلعة تقيمُ البينة على الطلقات الثلاث قبل الخلع. فإن البينة تقبل هاهنا ; لأنَّ الزوج ينفرد بالطلاق ، فربما لم تكن عالمةً عند الخلع، ثم علمت ، وصار كالمكاتب يقيم البينة على الإعتاق قبل الكتابة، فإنّها تقبلُ منه لاستبدادِ سيّده بالتحرير، هذا ما تخصُّصته من شروح «الهداية»
2. Because it includes the prohibition of the vulva of blood. For when a person is originally free, the vulva of his mother is prohibited for anyone who claims that she is his property. And the prohibition of the vulva is among the rights of Allah, and in the rights of Allah, a claim is not a condition. Thus the witnesses are accepted without evidence. And this is like when two men witness that this slave-girl was manumitted by her master, and she is silent, her prohibition (of marriage) is established without her claim, because the vulva is a right of Allah. And it was said: the claim is a condition for original freedom as well, due to the hiddenness of the pregnancy, for he may have been brought from dar al-harb as a child and does not know the freedom of his father or mother, so he acknowledges slavery, then later learns of his mother's or father's freedom and claims freedom. And contradiction in matters where there is hiddenness does not prevent the validity of the claim. And if the issue is placed in freedom by manumission, then contradiction does not prevent the validity of the claim, because the master is independent in manumission, so the slave might not know of his manumission, then later learns. So it is like the woman who is divorced (mukhtali'a) who establishes evidence of the three divorces before the khul'. For evidence is accepted here because the husband is independent in divorce, so she might not have known at the time of khul', then later learned. And it is like the mukatib who establishes evidence of manumission before the kitaba, for it is accepted from him because his master is independent in freeing. This is what I extracted from the commentaries of al-Hidaya.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage discusses a crucial point in Hanafi law: whether a claim (daʿwā) is a prerequisite for accepting testimony in cases of freedom (ḥurriyya). The author presents the Hanafi position that when witnesses testify that a person is free, their testimony is accepted even without a prior claim, because the prohibition of marrying the person's mother falls under the rights of Allah (ḥuqūq Allāh), which do not require a claim. He supports this with analogies: the case of a slave-girl whose manumission is witnessed (she is silent), the case of a woman who establishes evidence of divorce after khulʿ, and the case of a mukātab who establishes evidence of manumission after the kitāba. All these share the feature that the party (slave, woman) may not have known the fact earlier, and contradiction in such matters does not invalidate the claim. However, the author also notes an opposing view (qīla) that a claim is required for original freedom due to the hiddenness of lineage. This appears to be an intra-Hanafi difference.

Key Terms
حريَّة الأصل (ḥurriyyat al-aṣl): Original freedom, i.e., being born free as opposed to being a freed slave.
دعوى (daʿwā): A formal claim or lawsuit initiated by a party.
حقوق الله (ḥuqūq Allāh): Rights of God, which include matters of public morality and religious obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are witnesses for freedom accepted without a claim?
A) Because freedom is a fundamental right.
B) Because the prohibition of the womb is a right of Allah.
C) Because the claimant is always the slave.
D) Because the defendant has no standing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts witnesses for original freedom without a prior claim because the prohibition of the womb is a right of Allah, which does not require a formal claim.

Does Sealing a Witness Document Bar Later Ownership Claims?
Clarifying that sealing does not automatically bar claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a witness's sealing of a sale document bars a later ownership claim and explain the distinction between sealing and formal testimony.

Core Idea
Sealing a document does not imply acknowledgment; only testimony before a judge bars later ownership claims.

Imagine a person witnesses a property sale and seals the deed (affixes his signet). Later, he claims the property is actually his. Does his seal prevent him from asserting ownership? According to the Hanafi school, the answer is no — sealing alone is not an admission. This lesson unpacks the reasoning: sealing served to prevent forgery, not to affirm the seller's ownership. Only if the witness testified formally before a judge does the claim become barred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action in question
The witness writes his testimony on the sale document and affixes his seal (khātim). The question is whether this act constitutes an acknowledgment of the seller’s ownership.
2
State the default ruling
The text rules: 'no' — the witness's later claim of ownership is not invalidated by the mere act of sealing. The claim is still heard.
The phrase "وختم لا" means sealing alone does not bar the claim.
3
Understand the rationale
Sealing was customary for preservation against tampering. It is not a declaration of the seller's ownership because a sale can occur by a non-owner (e.g., a unauthorized sale subject to ratification). The witness may have written testimony simply to record the event or to evaluate the sale later.
The text distinguishes from ضمان الدرك (guarantee against claim), which is an explicit acknowledgment.
4
Identify the exception
If the witness testifies before a judge (shahāda ʿinda al-ḥākim) regarding the sale, then his claim is barred. Such testimony is considered an acknowledgment that the sale was valid and the seller owned the property.
The exception is based on the principle that a sane person intends his actions to be sound (al-ʿāqil yurīdu bi-taṣarrufihi al-ṣiḥḥa).
5
Apply the principle to related cases
The final note from al-Nahr: If the document contains wording that acknowledges ownership (e.g., explicit statement), then the seal reinforces that acknowledgment. Otherwise, the seal alone is neutral.
This shows that content matters; the seal is not an independent admission.

Source Text

Page 370. And if he testified and sealed, no. They said: If it is written in the document... (Zubdat al-Nihayah li-'Umdat al-Ri'ayah). (And if he testified and sealed, no): He said "and sealed" because the custom in previous times was that sealing in testimonies was for protection against alteration and substitution. (They said: If it is written in the document... as a pre-emptor, his pre-emption becomes void, and it is not rejected by revocation, for it is annulment not dissolution, for dissolution can only be without the opponent's consent. And if it was not conditional in it, then the intent is completion of the sale and its rulings, such that the buyer would not desire it except with the guarantee for fear of claim, so it becomes an acknowledgment from him that the seller was its owner at the time of sale, so his claim afterwards is not valid. [1] His statement: And if he testified and sealed, no; i.e., if he wrote his testimony in the purchase document and sealed that document, then the witness later claims that the house is his, his claim is not invalidated, rather it is heard, and the witness's writing and sealing on the document is not a delivery and acknowledgment that the sold property is the seller's property, because testimony cannot be conditional on sale due to lack of suitability, nor is it an acknowledgment of ownership. For sale may be from the owner or from someone else, and it is possible that he wrote the testimony to preserve the event or to consider the sale so that if he sees benefit in it he may ratify it, and there is nothing in it indicating its enforceability, unlike ضمان الدرك, which is an acknowledgment of the seller's ownership. [2] His statement: No; i.e., his claim is not invalidated unless he testified before the judge about the sale, and judgment was given on his testimony or not given, then it becomes delivery, so that his claim afterwards is not heard; because testimony of a sale against someone is an acknowledgment of the enforceability of the sale by agreement of the narrations; because a sane person intends correctness in his action, so it becomes as if he said: he sold while owning it, or sold an absolute enforceable sale. As in al-Tabyin. [3] His statement: The sealing...etc.; they used to seal after writing their names on the document out of fear of alteration and forgery, and the ruling does not differ. As in al-Minah. And in al-Nahr: I have not seen if they customarily make testimony only by sealing, and what should be relied upon is consideration of what is written in the document, for if it contains something that indicates acknowledgment of ownership, then the seal becomes an acknowledgment of it, otherwise no. End. [4] His statement: "wrote"; a passive verb, its subject is his statement: "sold his property" along with its conjuncts.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a person witnesses a sale and seals the document (i.e., puts his seal on the sale deed). The question is whether this act bars him from later claiming ownership of the property. The text rules: no, sealing alone does not bar the claim. The reason is that testimony and sealing are not an acknowledgment of the seller's ownership; they are merely to preserve the event. The seal was historically used for security against forgery. However, if the witness actually testifies before a judge (regarding the sale), then his claim is barred because such testimony is an acknowledgment that the sale is valid and binding. The commentary also distinguishes this from ضمان الدرك, which is a clear acknowledgment. The text cites various authorities: al-Tabyin, al-Minah, and al-Nahr. The final note from al-Nahr clarifies that the content of the document matters: if the document contains language acknowledging ownership, then the seal becomes an acknowledgment; otherwise, the seal alone is not sufficient. The underlying principle is that a sane person intends correctness in his actions, so testimony before a judge indicates the witness affirms the sale's validity.

Key Terms
ختم (khatam): The act of affixing one's seal (signet) on a document to authenticate it.
صك (sakk): A legal document, such as a deed of sale or a contract.
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony or witness statement; in this context, the act of witnessing a sale and writing that testimony on the document.
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): A claim that a property rightfully belongs to someone else, leading to eviction of the purchaser.
ضمان الدرك (ḍamān al-darak): A guarantee provided by the seller to the buyer against any prior claim (istihqāq) on the sold property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what circumstance does a witness's seal on a sale document bar him from later claiming ownership of the property?
A) If he sealed the document at the time of the sale
B) If he testified before a judge regarding the sale
C) If he was a relative of the buyer
D) If the document contains the word 'ownership'

Key Takeaway
A witness's seal on a sale document does not bar a later ownership claim; only formal testimony before a judge carries that effect.

Ruling on Prompting a Witness (Talqin)
Commentary explaining the prohibition of prompting a witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prompting a witness (talqin) and distinguish between permissible and disliked prompting.

Core Idea
Prompting a witness to say what he did not hear is makruh; reminding a fellow witness of what he forgot is not.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah clarifies an important distinction in the law of testimony. While it is prohibited to prompt a witness to utter words he did not hear, a witness may remind his co-witness of something already heard. Understanding this distinction helps avoid improper influence on testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of talqin
Recognize that talqin is prompting a witness to say something in his testimony that he did not personally witness.
2
State the general ruling
The text states that prompting a witness is 'makruh by consensus' (ittifaqan). This is a disliked act but not sinful.
The hukm is makruh tanzihi.
3
Identify the exception
One witness prompting his fellow witness is not makruh. This exception is explicitly mentioned by al-Birjandi.
The rationale: the co-witness is merely reminding of what was already heard, not introducing new information.
4
Apply the ruling
When encountering a scenario of talqin, determine who is prompting and whether the prompted content was heard by the witness.
If the prompter is not a fellow witness and the content is new, the act is makruh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذلك فيما لا يستفيد بتلقينه زيادة علم. [١]قوله : وذلـك...الخ ؛ فينبغي أن يذكر ما سمع منه ، ولا يقول : أشهد بكذا لِمَا لم يسمع منه، فإنه هو التلقين المكروه اتفاقا، أما تلقين أحد الشاهدين للآخر فغير مکروه، صرح به البرْجَندِيُّ في «شرح النُّقاية».
That is in a case where prompting does not confer additional knowledge. [1] His statement: 'That... etc': so he should mention what he heard from him, and he should not say: 'I testify to such-and-such' for what he did not hear from him, because that is the prompting which is disliked (makruh) by consensus. As for one of the two witnesses prompting the other, it is not disliked, as stated by al-Birjandi in Sharh al-Niqayah.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage from the commentary clarifies the ruling on prompting (talqin) a witness. The matn stated that prompting is only problematic when it does not bring additional knowledge. The commentator explains: the witness should only testify to what he personally heard. If he is prompted to say something he did not hear, that is makruh (disliked) by consensus. However, if one witness prompts his fellow witness (reminding him of something he already heard but forgot), that is not makruh. This distinction is explicitly mentioned by al-Birjandi in his commentary on al-Niqayah.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqīn): Prompting a witness to say something he did not hear or to testify in a particular manner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a judge prompting a witness to say something he did not hear?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
Prompting a witness to testify about something he did not hear is makruh by consensus; however, one witness prompting his fellow witness is not makruh.

Definition and Introduction to Testimony (Shahadah)
Opening definition and placement rationale for Kitab al-Shahadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of shahādah and explain why it is placed after adjudication in fiqh texts.

Core Idea
Testimony is a judicial informing of another's right; it comes after judgment because it is needed only upon denial.

This lesson opens the Book of Testimony from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. The author justifies placing testimony after adjudication, defines it linguistically and legally, and discusses the inclusion of retraction. Understanding this foundation is essential for the Hanafi law of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the placement rationale
Identify the two reasons given for placing testimony after adjudication: the judge needs it only at denial, and testimony is not binding without a judge's decision.
2
Distinguish linguistic vs. legal meaning
Note the lexical uses (seeing, attending, swearing) and contrast with the legal definition: ikhbār bi ḥaqq lil-ghayr ‘alā ākhar.
The legal definition is narrower and specific to court testimony.
3
Understand the inclusion of retraction
See that retraction is included as a nullifier, analogous to nullifiers of purity. Compare with al-Hidayah's separate treatment.
This reflects different organizational preferences, not a legal disagreement.
4
Identify the conditions and virtues
The text mentions many conditions (21) and the Quranic command to be just witnesses.
Details will follow in later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها
[١]
قوله : كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها ؛ اعلم أنَّ المتبادر كان تقديم مسائل الشهادة على القضاء ؛ لأنَّ القضاء موقوف على الشهادة، إذا كان ثبوت الحق بها، لكن أخرها ؛ لأنَّ القاضي يحتاج إليها عند الإنكار فكان ذلك من تتمة حكمه، أو لأنَّ الشهادة إنّما تقبلُ في مجلس القضاء، ولا تكون ملزمة بدون القضاء.
والرجوع عن الشهادة وإن كان رفعاً للشهادة، لكنه داخـل تحـتـهـا : كدخـول نواقض الطهارة في الطهارة ؛ ولذا أورده في كتاب الشهادة»، وذكــره صاحب «الهداية»(۱) في كتاب على حدة ؛ نظراً إلى أنه مبائن لها ، ومبائن الشيء قسم برأسه غير مندرج تحته، والشهادة : خبر درست واگاهي قاطع وكشتكي ورداه خداي تعالى. كذا في (منتهی الأرب».
يقال : شهدت الشيء : اطلعت عليه وعاينته ، وأنا شاهد، والجمع أشهاد وشهود، مثل شريف وأشراف، وقاعد وقعود، ويعدى بالهمزة، فيقال: أشهدته الشيء، وشهدت العيد أدركته وشاهدته مشاهدة ، مثل : عاينته معاينة وزناً ومعني، وشهد بالله : حلف ، وشهدت المجلس : حضرتُه فأنا شاهد، وشهيد أيضاً.
وعليه قوله : فَمَن شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمْهُ (۲) ؛ أي من كان حاضراً في الشهر مقيماً غير مسافرٍ فليصم ما حضر وأقام فيه، وأشهد بكذا شهادة يتعدى بالباء ؛ لأنه بمعنى أخبر به، قال ابن فارس: الشهادة الإخبار بما قد شوهد. كذا في «المصباح المنير»(۳)، وإن شئت زيادة التفصيل فارجع إليه.
وفي الشريعة : ما ذكره المصنف الله بقوله : هي إخبار بحق للغير على آخر. شروطها كثيرة، تأتي في أثناء المسائل إن شاء الله ، حتى قال صاحب «البحر») : إنَّ شرائطها : أحد وعشرون ومحاسنها كثيرة منها : امتثال الأمر في قوله
كُونُوا قَوْمِينَ لِلَّهِ شُهَدَاءَ بِالْقِسْطِ (٥)
Book of Testimony and Retraction Thereof. [1] His saying: Book of Testimony and Retraction thereof; know that the immediate inclination was to present the issues of testimony before those of adjudication, because adjudication depends on testimony, since the establishment of right is by it. But he delayed it because the judge needs it at the time of denial, so that was part of his ruling, or because testimony is only accepted in the court of adjudication and is not binding without adjudication. Retraction of testimony, although it is a removal of testimony, is included under it as the nullifiers of purity are included under purity; hence he included it in the Book of Testimony. The author of Al-Hidayah mentioned it in a separate book, considering that it is distinct from testimony, and a distinct thing is a separate section not included under it. Testimony (ash-shahadah) is: a certain report, absolute knowledge, a statement, and a witness for God Almighty. This is in Muntaha al-Arab. It is said: shahidtu ash-shay'a: I became aware of it and saw it, and I am a shahid (witness); the plural is ashhad and shuhud, like sharif and ashraf, qa'id and qu'ud. It is made transitive with the hamzah, so it is said: ashadtuhu ash-shay'a (I made him witness it). Shahidtu al-'id (I attended the festival) means I reached it and witnessed it, like 'ayantu mu'ayanah in form and meaning. Shahida Billah means he swore. Shahidtu al-majlis means I attended it, so I am a shahid and also shahid. Upon this is His saying: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (Al-Baqarah 2:185); i.e., whoever is present in the month, resident not traveling, let him fast what he is present in it. Ashhadu bi kadha shahadah is transitive with ba' because it means to inform with it. Ibn Faris said: Al-Shahadah is informing about what has been witnessed. This is in Al-Misbah al-Munir. And if you wish for further detail, refer to it. In Shari'ah: It is what the author - may God have mercy on him - mentioned in his saying: It is an informing of a right belonging to another against someone else. Its conditions are many, to come in the issues if God wills. Even the author of Al-Bahr said: Its conditions are twenty-one, and its merits are many, including compliance with the command in His saying: 'Be maintainers of justice, witnesses for God' (Al-Ma'idah 5:8).
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This opening passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah introduces the Book of Testimony (Kitab al-Shahadah). The commentator begins by justifying why the author placed the book on testimony after adjudication (al-qada') rather than before. Intuitively, testimony should precede because judgment depends on it—rights are proven through testimony. However, the author delayed it because the judge only needs testimony at the point of denial, making it a completion of the judge's ruling; alternatively, because testimony is only accepted in a judicial setting and is not binding without a judge's decision. This shows the interdependence of testimony and adjudication.

Next, the commentator discusses retraction of testimony (al-ruju' 'an al-shahadah). Although retraction nullifies testimony, it is included in this book because it is a nullifier (nawqid) of the act, similar to how nullifiers of purity (nawaqid al-taharah) are included in the book of purity. The author of al-Hidayah, however, treated retraction in a separate chapter, viewing it as distinct from testimony itself.

The passage then defines shahadah linguistically (lughatan) and legally (shar'an). Lexically, shahadah means a definitive report (khabar durust), absolute awareness (agahi qati'), and a statement of verification. The commentator gives various usages: 'shahidtu al-shay'a' (I saw it), 'shahidtu al-'id' (I attended it), 'shahidtu Billah' (I swore by God). The plural forms are ashhad and shuhud. The word can be made transitive with the hamzah: 'ashadtuhu' (I made him witness).

The legal definition, as stated by the author (the original matn), is: 'Informing of a right belonging to another against someone else' (ikhbar bi haqq lil-ghayr 'ala akhar). This definition restricts testimony to claims involving a right (haqq) due to another person (al-ghayr) against a defendant (akhar). Thus, testimony about one's own right or about non-legal matters is not included. The commentator notes that the conditions of testimony are numerous (twenty-one conditions according to some), and these will be explained throughout the book. He also highlights the virtue of testimony by citing the Quranic verse (Al-Ma'idah 5:8) commanding justice in testimony.

This lesson lays the foundation for understanding the Hanafi law of evidence, distinguishing testimony from mere information, and framing it within the judicial process.

Key Terms
الشهادة (ash-shahādah): Informing (ikhbār) of a right (ḥaqq) belonging to another (al-ghayr) against someone else (akhar).
شاهد (shāhid): One who witnesses/testifies; plural ash-hād and shuhūd.
الرجوع عن الشهادة (ar-rujū‘ ‘an ash-shahādah): Retraction of testimony; considered a nullifier included in the book of testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal (shar‘ī) definition of shahādah?
A) A general report of anything witnessed.
B) Informing of a right belonging to another against someone else.
C) Swearing an oath by God.
D) Attending a court session.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of testimony restricts it to judicial informing of a right belonging to another, and retraction is its nullifier.

The Definition of Shahada and Its Legal Framework
Defines shahada linguistically and legally, distinguishes three types of notifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of shahada and distinguish it from claim and confession.

Core Idea
Shahada is a report of another’s right against a third party, accepted only in court.

Testimony (shahada) is a foundational concept in Islamic judicial procedure. This passage opens the Book of Testimony by clarifying its definition—both linguistically and legally—and explaining why the chapter is placed after judgment. Understanding this definition is essential for distinguishing testimony from other types of legal notifications such as claims and confessions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic origins of shahada
Explore the Arabic roots: shahada means to witness, see, attend, or take an oath. Note the plural forms and transitive uses.
The linguistic definition includes meanings like 'correct report' and 'decisive knowledge'.
2
Extract the legal (sharʿī) definition
The author states: 'It is an informing of a right belonging to another person against another.' This is the core legal definition.
Observe that the right is for someone else (al-ghayr) and against another party (ʿalā ākhar).
3
Distinguish the three types of notifications (al-ikhbārāt)
The passage categorizes all legal notifications into three: testimony (right of a third party against another), claim (right of the informant against another), and confession (right of another against the informant).
This tripartite division helps avoid confusion between different legal statements.
4
Note the condition of the court of judgment
The passage explains that testimony is only accepted in the court (majlis al-qaḍāʾ) and is not binding outside it. This is a key condition.
Examples: Testimony for adultery or crescent sighting may be considered testimony in a broader sense but not in the legal sense defined here.
5
Understand the inclusion of revocation within the book
Although revocation (rujūʿ) removes testimony, it is included in the Book of Testimony by analogy with nullifiers of purity. The author of al-Hidayah placed it separately, but most follow the inclusion.
This highlights the principle that related matters are often grouped together for completeness.

Source Text

كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها اعلم أن المتبادر كان تقديم مسائل الشهادة على القضاء لأن القضاء موقوف على الشهادة إذا كان ثبوت الحق بها لكن أخرها لأن القاضي يحتاج إليها عند الإنكار فكان ذلك من تتمة حكمه أو لأن الشهادة إنما تقبل في مجلس القضاء ولا تكون ملزمة بدون القضاء والرجوع عن الشهادة وإن كان رفعا للشهادة لكنه داخل تحتها كدخول نواقض الطهارة في الطهارة ولذا أورده في كتاب الشهادة وذكره صاحب الهداية في كتاب على حدة نظرا إلى أنه مبائن لها ومبائن الشيء قسم برأسه غير مندرج تحته والشهادة خبر درست وگاهي قاطع وكشتكي ورداه خداي تعالى كذا في منتهى الأرب يقال شهدت الشيء اطلعت عليه وعاينته وأنا شاهد والجمع أشهاد وشهود مثل شريف وأشراف وقاعد وقعود ويعدى بالهمزة فيقال أشهدته الشيء وشهدت العيد أدركته وشاهدته مشاهدة مثل عاينته معاينة وزنا ومعنى وشهد بالله حلف وشهدت المجلس حضرته فأنا شاهد وشهيد أيضا وعليه قوله فمن شهد منكم الشهر فليصمه أي من كان حاضرا في الشهر مقيما غير مسافر فليصم ما حضر وأقام فيه وأشهد بكذا شهادة يتعدى بالباء لأنه بمعنى أخبر به قال ابن فارس الشهادة الإخبار بما قد شوهد كذا في المصباح المنير وإن شئت زيادة التفصيل فارجع إليه وفي الشريعة ما ذكره المصنف بقوله هي إخبار بحق للغير على آخر شروطها كثيرة تأتي في أثناء المسائل إن شاء الله حتى قال صاحب البحر إن شرائطها أحد وعشرون ومحاسنها كثيرة منها امتثال الأمر في قوله كونوا قومين لله شهداء بالقسط هي إخبار بحق للغير على آخر الإخبارات ثلاثة إما بحق للغير على آخر وهو الشهادة أو بحق للمخبر على آخر وهو الدعوى أو بالعكس وهو الإقرار وبهذا يندفع الاعتراضات كذا ذكره البرجندي في شرح النقاية
The Book of Testimony and Its Revocation. Know that the immediate understanding was to present the issues of testimony before judgment because judgment depends on testimony when the establishment of the right is through it, but he delayed it because the judge needs it at the time of denial, so that was a completion of his judgment, or because testimony is only accepted in the court of judgment and is not binding without judgment. Revocation of testimony, although it is a removal of testimony, is included under it, like the inclusion of nullifiers of purity in purity. Therefore, he included it in the Book of Testimony, while the author of al-Hidayah mentioned it in a separate book, considering that it is distinct from it, and something distinct is a division by itself not included under it. Testimony: a correct report, decisive knowledge, testimony, and the garment of Allah, the Exalted. Thus in Muntaha al-Arab. It is said: I witnessed the thing, i.e., I became acquainted with it and saw it, and I am a witness; the plural is ashhad and shuhud, like sharif and ashraf, and qa'id and qu'ud. It is made transitive with the hamza, so it is said: I made him witness the thing. I witnessed the Eid, i.e., I attained it and witnessed it as an eyewitness, like: I saw it as a viewing, in form and meaning. He swore by Allah: he took an oath. I witnessed the assembly: I attended it, so I am a witness, also a shahid. Based on this is His statement: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (Quran 2:185), meaning whoever is present in the month, residing, not traveling, let him fast whatever he is present and resides therein. And he testified to something: a testimony, it is transitive with the ba' because it means he informed by it. Ibn Faris said: Testimony is informing about what has been witnessed. Thus in al-Misbah al-Munir. If you wish for further detail, refer to it. In the Shariah, it is what the author mentioned by his statement: 'It is an informing of a right belonging to another person against another.' Its conditions are many, they will come in the course of the issues, Allah willing, until the author of al-Bahr said: Its conditions are twenty-one, and its merits are many, including compliance with the command in His statement: 'Be upholders of justice, witnesses for Allah' (Quran 5:8). It is an informing of a right for another person against another. The notifications are three: either a right belonging to another person against another — this is testimony; or a right belonging to the informant against another — this is a claim; or the opposite — this is confession. And with this, objections are repelled. Thus mentioned by al-Birjandi in Sharh al-Nuqaya.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Testimony and begins by justifying why the chapter on testimony is placed after the chapter on judgment, whereas one might expect it to precede it, since judgment depends on testimony for establishing rights. The author provides two reasons: first, the judge needs testimony only when there is a denial, so it is a completion of his judgment; second, testimony is only accepted in the court of judgment and is not binding without it. Then, the author addresses the inclusion of revocation of testimony within this book, explaining that although revocation is a removal of testimony, it is included under it, just as nullifiers of purity are included in the book of purity. The author of al-Hidayah placed it in a separate book because he considered it distinct. The linguistic definition is then given: testimony is a 'correct report,' 'decisive knowledge,' 'testimony,' and 'the garment of Allah.' Various linguistic derivations are explained: shahada means to see or witness, and it is used for oaths and attendance. The legal definition is taken from the author of the matn: 'It is an informing of a right belonging to another person against another.' The author notes that there are many conditions, enumerated by the author of al-Bahr as twenty-one. Then, three types of notifications are distinguished: testimony (right of another against a third party), claim (right of the informant against another), and confession (right of another against the informant). Finally, an additional condition is mentioned: the testimony must be in the court of judgment, and examples of excluded cases are given, such as testimony for adultery and sighting of the crescent moon, with a note that these can also be considered testimony in a broader sense. The passage concludes with a statement that these definitions repel objections.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahāda): A report of a right belonging to another person against a third party, made in the court of judgment.
الإخبار (al-ikhbār): A notification, of which there are three types: testimony, claim, and confession.
شاهد (shāhid): One who gives testimony; also means one who is present or has witnessed something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Testimony, claim, and confession
B) Testimony, oath, and confession
C) Claim, denial, and oath
D) Testimony, admission, and denial

Key Takeaway
Shahada in Hanafi law is legally defined as an informing of a right belonging to another person against another, with the additional condition that it must be given in the court of judgment.

Obligation of Testimony When Requested by the Claimant
States that testifying is obligatory when the claimant requests it, and its ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which testifying becomes obligatory (fard) and explain the consequences of a judge's refusal to act on valid testimony.

Core Idea
Testimony becomes a personal obligation when the claimant requests it, and the judge must rule by it after tazkiyah.

This passage from a Hanafi legal commentary clarifies a crucial point: testifying is not always optional. When a claimant asks you to testify, it becomes your personal duty. Moreover, the judge is bound to decide based on that testimony once the witness's integrity is verified. The text also addresses the consequences if the judge refuses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what level of hukm applies. The act is 'testifying when requested by the claimant' and the ruling is 'fard' (specifically fard 'ayn).
The text uses 'يفترض أداؤها' meaning 'its performance is obligatory.'
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites consensus (ijma) and textual evidence (nusus) as the proof that testimony is binding, overriding the counterargument from qiyas.
The specific nusus are not quoted here but referenced as established in larger works.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling. Ijma and nusus definitively establish that testimony must be accepted and acted upon, despite the theoretical possibility of falsehood.
Qiyas would suggest non-bindingness, but it is overridden by stronger evidence.
4
Analyze the consequences for the judge
If the judge refuses to rule by valid testimony, he sins, deserves dismissal (since sin makes him fasiq), is subject to ta'zir, and may become a disbeliever if he denies the obligation.
This highlights the gravity of the judge's duty.
5
Understand the overriding of qiyas
Recognize that the Hanafi method gives priority to nusus and ijma over qiyas when they conflict. The principle is that textual authority and consensus prevail.
This is a key usul principle illustrated here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وتجب بطلب المدعي يعني يفترض أداؤها إذا طلبت منه لقوله ركنتها استعمال لفظ الشهادة وحكمها فرض الحكم على القاضي بموجبها بعد التزكية فلو امتنع القاضي عن الحكم بها بعد وجود شرائطها أثم لتركه الفرض وهو قضاؤه بها واستحق العزل لأن الفاسق يستحقه على المذهب وعزر لارتكابه الممنوع شرعا وكفر إن لم يعتقد افتراض القضاء عليه بعد توفير شرائطه والقياس يأبى أن تكون الشهادة ملزمة لأنه خبر محتمل للصدق والكذب لكن ترك ذلك بالنصوص والإجماع وزيادة التحقيق والتفصيل في المبسوطات
His statement: 'And it becomes obligatory by the request of the claimant' means that its performance is obligatory when it is requested from him, due to His statement. Its pillar: using the word 'testimony.' Its ruling: it is obligatory for the judge to pass judgment based on it after verifying the integrity (tazkiyah). If the judge refrains from ruling by it after its conditions are met, he commits a sin because he abandons the obligation, which is his judgment by it, and he deserves dismissal because the sinful person deserves it according to the madhhab, and he is to be disciplined for committing what is legally prohibited, and he becomes a disbeliever if he does not believe that judgment upon him is obligatory after fulfilling its conditions. Qiyas (analogy) would reject that testimony is binding because it is a report that may be true or false, but that was abandoned based on texts (nusus) and consensus (ijma), and further investigation and detail are in the expansive works.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage expounds on the ruling that testimony becomes obligatory when the claimant requests it. The author explains 'obligatory' here means a personal obligation (fard) on the witness to testify. The pillar (rukn) of testimony is the utterance of the word 'shahada' (I testify). The legal effect (hukm) is that it becomes obligatory for the judge to pass judgment based on the testimony after verifying the witness's integrity (tazkiyah). If the judge refuses to judge by valid testimony, he sins, deserves dismissal (since he becomes sinful and a sinful person deserves dismissal according to the Hanafi madhhab), and is subject to discretionary punishment (ta'zir). If he does not believe that judging by it is obligatory, he commits disbelief (kufr). The passage then addresses a qiyas-based objection: testimony might be false, so it should not be binding. However, the Hanafi school responds that this objection is overridden by textual evidence (nusus from Quran and Sunnah) and consensus (ijma). The detailed discussion is found in larger works like al-Mabsut.

Key Terms
التزكية (al-tazkiya): Verifying the integrity of the witness, i.e., ensuring they are trustworthy and upright.
الركن (al-rukn): The pillar of testimony: uttering the word 'shahada' (I testify).
الإجماع (al-ijma): Consensus of the scholars, used here to override qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does testifying become a personal obligation (fard) according to this passage?
A) When the judge requests it
B) When the claimant requests it
C) When the witness has direct knowledge
D) When the defendant denies the claim

Key Takeaway
Testimony becomes a personal obligation when the claimant requests it, and the judge must rule by it after verifying the witness's integrity; refusal by the judge leads to serious consequences.

Shahadat — Testimony

Definition and Obligation of Testimony (Shahada)
Defines testimony and states its obligation with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define testimony (shahada) in Hanafi law, distinguish it from claim (da'wa) and confession (iqrar), and identify the conditions under which it becomes individually obligatory (fard 'ayn).

Core Idea
Testimony is a report of another's right given in court; it becomes an individual obligation upon request when accepted by the judge.

Testimony (shahada) is a cornerstone of Islamic judicial proof. This lesson explains its precise definition, distinguishing it from da'wa and iqrar, and establishes the ruling that it becomes a personal obligation (fard 'ayn) when requested by the claimant and accepted by the judge. We will examine the Quranic proofs and the Hanafi principle that a prohibition of refusal implies a command to testify.

Guided Path
1
Deconstruct the definition
Identify the four key elements: informative report (ikhbar), right of another, against another, and implicitly in court.
The definition excludes claims (da'wa) and confessions (iqrar).
2
Distinguish testimony from other reports
Classify reports into three categories: testimony (right of another against another), claim (right of self against another), confession (right of another against self).
Also exclude counseling and denial.
3
Identify the rukn and ruling
The rukn is uttering the word 'shahada'. The ruling is that the judge must judge by it; for the witness, it becomes fard 'ayn upon request.
The witness sins if he refuses knowing the judge will accept.
4
Analyze the Quranic proof and usul principle
The prohibition of refusal (2:282) and concealment (2:283) imply a command to testify, based on the Hanafi principle that prohibition of an act with a single opposite is a command of that opposite.
This makes testimony a fard 'ayn upon request.
5
Consider exceptions and conditions
The obligation is lifted if the judge would not accept the testimony, if another suffices, or if hardship (e.g., long distance) exists.
Also, old age or lack of transport may excuse, but claimant providing transport may change the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هي إخبار بحق للغير على آخر، وتَحِبُ (هي إخبار بحق للغير على آخر)، الإخبارات ثلاثة :
١. إما بحق للغير على آخر، وهو الشَّهادة. ٢ . أو بحق للمخبر على آخر، وهو الدعوى.
. أو بالعكس، وهو الإقرار.
(وتحب بطلب المدعى)
وركتها : استعمال لفظ الشهادة.
وحكمها : فرض الحكم على القاضي بموجبها بعد التزكية، فلو امتنع القاضي عن الحكم بها بعد وجودِ شرائطها أثم ؛ لتركه الفرض ، وهو قضاؤه بها، واستحق العزل ؛ لأنَّ الفاسق يستحقه على المذهب، وعُزّرَ لارتكابه الممنوع شرعاً ، وكفر إن لم يعتقد افتراض القضاء عليه بعد توفير شرائطه.
والقياس يأبى أن تكون الشهادة ملزمة ؛ لأنه خبر محتمل للصدق والكذب، لكن
ترك ذلك بالنصوص والإجماع، وزيادة التحقيق والتفصيل في المبسوطات. [1] قوله : هي إخبار ... الخ ؛ فالإخبار يتناول المجاوزة والشهادة والدعوى والإنكار. وقوله بحق ؛ يخرج المجاوزة.
وقوله : للغير؛ أي لغير المخبر، يخرجُ الدّعوى ، وكذا يخرج الإنكار، فإنّه إخبار بما في يده لنفسه. وقوله : على آخر ؛ يخرج الإقرار، ولا بد من قيد آخر، وهو قولنا : في مجلس الحكم ؛ ليخرج ما ليس في مجلس الحكم، فإنّه لا يسمّى شهادة، ويدخل في هذا التعريف دعوى الوكيل، ويخرجُ عنه الشهادة في الزنا والشهادة في هلال رمضان ، وهلال العيد، إلا أن يقال : إنه يثبت بذلك حقُّ الحد للشارع على الزاني، وحق الصوم أو الفطر على المكلّف. فإنَّ المراد بالإخبار أعم من أن يكون بلا واسطة أو بواسطة ؛ كالشهادة بالبيع ، فإنّها بالواسطة شهادة بحق الثمن للبائع على المشتري ، وإلا ظهر أن يقال : هي الإخبار بصحة الشيء عن عيان أو سماع في مجلس الحكم على وجه لا يعود منفعته أو ضرره إلى المخبر، بذلك يندفع الاعتراضات كذا ذكره البرْجَندِي في «شرح النُّقاية».
[٢] قوله : وتجب بطلب المدعي ؛ يعني يفترض أداؤها إذا طلبت منه ؛ لقوله :
وَلَا يَأْبَ الشُّهَدَاءُ إِذَا مَا دُعُوا ) ، وقوله : ( وَلَا تَكْتُمُوا الشَّهَادَةً وَمَن يَكْتُمْهَا فَإِنَّهُ : ايم قلبه (۲) ، وهذا إن كان نهياً عن الإباء والكتمان، لكن النهي عن الشيء يكون أمراً بضده إذا كان له ضد واحد ؛ لأنَّ الانتهاء لا يكون إلا بالاشتغال به. فكان أداء الشهادة فرضاً قطعاً كفريضة الانتهاء عن الكتمان ، فصار كالأمر به بل أكد ؛ ولهذا أسند الإثم إلى الآلة التي وقع بها الفعل وهو القلب، لِمَا عُرِفَ أَنَّ إسناد الفعل إلى محله يكون أقوى من الإسنادِ إلى كلّه، فقوله : أبصرته بعيني أقوى من قولهم أبصرتُه ، وإسناده إلى أشرف الجوارح دليل على أنه أعظم الجرائم بعد الكفر بالله عالة. ثم إنما يأثم إذا علم أن القاضي يقبلُ شهادته وتعين عليه الأداء، وإن علم أن القاضى لا يقبل شهادته، أو كانوا جماعةً فأدَّى غيره من تقبل شهادته فقبلت ، قالوا : لا يأثم، وإن ادَّعى غيره، ولم تقبل شهادته يأثم من لم يؤد إذا كان ممن تقبل شهادته ؛ لأنَّ امتناعه يؤدي إلى تضييع الحقوق.
هذا إذا كان موضع الشاهد قريباً من موضع القاضي، وإن كان بعيداً بحيث لا يمكنه أن يَغْدُو إلى القاضي لأداء الشهادة ويرجع إلى أهله في يومه ذلك ، قالوا : لا يأثم ؛ لأنه يلحقه الضرر بذلك ، وقال : وَلَا يُضَارَ كَاتِبٌ وَلَا شَهِيدٌ (٣)
ثم إن كان الشاهد شيخاً كبيراً لا يقدر على المشي إلى مجلس الحكم وليس له
شيءٌ للركوب فأَرْكَبُه المدعي من عنده ، قالوا : لا بأس به، وتقبل شهادته ؛ لأنه من باب الإكرام للشهود ، وقال : أكرموا الشهود ) ، وإن كان يقدر وركبه المدعي من عنده قالوا : لا تقبل كذا في «التبيين» ) ، وغيره من المبسوطات.
[١]قوله : بطلب المدعي ؛ قال شيخ الإسلام الله : لو أخَّرَ الشاهد الشهادة بعد
It is informing of a right for another against another, and it is obligatory (by request of the claimant). The types of reports are three: 1. A right for another against another – that is testimony. 2. A right for the informant against another – that is a claim. 3. The opposite – that is confession. (And it becomes obligatory by request of the claimant). Its pillar is the use of the word 'testimony'. Its ruling is that the judge's judgment by it is obligatory after establishing the witnesses' integrity; if the judge refrains from judging by it after its conditions are fulfilled, he sins for abandoning the obligation, and he deserves removal because the sinner deserves it according to the madhhab, and he is disciplined for committing what is legally prohibited, and he becomes a disbeliever if he does not believe that judgment by it is obligatory after its conditions are fulfilled. Analogy would reject that testimony is binding because it is a report that may be true or false, but that is abandoned due to texts and consensus, and further verification and detail is found in the expanded works. [1] His statement: 'It is informing... etc.'; so 'informing' encompasses counseling, testimony, claim, and denial. His statement: 'of a right' excludes counseling. His statement: 'for another' i.e., other than the informant, excludes the claim, and also excludes denial, for it is informing of what is in his hand for himself. His statement: 'against another' excludes confession. Another condition is needed, which is our statement: 'in the court of judgment', to exclude what is not in the court, for it is not called testimony. This definition includes the claim of an agent, and excludes testimony about adultery and testimony about the crescent of Ramadan and Eid, unless it is said that by that the right of punishment for the Legislator against the adulterer is established, and the right of fasting or breaking fast against the obligated person. For the meaning of 'informing' is general, whether direct or indirect; like testimony of sale, for it indirectly is testimony of the right of price for the seller against the buyer. Otherwise it would appear to be said: it is informing of the soundness of a thing from sight or hearing in the court of judgment in a way that its benefit or harm does not return to the informant. By this the objections are repelled, as mentioned by al-Barjandi in 'Sharh al-Nuqayah'. [2] His statement: 'and it becomes obligatory by request of the claimant' means its performance becomes obligatory when requested from him, because of His statement: 'And let not the witnesses refuse when they are called' (2:282), and His statement: 'And do not conceal testimony, and whoever conceals it, then indeed his heart is sinful' (2:283). This is a prohibition against refusal and concealment, but the prohibition of something is a command of its opposite if it has a single opposite, because refraining is only by engagement in it. So the performance of testimony is definitely a duty like the duty of refraining from concealment, so it became like a command, even stronger. For this reason, sin is attributed to the instrument with which the act is done, the heart, because it is known that attributing an act to its place is stronger than attributing it to the whole, e.g., 'I saw it with my eye' is stronger than 'I saw it', and attributing it to the noblest organ indicates that it is the greatest sin after disbelief in Allah. Then he sins if he knows that the judge accepts his testimony and he is obliged to perform it. If he knows that the judge does not accept his testimony, or there is a group and someone else whose testimony is accepted performs it, they said: he does not sin. If another claims and his testimony is not accepted, then the one who did not perform sins if he is among those whose testimony is accepted, because his refusal leads to loss of rights. This is if the witness's place is near the judge's place. If it is far such that he cannot go to the judge to perform testimony and return to his family that same day, they said: he does not sin, because harm would befall him, and Allah said: 'Let no scribe be harmed, nor witness' (2:282). Then if the witness is an old man who cannot walk to the court and has no means of riding, and the claimant provides him with something to ride from his own, they said: there is no harm, and his testimony is accepted, because it is a form of honoring the witnesses, and it was said: 'Honor the witnesses'. If he is able to walk but the claimant rides him from his own, they said: it is not accepted, as stated in 'al-Tabyin' and other expanded works. [1] His statement: 'by request of the claimant'; Shaykh al-Islam said: if the witness delays the testimony after...
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage begins by defining testimony (shahada) as a specific type of report: informing of a right belonging to another person against another person. The author distinguishes testimony from other reports: if the right is for the speaker against another, it is a claim (da'wa); if it is for the speaker himself against another? Actually the text says: 'or a right for the informant against another, that is a claim' and the opposite (right of another against the informant) is confession (iqrar). So testimony is always about a right of a non-informant against a non-informant. The author then notes that testimony's pillar (rukn) is uttering the word 'shahada' (I testify). Its ruling is that the judge must rule by it after verifying the witness's integrity; if he refuses, he sins and is removed. The author then addresses a possible analogy that testimony should not be binding because it could be false, but this is overridden by Quranic texts and consensus. A more thorough definition is provided: testimony is informing of the soundness of something from sight or hearing in court, without benefit or harm returning to the witness. This excludes reports outside court. The passage then shifts to the obligation of giving testimony upon request. It becomes fard (obligatory) when requested by the claimant, based on Quran 2:282 ('Let not the witnesses refuse when they are called') and 2:283 ('Do not conceal testimony; whoever conceals it, his heart is sinful'). The author explains the legal principle: a prohibition of an act is a command of its opposite (if there is a single opposite). So prohibition of refusal is a command to testify. The sin is attributed to the heart for emphasis. The witness sins only if the judge would accept his testimony. If the judge would not accept it (e.g., the witness is not reliable), or if another witness suffices, he does not sin. The obligation is also affected by distance: if the witness lives far, he is not required to travel if it causes hardship (based on Quran 2:282, 'Let no witness be harmed'). If an old man cannot walk, the claimant may provide transport without issue, but if the witness can walk and the claimant provides transport, some say the testimony is not accepted (to avoid suspicion of bias). This discussion is found in 'al-Tabyin' and other expanded works.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Informing of a right of another against another in court, based on sight or hearing, without benefit or harm to the informant.
إخبار (ikhbar): A report; includes testimony, claim, confession, denial, and counseling.
دعوى (da'wa): A claim where the informant asserts a right for himself against another.
إقرار (iqrar): Confession: informing of a right of another against the informant himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does giving testimony become fard 'ayn (individually obligatory)?
A) As soon as a person witnesses an event
B) When the judge requests the testimony in court
C) When the claimant requests it and the witness knows the judge will accept it
D) Only if the witness is related to the claimant

Key Takeaway
Testimony (shahada) is a distinct legal report that becomes an individual obligation (fard 'ayn) upon the claimant's request if the judge accepts it and no hardship prevents it.

The Obligation to Testify When Summoned: Conditions and Exceptions
States the obligation to testify based on Quranic commands with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of testimony when called, identify the conditions for its obligation, and apply the exceptions to determine when a witness is not sinful.

Core Idea
Testimony is fard upon the witness only if the judge will accept it and no one else has fulfilled it.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on the obligation to testify when summoned by a court. The ruling is derived from Quranic verses that prohibit refusal and concealment. However, the obligation is not absolute — it is conditioned on acceptance by the judge, proximity, and necessity. We will explore these conditions and the exceptions for distance, inability, and delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling from the Quranic verses
The Quran prohibits refusing testimony and concealing it. The prohibition implies a command to testify, making it a fard obligation.
The verses are 2:282-283.
2
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
A prohibition of something with only one opposite is a command to that opposite. Thus, prohibition of iba' (refusal) is a command to testify.
This principle is key to deriving obligation from a prohibition.
3
Determine when the obligation applies
The witness must know the judge will accept his testimony and his testimony must be needed (no others have fulfilled it). Otherwise, no sin for not testifying.
Knowledge of acceptance is a condition for wujub.
4
Consider the distance exception
If the witness lives so far that he cannot go to the judge and return in a day, the obligation drops due to harm (Quran 2:282).
Distance is measured by the ability to return the same day.
5
Analyze the effect of delay without excuse
Delaying testimony after being called, without excuse, creates suspicion of seeking reward, so the testimony is rejected.
This is based on a statement from Shaykh al-Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها تعريفها ونصابها وما يتحمله الشاهد بطلب المدعى بطلب المدعى ) (1) وَلَا يَأْبَ الشُّهَدَاءُ إِذَا مَا دُعُوا ) ، وقوله : ( وَلَا تَكْتُمُوا الشَّهَادَةً وَمَن يَكْتُمْهَا فَإِنَّهُ آثِمٌ قَلْبُهُ ) (2) ، وهذا إن كان نهياً عن الإباء والكتمان، لكن النهي عن الشيء يكون أمراً بضده إذا كان له ضد واحد ؛ لأنَّ الانتهاء لا يكون إلا بالاشتغال به. فكان أداء الشهادة فرضاً قطعاً كفريضة الانتهاء عن الكتمان ، فصار كالأمر به بل أكد ؛ ولهذا أسند الإثم إلى الآلة التي وقع بها الفعل وهو القلب، لِمَا عُرِفَ أَنَّ إسناد الفعل إلى محله يكون أقوى من الإسنادِ إلى كلّه، فقوله : أبصرته بعيني أقوى من قولهم أبصرتُه ، وإسناده إلى أشرف الجوارح دليل على أنه أعظم الجرائم بعد الكفر بالله عَزَّ وَجَلَّ. ثم إنما يأثم إذا علم أن القاضي يقبلُ شهادته وتعين عليه الأداء، وإن علم أن القاضى لا يقبل شهادته، أو كانوا جماعةً فأدَّى غيره من تقبل شهادته فقبلت ، قالوا : لا يأثم، وإن ادَّعى غيره، ولم تقبل شهادته يأثم من لم يؤد إذا كان ممن تقبل شهادته ؛ لأنَّ امتناعه يؤدي إلى تضييع الحقوق. هذا إذا كان موضع الشاهد قريباً من موضع القاضي، وإن كان بعيداً بحيث لا يمكنه أن يَغْدُو إلى القاضي لأداء الشهادة ويرجع إلى أهله في يومه ذلك ، قالوا : لا يأثم ؛ لأنه يلحقه الضرر بذلك ، وقال : وَلَا يُضَارَّ كَاتِبٌ وَلَا شَهِيدٌ (3) ثم إن كان الشاهد شيخاً كبيراً لا يقدر على المشي إلى مجلس الحكم وليس له شيءٌ للركوب فأَرْكَبَهُ المدعي من عنده ، قالوا : لا بأس به، وتقبل شهادته ؛ لأنه من باب الإكرام للشهود ، وقال : أكرموا الشهود ) (4) ، وإن كان يقدر وركبه المدعي من عنده قالوا : لا تقبل . كذا في «التبيين» (5) ، وغيره من المبسوطات. [1] قوله : بطلب المدعي ؛ قال شيخ الإسلام : لو أخَّرَ الشاهد الشهادة بعد الطلب بلا عذر ظاهر ثم أدى لا تقبل شهادته ؛ لأنه لما ترك الأداء مع إمكانه احتمل أنه ترك ؛ لأنه أراد الأجر على الأداء، فتمكن في شهادته نوع تهمة، والتهمة مانعة من القبول. كذا في «كمال الدراية».
The Book of Testimony and Retraction from It: Its Definition, Its Quorum, and What the Witness Bears. Upon the request of the plaintiff. (1) And do not refuse to testify when you are called (2:282), and His saying: And do not conceal the testimony, and whoever conceals it, then indeed his heart is sinful (2:283). And this, even though it is a prohibition of refusal and concealment, but the prohibition of something is a command to its opposite if it has only one opposite, because cessation (from the prohibited) cannot occur except by engaging in its opposite. Thus, performing testimony is absolutely a fard obligation, just as the obligation to cease from concealment, so it becomes like a command to it, rather more emphasized. And for this reason, the sin is attributed to the instrument by which the act occurred, namely the heart, because it is known that attributing the act to its location is stronger than attributing it to the whole. So saying 'I saw it with my eye' is stronger than saying 'I saw it,' and its attribution to the noblest of limbs indicates that it is the greatest sin after disbelief in Allah Almighty. Then, he only sins if he knows that the judge will accept his testimony and it is incumbent upon him to perform; if he knows that the judge will not accept his testimony, or if there is a group and someone else whose testimony is accepted has performed it and it is accepted, they said: he does not sin. And if someone else claimed (i.e., the plaintiff) and his testimony was not accepted, then the one who did not perform sins if he is among those whose testimony is accepted, because his refusal leads to the loss of rights. This applies when the place of the witness is near to the place of the judge. And if it is far such that he cannot go to the judge in the morning to perform testimony and return to his family on that same day, they said: he does not sin, because harm befalls him by that, and He said: And do not harm a scribe or a witness (2:282). Then, if the witness is an old man who cannot walk to the courtroom and has no means of riding, so the plaintiff provides him with a ride from his own, they said: there is no harm and his testimony is accepted, because it is a form of honoring the witnesses, and he said: Honor the witnesses (a hadith). And if he is able (to walk) and the plaintiff provides him a ride from his own, they said: it is not accepted. Thus in al-Tabyin and other comprehensive works. [1] His saying: 'upon the request of the plaintiff'; Shaykh al-Islam said: If the witness delays the testimony after the request without a clear excuse and then performs, his testimony is not accepted, because when he left performing despite ability, it is probable that he left it because he wanted the reward for performing, so a type of suspicion has become established in his testimony, and suspicion prevents acceptance. Thus in Kamal al-Dirayah.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Quran concerning the obligation to testify when summoned. The author begins by citing two Quranic verses: 'Do not refuse to testify when called' and 'Do not conceal testimony.' He then applies the usul principle that a prohibition implies a command to its opposite when there is only one opposite. Thus, refusing and concealing are prohibited, and the opposite is performing testimony, so it becomes a fard obligation. The sin is attributed to the heart to emphasize gravity. However, the obligation is conditional: the witness must know the judge will accept his testimony, and he must be the one needed. If the judge refuses his testimony, or if others have already given sufficient testimony, he does not sin. Distance that prevents returning in a day removes the obligation due to harm. For an elderly witness unable to walk, the plaintiff may provide transport without affecting acceptance, unless he is able to walk. Finally, if a witness delays testimony without excuse, his testimony is rejected due to suspicion of seeking reward.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahādah): Courtroom testimony by a witness
إباء (ibā'): Refusal to testify when called
كتمان (kitmān): Concealment of knowledge of evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a witness incur sin for failing to testify upon being called?
A) If he knows the judge will accept his testimony and he is the only one who can fulfill it.
B) Always, regardless of circumstances.
C) Only if he is far away.
D) Only if he is the plaintiff.

Key Takeaway
Testimony when called is obligatory only if the judge would accept it, it is needed, and the witness is not too distant or excused; delay without excuse vitiates the testimony due to suspicion of worldly motive.

Covering Hudud and Testimony Wording for Theft
Ruling on concealing hudud and proper testimony wording for theft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering hudud and apply the proper wording in theft testimony to avoid necessitating the hadd.

Core Idea
Covering hudud is preferred; in theft, say 'akhadha' not 'saraqa' to protect the victim's compensation right.

This commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explores two interrelated rulings: the first is that it is mustahabb (preferable) to conceal hudud crimes when possible, based on hadith and the Prophetic practice of averting punishments. The second concerns testimony wording in theft cases: a witness should say 'akhadha' (took) rather than 'saraqa' (stole) to avoid triggering the hadd amputation and to preserve the victim's right to monetary compensation. The passage also addresses a potential conflict with the Quranic command 'do not conceal testimony' and provides a Hanafi resolution based on context and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two main legal statements: covering hudud is 'more beloved' (mustahabb) and the witness should say 'akhadha' not 'saraqa'. Note the rationale given for each.
The two rulings are connected by the goal of prioritizing the slave's right over the hadd.
2
Examine the dalil and objection
Read the hadith evidence (cover a Muslim, Allah covers him) and the Prophetic teaching of a way out for confessors. Note the objection from the verse 'do not conceal testimony' and the Hanafi response distinguishing rights of Allah from rights of servants.
The response uses context and consensus (ijma) to restrict the general command.
3
Understand the ruling on testimony without request
The passage states that testimony in rights of Allah (e.g., freeing a slave, divorcing) is obligatory even without a request. Recognize this as an exception to the general preference for covering.
This shows the hierarchy: in haqq Allah, coverage is preferred except when silence would cause loss of the right.
4
Analyze the story of Abu Yusuf
Work through the scenario: admission of 'taking' first establishes guarantee and drops the hadd; subsequent admission of theft cannot bring back the hadd because that would nullify the guarantee. This illustrates the rule that once a right is established, it cannot be overridden by a later contradictory admission.
This is a practical application of istihsan (juristic preference) to reconcile conflicting rights.
5
Synthesize the legal principle
State the overarching principle: in hudud, covering is preferred to protect the right of Allah (mercy) and the right of the servant (compensation). The mufta bihi is to use 'akhadha' and to encourage concealment in hadd cases.
This principle is mukhtalaf fih; the Shafi'i position may differ.

Source Text

[٢]قوله : لئلا يضيع حق المالك ; ورعاية حق الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو الحد ليس بأهم من حكي أنَّ هارون الرشيد ه كان مع جماعة من الفقهاء وفيهم أبو يوسف فادَّعى رجل على آخر بأنه أخذ ماله من بيته، فأقر بالأخذ فسأل الفقهاء، فأفتوا بقطع يده. فقال أبو يوسف : لا ; لأنه لم يقر بالسرقة، وإنّما أقرَّ بالأخذ، فادَّعى المدعي أنه سرق، فأقر لها، فأفتوا بقطع يده، وخالفهم أبو يوسف له فقالوا له، ثمَّ قال : لأنه لما أقرَّ أَوَّلاً بالأخذ ثبت الضمان عليه، وسقط القطع ، فلا يقبلُ إقراره بعده بما يسقط الضمان عنه فعجبوا ذكره الإمامُ الرَّازي في تفسيره المسمّى بـ «مفاتيح الغيب».
And covering them in hudud is more beloved, and he says in theft: 'took', not 'stole'. Covering them in hudud is more beloved: i.e., better. He says in theft: 'took', not 'stole': He only says 'took' so that the right of the owner is not lost. The request without an apparent excuse then he performs, his testimony is not accepted; because when he delayed performance with ability, it is likely that he delayed because he wanted reward for performing, so a kind of suspicion arises in his testimony, and suspicion prevents acceptance. So in 'Kamal al-Dirayah'. And performance is obligatory without request if the testimony is in the rights of Allah Almighty, like freeing a slave woman and divorcing a woman, free or slave. So in 'al-Manh'. [1] His statement: 'more beloved': i.e., better than revealing it; so the witness is given a choice between revealing for what is in it of removing corruption or killing, and between concealing it, and it is better because of what Bukhari and Muslim narrated from the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said: 'Whoever covers a Muslim, Allah will cover him in this world and the Hereafter, and Allah is in the aid of the servant as long as the servant is in the aid of his brother,' and because the Prophet prompted the confessor of zina and the confessor of theft to avert the hadd. If it is said: this contradicts His statement: 'Do not conceal testimony,' and restricting an unrestricted [text] from the Book is not permissible by a solitary report. The answer: the verse is interpreted as referring to testimony in the rights of servants, by the context of the verse, which is the verse of debt, and by consensus, and by His statement: 'Indeed, those who like that immorality should be spread...' It is specific to hudud because they are the right of Allah, and He is free of need, generous, kind to His servants, unlike others, for they are the right of the servant, and he is needful and stingy. So in 'Kamal al-Dirayah' and others. [2] His statement: 'so that the right of the owner is not lost' and observing the right of Allah and that is the hadd is not more important than... It is narrated that Harun al-Rashid was with a group of jurists, among them Abu Yusuf. A man claimed against another that he took his money from his house. He admitted the taking, so they asked the jurists, and they gave a fatwa to cut off his hand. Abu Yusuf said: No, because he did not admit to theft; he only admitted to taking. The claimant then claimed theft, and he admitted to it, so they gave a fatwa to cut off his hand, and Abu Yusuf differed with them. They said to him, then he said: Because when he first admitted to taking, the guarantee (damān) was established, and the cutting was dropped, so his subsequent admission that would drop the guarantee is not accepted. They were amazed. Al-Razi mentioned this in his Tafsir called 'Mafatih al-Ghayb'.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the statement of the matn that covering sins in hudud cases is more beloved (mustahabb), and that a witness in a theft case should say 'akhadha' (he took) rather than 'saraqa' (he stole). The commentator explains the rationale: saying 'saraqa' would necessitate the hadd (amputation), which would conflict with the victim's right to compensation (damān). Hadith evidence is provided: the Prophet said covering a Muslim brings divine covering, and he himself taught a way out for confessors to avoid hadd. An objection is raised that covering testimony contradicts the Quranic command 'do not conceal testimony.' The response distinguishes between rights of Allah (hudud) and rights of servants (property). For rights of Allah, covering is preferred; for rights of servants, testimony is obligatory if requested. The passage also includes a ruling: testimony in rights of Allah is obligatory even without a request, illustrated by freeing a slave or divorcing a spouse. Finally, a story involving Harun al-Rashid and Abu Yusuf illustrates the ruling: an admission of 'taking' (akhadha) establishes guarantee (damān) and drops the hadd, so a subsequent admission of theft is ineffective. This shows Hanafi juristic reasoning (istihsan) that prioritizes reconciling conflicting rights.

Key Terms
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed punishments for crimes against Allah, such as theft, zina, and drinking alcohol.
الشهادة (al-shahadah): Testimony given in court; the act of bearing witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because 'saraqa' is a harsh word that may offend the defendant.
B) To avoid necessitating the hadd amputation and protect the victim's compensation right.
C) Because the Quran commands using euphemisms for crimes.
D) Because the witness may not be certain of the theft.

Key Takeaway
Covering hudud is mustahabb and testimony in theft should be worded to preserve the victim's right to compensation, balancing the right of Allah and the right of the servant.

Four Male Witnesses Required for Zina Testimony
Proof for the nisab of four male witnesses for zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic evidence and the rationale for requiring four male witnesses for zina testimony in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Zina testimony requires four male witnesses — the Quran explicitly commands it and consensus affirms.

This lesson examines the nisab (required number) of witnesses for zina. The Hanafi school, based on clear Quranic texts and consensus, mandates four male witnesses. We will explore the proofs and the legal rationale that makes the hadd difficult to apply, promoting concealment of sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states that the nisab for zina is four men. This is the required number of witnesses for the hadd punishment to be executed.
The nisab is a condition for the hadd, not for the act of testifying itself.
2
Examine the Quranic proofs
The commentary cites three verses: Surah an-Nisa (4:15) commands four witnesses for lewdness; Surah an-Nur (24:4) requires four witnesses for accusing chaste women; and the hadith of Hilal ibn Umayya where the Prophet demanded four witnesses.
The verses use masculine pronouns, indicating male witnesses.
3
Understand the linguistic indication
The Arabic terms 'arba'atan minkum' and 'arba'ati shuhadaa' use masculine forms, which Hanafi usul interprets as exclusive to males unless a qarina indicates otherwise.
This is a dalalah qat'iyyah (definitive indication) for the Hanafis.
4
Note consensus and rationale
The commentator states that ijma has been reached on requiring male witnesses. The rationale is that Allah loves concealment and makes the hadd rarely applicable, thus protecting people's honor.
The difficulty of proving zina serves as a deterrent against false accusations.
5
Relate to consequences
If four male witnesses are not produced, the accuser faces hadd al-qadhf (if accuser is non-spouse) or li'an (if spouse). This reinforces the strictness of the requirement.
Li'an is a special procedure that substitutes for the hadd of qadhf when the accuser is the spouse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) قوله : أربعة رجال ; لقوله : وَالَّتِي يَأْتِينَ الْفَاحِشَةَ مِن نِسَا بِكُمْ فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةً مِّنكُمْ ) ، وقوله : وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بأربعة مهداة ، ولقوله : «ائت بأربعة يشهدون على صدق مقالتك». وهذه الألفاظ موضوعة للمذكر دون المؤنَّث، وقد انعقد الإجماع على اشتراط الذكور فيه ; لأنَّ الله تعالى يحب الستر على عباده، وأوعد بالعذاب من أحب إشاعة الفاحشة على المؤمنين، كما تلونا عليك، وفي اشتراط الأربعة على هذه الفاحشة قلَّمَا يتحقق، ووجب على ما نُسب إلى هذه الفاحشة الحدَّ إن كان أجنبياً، واللعان إن كان
[2] His statement: 'four men' — due to His statement: 'And those who commit lewdness among your women, bring against them four witnesses from among you,' and His statement: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses,' and his statement: 'Bring four witnesses who testify to the truth of your claim.' These expressions are for males, not females, and consensus has been established on the requirement of males, because Allah loves concealment for His servants, and threatens with punishment those who love that immorality should spread among the believers, as we recited to you. And in requiring four for this lewdness, it is rarely proven, and what is attributed to this lewdness requires the hadd if it was between strangers, and the li'an if it was...
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's statement that the required number of witnesses for zina is four men. The commentator provides three Qur'anic proofs: Surah an-Nisa (4:15) commands four witnesses for lewdness; Surah an-Nur (24:4) requires four witnesses for accusing chaste women; and the Prophet told Hilal ibn Umayya to bring four witnesses. The words are in masculine form, and consensus (ijma) has been reached that only male witnesses are accepted for zina. The rationale is that Allah loves concealment and making the hadd difficult to apply. If witnesses are insufficient, the accuser receives hadd (if falsely accusing a muhsan) or li'an (if the accuser is the spouse).

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The required number of witnesses for a particular crime or transaction.
اللعان (al-li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when a husband accuses his wife of zina without witnesses, and she denies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the Quranic verses use masculine pronouns and it makes the hadd difficult to apply
C) Because it is easier to find male witnesses
D) Because the Prophet said women cannot testify in hudud

Key Takeaway
The nisab for zina is four male witnesses, established by Quranic text and ijma, making the hadd rarely applied to protect honor.
