Wording of Testimony in Theft Cases
Ruling on witness wording in theft cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the wording of testimony in theft cases and apply the principle that amputation and damages cannot coexist.

Core Idea
A witness should avoid saying 'saraqa' to preserve the victim's right to compensation, because hadd and damages are incompatible.

How should a witness describe a theft in court? The answer matters more than you think. In Hanafi fiqh, the precise wording a witness uses can determine whether the punishment of amputation becomes obligatory, and whether the victim can recover financial compensation. This lesson unpacks a ruling that may seem counterintuitive: the witness should say 'he took' rather than 'he stole', because the two consequences—hadd and damages—cannot be combined. We will explore the proof, the principle, and a classical story that brings the rule to life.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Identify what the text says about the witness's wording in a theft case.
The witness should avoid saying 'saraqa' (he stole) and instead say 'akhadha' (he took).
2
Identify the Proof
Find the legal reason given: 'because if theft became apparent, amputation would be required, and damages do not coexist with amputation.'
The proof is the established principle that hadd (amputation) and daman (financial liability) cannot be combined.
3
Apply the Principle to the Story
Analyze the story of Harun al-Rashid and Abu Yusuf. Note how the defendant's admission of 'taking' established damages, which precluded amputation.
Abu Yusuf argued that once damages are fixed, a later admission of theft (which would trigger hadd) is not accepted because it would negate the liability.
4
Derive the Legal Maxim
Formulate the underlying maxim from this ruling: al-daman wa al-hadd la yajtami'an (damages and hadd punishment do not coexist).
This maxim governs similar cases where a financial right and a corporal punishment conflict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقولُ : سَرَق ; لئلا يُحِبُّ الحَد . [ 1 ] قوله : لئلا يجب الحد ; ولأنه لو ظهرت السرقة لوجب القطع، والضمان لا يجامع القطع، فلا يحصلُ إحياء حق العبد ، حكي أنَّ هارون الرشيد ه كان مع جماعة من الفقهاء وفيهم أبو يوسف فادَّعى رجل على آخر بأنه أخذ ماله من بيته، فأقر بالأخذ فسأل الفقهاء، فأفتوا بقطع يده. فقال أبو يوسف : لا ; لأنه لم يقر بالسرقة، وإنّما أقرَّ بالأخذ، فادَّعى المدعي أنه سرق، فأقر لها، فأفتوا بقطع يده، وخالفهم أبو يوسف له فقالوا له، ثمَّ قال : لأنه لما أقرَّ أَوَّلاً بالأخذ ثبت الضمان عليه، وسقط القطع ، فلا يقبلُ إقراره بعده بما يسقط الضمان عنه فعجبوا ذكره الإمامُ الرَّازي في تفسيره المسمّى بـ «مفاتيح الغيب».
And he should not say: he stole, so that the prescribed punishment is not required. [1] His saying: so that the hadd is not wajib; and because if theft became apparent, amputation would be required, and damages do not coexist with amputation, so the revival of the slave's right is not achieved. It is narrated that Harun al-Rashid was with a group of jurists including Abu Yusuf, and a man sued another alleging that he took his property from his house. He (the defendant) admitted the taking. The jurists were asked, and they gave a fatwa to cut off his hand. Abu Yusuf said: No, because he did not admit to theft, he only admitted to taking. The plaintiff claimed he stole, so he admitted? Then the jurists gave a fatwa to cut off his hand, and Abu Yusuf disagreed with them. Then he said: because when he first admitted to taking, the liability (damages) was established, and the amputation fell, so his subsequent admission that would negate the damages is not accepted. They were astonished. Imam al-Razi mentioned this in his tafsir named Mafatih al-Ghayb.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling about the wording a witness should use in theft cases. The ruling: The witness should not say "he stole" (saraqa) because that would make the hadd of amputation obligatory; instead, he should say "he took" (akhadha). The reasoning is that amputation and damages are incompatible: if amputation is carried out, the victim loses the right to financial compensation. The story of Harun al-Rashid and Abu Yusuf illustrates this principle: a man admitted to taking property but not to stealing. The other jurists initially ruled for amputation, but Abu Yusuf argued that the admission of taking established damages, which precluded amputation. Once damages are fixed, a later admission cannot overturn them. The proof is based on the legal principle that damages and hadd cannot coexist (al-daman wa al-hadd la yajtami'an). This ruling is unique to Hanafi fiqh in its explicit guidance on witness wording.

Key Terms
سَرَق (saraqa): The act of theft that triggers the hadd of amputation.
ضمان (daman): Financial liability for the property taken.
قطع (qat'): Amputation of the hand as the prescribed punishment for theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because 'saraqa' is a harsh word.
B) Because saying 'he took' is more accurate.
C) To avoid making the hadd of amputation obligatory.
D) Because the judge does not like the word.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school instructs witnesses to say 'he took' instead of 'he stole' to protect the victim's right to damages, because amputation and financial liability are mutually exclusive.

Witness Requirement for Zina: Four Men
Establishes the number and gender of witnesses for zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witness requirements for zina, identify the primary Quranic and hadith proofs, and explain why women's testimony is rejected using the concept of shubhat al-badaliyyah.

Core Idea
Four male witnesses are required for zina; women's testimony is rejected to preserve concealment and due to the principle of shubhat al-badaliyyah.

This lesson examines the strict witness requirement for establishing the hadd of zina. Unlike other areas of fiqh where two male witnesses suffice, zina requires four men. The Hanafi school defends this position using Quranic texts, the sunnah, and the unique usul concept of shubhat al-badaliyyah. We will explore the evidence and the rationale behind the exclusion of women's testimony in hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled? Zina (unlawful intercourse). What is the ruling? The hadd requires four male witnesses.
The nisab (required number) for zina is four men.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verses Surah An-Nisa 4:15 and Surah An-Nur 24:4, and a hadith. Note the imperative form 'fastashhidu' indicating obligation, and 'arba'atan minkum' specifying four, with 'minkum' implying males due to the masculine plural.
The text also cites consensus for the condition of males.
3
Understand the rationale of satr
Allah loves concealment; requiring four men makes conviction rare, preserving secrecy. If the accused is a stranger, hadd applies; if a spouse, li'an applies.
This emphasizes the reluctance to publicize sins.
4
Analyze the minority opinion and Hanafi rebuttal
'Ata' and Hammad allowed three men and two women. The Hanafi rebuttal: hadith of al-Zuhri that the sunnah does not accept women's testimony in hudud; and the concept of shubhat al-badaliyyah: women's testimony is a semblance of substitution, and since even real substitution (like testimony on testimony) is rejected, the semblance is also rejected.
The concept of shubhat al-badaliyyah is unique to Hanafi usul.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi position
Combine the evidence: Quranic imperative, sunnah, consensus, and usul reasoning. The ruling is that only four male witnesses are accepted; women's testimony is not considered in hudud.
This is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونصابها : للزنا : أربعة رجال) رعاية حق العبد. [ 1 ] قوله : لئلا يجب الحد ; ولأنه لو ظهرت السرقة لوجب القطع، والضمان لا يجامع القطع، فلا يحصلُ إحياء حق العبد ، حكي أنَّ هارون الرشيد ه كان مع جماعة من الفقهاء وفيهم أبو يوسف فادَّعى رجل على آخر بأنه أخذ ماله من بيته، فأقر بالأخذ فسأل الفقهاء، فأفتوا بقطع يده. فقال أبو يوسف : لا ; لأنه لم يقر بالسرقة، وإنّما أقرَّ بالأخذ، فادَّعى المدعي أنه سرق، فأقر لها، فأفتوا بقطع يده، وخالفهم أبو يوسف له فقالوا له، ثمَّ قال : لأنه لما أقرَّ أَوَّلاً بالأخذ ثبت الضمان عليه، وسقط القطع ، فلا يقبلُ إقراره بعده بما يسقط الضمان عنه فعجبوا ذكره الإمامُ الرَّازي في تفسيره المسمّى بـ «مفاتيح الغيب». (۲) قوله : أربعة رجال ; لقوله : وَالَّتِي يَأْتِينَ الْفَاحِشَةَ مِن نِسَا بِكُمْ فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةً مِّنكُمْ ) (١) ، وقوله : وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بأربعة مهداة (۲) ، ولقوله : «ائت بأربعة يشهدون على صدق مقالتك»(۳). وهذه الألفاظ موضوعة للمذكر دون المؤنَّث، وقد انعقد الإجماع على اشتراط الذكور فيه ; لأنَّ الله تعالى يحب الستر على عباده، وأوعد بالعذاب من أحب إشاعة الفاحشة على المؤمنين، كما تلونا عليك، وفي اشتراط الأربعة على هذه الفاحشة قلَّمَا يتحقق، ووجب على ما نُسب إلى هذه الفاحشة الحدَّ إن كان أجنبياً، واللعان إن كان زوجاً، وكل ذلك يؤكد معنى الستر، ويمنع من الإظهار. كذا في «التبيين»)، وغيره. وعن عطاء وحماد الله : ولو شهد ثلاثة رجال وامرأتان في الزنا قبلوا ; لإطلاق قوله الالة : أَرْبَعَةً مِّنكُمْ ) (۲) ، والتاء لا تدخل في العدد، إلا إذا كان معدوده مذكراً. ولنا : ما روى ابن أبي شيبة في «مصنِّفه» : عن حفص بن حجاج عن الزُّهْرِيُّ أَنه قال : مضت السنة من رسول الله الله والخليفتين من بعده أن لا تجوز شهادة النساء في الحدود» (۳). ولأن في شهادة النساء شبهة البدلية ، قال الله : فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُونَا رَجُلَيْنِ فَرَجُلٌ وامراتان ) (4) ، وليست ببدل حقيقة; لأنَّ البدل الحقيقي لا يصار إليه مع القدرة على الأصل. ولا شك في جواز المصير إلى استشهاد المرأتين والرجل، مع القدرة على استشهاد الرجلين، وحقيقة البدليّة غير محتملة في الحدود، حتى لا تقبل الشهادة على الشهادة فيها ، فكذلك شبهة البدلية اعتبار الشبهة بالحقيقة ; لأنَّ الشبهة فيما تسقط بالشبهات كالحقيقة. كذا في «كمال الدراية»، وغيره.
[The number of witnesses required] For zina: four men. (2) His saying: four men; because of His sayings: 'And those who commit unlawful intercourse from among your women, then seek four witnesses from among you' (4:15), and 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses' (24:4), and 'Bring four witnesses to attest to the truth of your statement' (as reported). These expressions are set for males, not females, and consensus has been made on the condition of males therein. Because Allah loves concealment for His servants, and warned with punishment those who love the spread of immorality among the believers. In requiring four witnesses for this immorality, it is rarely realized, and the hadd is obligated for one who is a stranger, and the li'an for a spouse. All this emphasizes the meaning of concealment and prevents disclosure. Thus in al-Tibyan and others. And it is narrated from 'Ata' and Hammad: If three men and two women testify for zina, it is accepted because of the generality of the verse 'four from among you' (4:15), and the ta' (feminine suffix) does not enter into the number except when its counted is masculine. And for us: What Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated in his Musannaf from Hafs ibn Hajjaj from al-Zuhri that he said: 'The sunnah of the Messenger of Allah and the two caliphs after him has passed that the testimony of women is not permitted in hudud.' And because in the testimony of women there is the semblance of substitution (shubhat al-badaliyyah). Allah said: 'If there are not two men, then one man and two women' (2:282), and it is not a real substitution; because a real substitution is not resorted to when the original is possible. And there is no doubt about the permissibility of resorting to the testimony of two women and one man when it is possible to have two men. And the reality of substitution is not plausible in hudud, so much so that testimony upon testimony is not accepted in them. Thus the semblance of substitution is considered the same as the reality, because what is dropped by doubts is like the reality. Thus in Kamal al-Dirayah and others.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage establishes the witness requirement for zina (unlawful intercourse). The ruling: four male witnesses are required. The evidence is drawn from three Quranic verses (4:15, 24:4, and a hadith) and the consensus of the ummah. The Hanafi school holds that these witnesses must be men; women's testimony is not accepted in hudud. The minority opinion of 'Ata' and Hammad, who accepted three men and two women, is refuted on two grounds: first, the hadith of al-Zuhri that the sunnah is to not accept women's testimony in hudud; second, the concept of 'shubhat al-badaliyyah' (semblance of substitution). In financial transactions, women may substitute for a man only when two males are unavailable. However, in hudud, since even real substitution (like testimony on testimony) is not accepted, the semblance is also unacceptable. The requirement of four males is deliberate: it makes conviction rare, preserving the principle of concealment (satr). If the accused is a stranger to the woman, he faces the hadd; if he is her husband, li'an (mutual cursing) applies. The entire system emphasizes Islamic reluctance to publicize sins.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The required number of witnesses for a specific case.
زنا (zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married to each other.
شبهة البدلية (shubhat al-badaliyyah): The semblance of substitution: women's testimony is considered a substitute for men, but since real substitution is not allowed in hudud, the semblance is also rejected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence used by the Hanafi school to reject women's testimony in hudud cases?
A) Quran 4:15
B) The hadith of al-Zuhri that the sunnah is to not accept women's testimony in hudud
C) The concept of qiyas
D) Consensus of the four caliphs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires four male witnesses for zina, rejecting women's testimony based on explicit Quran and Sunnah, as well as the usul concept that hudud are not subject to substitutional testimony.

The Two-Male-Witness Requirement for Hudud and Qisas
States witness requirement for qisas and hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi witness requirement for qisas and hudud (excluding zina) and cite the primary Quranic evidence and its extension by qiyas.

Core Idea
Two male witnesses are required for qisas and hudud; women's testimony is excluded by Quranic command and qiyas.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya focuses on the strict evidentiary standard for hudud and qisas: two male witnesses. The text cites the well-known debt verse (2:282) and extends its requirement to criminal cases through qiyas. We will unpack the dalil, the objection, and the Hanafi response to understand the school's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states 'For qisas and the remaining hudud: two men.' Determine which crimes are included and excluded.
Excluded: zina (requires four male witnesses or specific evidence).
2
Locate the primary proof
Find the Quranic verse cited (2:282) and note the exact wording that serves as evidence.
The imperative 'fastashhidu' indicates obligation.
3
Understand the extension by qiyas
The verse was revealed for financial transactions. Explain how the Hanafi school applies it to hudud and qisas through common 'illa (effective cause).
The 'illa is the need for reliable testimony to prevent wrongful punishment.
4
Address the objection
The text raises an objection: the verse is about debts, so how can it apply to hudud? The Hanafi response uses qiyas, which will be detailed in subsequent pages.
This objection may arise from other schools or from a superficial reading.
5
Note the exclusion of women's testimony
The passage explicitly rejects women's testimony for hudud and qisas, citing the principle of 'shubhat al-badaliyyah' (semblance of substitution).
Women's testimony is accepted in other areas (e.g., financial transactions) but not here due to the seriousness of the punishment.

[١] قوله : وللقـود ; أي القصاص في النفس والطرف وباقي الحدود غير الزنا من حد السرقة وقطع الطريق والقذف والشرب وغيرها رجلان ; فلا يقبلُ فيها شهادةً النساء ; لقوله : وَاسْتَشْهِدُوا شَهِيدَيْنِ مِن رِجَالِكُمْ )) ، ولما روينا من حديث الزُّهْرِيّ ; ولأنَّ في شهادةِ النساء شبهة البدلية كما ذكرنا. (0) فإن قلت : الآية المذكورة قد وردت في المداينات، فكيف تكون حجةٌ في الحدود والقصاص. (۱) تبيين الحقائق (٤ : ٢٠٨). (۲) النساء : ١٥ . (۳) مصنف ابن أبي شيبة»(٥ : ٥٣٣). (٤) البقرة : من الآية ٢٨٢. (٥) البقرة : ٢٨٢.
For qisas and the remaining hudud: two men. [1] His saying: 'For qisas' i.e., retaliation for life and limb, and the remaining hudud other than zina, such as the hadd of theft, highway robbery, slander, drinking, etc. So the testimony of women is not accepted therein, because of His saying: 'And bring two witnesses from among your men' (2:282), and because of what we narrated from the hadith of al-Zuhri, and because in the testimony of women there is the semblance of substitution as we mentioned. (0) If you say: The mentioned verse was revealed for debts, so how can it be a proof for hudud and qisas? (1) Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (4:208). (2) An-Nisa' 4:15. (3) Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah (5:533). (4) Al-Baqarah 2:282. (5) Al-Baqarah 2:282.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage establishes the witness requirement for qisas (retaliation) and other hudud (prescribed punishments) excluding zina. The ruling: two male witnesses are required. This includes hadd for theft, highway robbery, slander, drinking alcohol, etc. The evidence is from Quran 2:282, which commands to bring two male witnesses, and from the hadith of al-Zuhri mentioned previously. The text then raises an objection: verse 2:282 was revealed in the context of debts, so how can it apply to hudud? The answer is not provided in this excerpt, but the Hanafi position is that the 'illa (effective cause) of the verse is the need for reliable testimony, which applies equally to hudud. The principle of shubhat al-badaliyyah is also invoked: since women's testimony is a substitute for men only when necessary, and since hudud are so serious that even real substitution (testimony on testimony) is not accepted, the semblance of substitution is also rejected. This ruling reinforces the strict evidentiary standards in Islamic criminal law.

Key Terms
قود (qawad): Synonym for qisas, retaliation.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah, e.g., for theft, slander, drinking.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation for murder or injury; the punishment matches the crime.
شبهة البدلية (shubhat al-badaliyyah): The semblance of substitution; the idea that women's testimony is considered a substitute for men's in certain contexts, which makes it less reliable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires two male witnesses for hudud and qisas based on the Quranic imperative and extended by qiyas; women's testimony is excluded due to the seriousness of the punishment.

Shahadat — Testimony

Women's Testimony in Qisas and Hudud
States the ruling that women's testimony is not accepted in qisas and hudud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's testimony in qisas and hudud, explain the three proofs (Quran, sunnah, shubha al-badaliyya), and apply the principle that the generality of the word (ʿumūm al-lafẓ) is considered over the specificity of the occasion.

Core Idea
Women's testimony is invalid in qisas and hudud because of the general Quranic command, established sunnah, and the semblance of substitution that creates doubt.

This lesson addresses a crucial rule in Hanafi criminal procedure: the exclusion of women's testimony in qisas (retaliation) and most hudud offenses. The text combines textual proof from the Quran and hadith with a rational underpinning known as shubha al-badaliyya (semblance of substitution). By the end of this lesson, you will understand not only the ruling but also the legal reasoning that supports it, and you will be able to respond to common objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
First, identify what act is being ruled upon (testimony in qisas and hudud other than zina) and what the ruling is (invalid; only two male witnesses suffice). Note that the ruling explicitly excludes zina, which requires four male witnesses.
The term 'ḥudūd' here excludes the hadd of zina; the text later explains that no other right is established by more than two witnesses.
2
Locate the Quranic Proof
The primary Quranic proof is al-Baqara 2:282, which commands 'two men' as witnesses for all rights. Although this verse was revealed concerning debts, the Hanafi principle of ʿumūm al-lafẓ (generality of the word) extends it to all rights, including hudud.
The text addresses the objection that the verse is about debts and responds that consideration is for the general wording, not the specific occasion.
3
Examine the Sunnah Proof
The author cites the hadith of al-Zuhri, transmitted by Ibn Abi Shayba, that the established practice (sunnah) of the Prophet and the two caliphs was to reject women's testimony in hudud. This serves as a secondary textual proof.
This hadith is from the Muṣannaf of Ibn Abī Shayba, a key collection for Hanafi arguments.
4
Understand the Rational Proof (Shubha al-Badaliyya)
The third proof is rational: women's testimony in financial matters is a substitute (badal) for men's testimony, as per the verse. A true substitute is not used when the original is available. Since hudud are averted by doubts (shubuhāt), the semblance of substitution casts doubt, so women's testimony is excluded.
The text argues that if the substitute (women) were accepted, it would create distrust in the original (men) in hudud, which are too severe for such uncertainty.
5
Respond to the Opposing View
The text mentions that Ata and Hammad accepted testimony of three men and two women for zina based on the general wording of the verse. The Hanafi response is that the verse for zina specifies 'four men' and the feminine tā does not enter the number, but the established practice (sunnah) overrides this. Additionally, the shubha al-badaliyya reasoning excludes substitution in hudud.
This shows the Hanafi method of weighing proofs: sunnah and analogy can specify the general Quranic command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللقود وباقي الحدود: رجلان. زوجاً، وكل ذلك يؤكد معنى الستر، ويمنع من الإظهار. كذا في «التبيين»)، وغيره. وعن عطاء وحماد الله : ولو شهد ثلاثة رجال وامرأتان في الزنا قبلوا ؛ لإطلاق قوله الله : أَرْبَعَةً مِّنكُمْ (النساء: 15) ، والتاء لا تدخل في العدد، إلا إذا كان معدوده مذكراً. ولنا : ما روى ابن أبي شيبة في «مصنِّفه» : عن حفص بن حجاج عن الزُّهْرِيُّ أَنه قال : مضت السنة من رسول الله الله والخليفتين من بعده أن لا تجوز شهادة النساء في الحدود» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة). ولأن في شهادة النساء شبهة البدلية ، قال الله : فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُونَا رَجُلَيْنِ فَرَجُلٌ وامراتان (البقرة: 282) ، وليست ببدل حقيقة؛ لأنَّ البدل الحقيقي لا يصار إليه مع القدرة على الأصل. ولا شك في جواز المصير إلى استشهاد المرأتين والرجل، مع القدرة على استشهاد الرجلين، وحقيقة البدليّة غير محتملة في الحدود، حتى لا تقبل الشهادة على الشهادة فيها ، فكذلك شبهة البدلية اعتبار الشبهة بالحقيقة ؛ لأنَّ الشبهة فيما تسقط بالشبهات كالحقيقة. كذا في «كمال الدراية»، وغيره.
[١]قوله : وللقـود ؛ أي القصاص في النفس والطرف وباقي الحدود غير الزنا من حد السرقة وقطع الطريق والقذف والشرب وغيرها رجلان ؛ فلا يقبلُ فيها شهادةً النساء ؛ لقوله : وَاسْتَشْهِدُوا شَهِيدَيْنِ مِن رِجَالِكُمْ (البقرة: 282) ، ولما روينا من حديث الزُّهْرِيّ ؛ ولأنَّ في شهادةِ النساء شبهة البدلية كما ذكرنا.
فإن قلت : الآية المذكورة قد وردت في المداينات، فكيف تكون حجةٌ في الحدود والقصاص.
قلنا : العبرة لعموم اللفظ لا لخصوص السبب، كما بُرْهِنَ في غير موضع، ولا حق يثبت شرعاً بالشهود التي فوق الاثنين سوى حد الزنا، فتعين ثبوت سائر الحقوق بالاثنين من الشهود، ومن سائر الحقوق بقيَّةُ الحدود، فتثبت بشهادة رجلين.
وضم صاحب «المنح» إلى بقية الحدودِ إسلام كافر ذكر، وردة مسلم، فإنّهما لا تقبل فيهما إلا شهادة رجلين، فتقبل شهادة رجل وامرأتين بإسلامها، والظاهر أنَّ أصحاب المتون لم يصرحوا بهما ، اكتفاء بذكر القود ؛ لدخولهما تحته، لكنَّ التصريح بهما أولى.
And for retaliation (qisas) and the rest of the hudud: two men. [Zawj and so on all emphasize the meaning of concealment and prevent disclosure. Thus in al-Tabyin and others. And from Ata and Hammad: if three men and two women testify in zina, they are accepted, due to the general import of His saying: 'Four witnesses from among you' (al-Nisa: 15), and the feminine taa does not enter the number unless its counted is masculine. And for us: what Ibn Abi Shayba narrated in his Musannaf: from Hafs ibn Hujayj from al-Zuhri that he said: 'The sunnah from the Messenger of Allah and the two Caliphs after him is that the testimony of women is not permissible in hudud.' And because in the testimony of women there is an aspect of substitution (shubha al-badaliyya). Allah said: 'If they are not two men, then one man and two women' (al-Baqara: 282), and it is not a true substitute because a true substitute is not resorted to when the original is available. And there is no doubt about the permissibility of resorting to calling two women and one man when able to call two men, and the reality of substitution is not admissible in hudud, just as testimony upon testimony is not accepted therein. So likewise the semblance of substitution is considering the semblance as reality because [hudud] are averted by doubts. Thus in Kamal al-Diraya and others.
[1] His saying: 'And for qisas' i.e., retaliation in life and limb and the rest of hudud other than zina—like the hadd of theft, highway robbery, slander, drinking, and others—two men; so the testimony of women is not accepted therein, due to His saying: 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men' (al-Baqara: 282), and because of what we narrated from the hadith of al-Zuhri, and because in women's testimony there is the semblance of substitution as we mentioned.
If you say: The mentioned verse came concerning debts, so how is it a proof in hudud and qisas?
We say: Consideration is for the generality of the word, not the specificity of the occasion, as demonstrated elsewhere. And no right is established legally by witnesses more than two except the hadd of zina. So the establishment of all other rights is determined by two witnesses from among them. And from the other rights are the rest of the hudud, so they are established by the testimony of two men.
And the author of al-Minh joined to the rest of the hudud: the Islam of a male disbeliever and the apostasy of a Muslim, for only the testimony of two men is accepted in them, so the testimony of one man and two women is not accepted for his Islam. And it appears that the authors of the matns did not mention them explicitly, being content with mentioning qisas because they fall under it, but explicit mention is better.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states the general Hanafi rule that in cases of qisas (retaliation for murder or injury) and all hudud punishments other than zina, the testimony of women is not accepted at all; only the testimony of two male witnesses suffices. The proof comes from multiple sources: First, the Quranic verse in Surah al-Baqara (2:282) which, although revealed about debts, is taken in its general meaning to apply to all rights, including hudud. Second, the hadith of al-Zuhri that the established practice of the Prophet and the two caliphs was to reject women's testimony in hudud. Third, the principle of shubha al-badaliyya (semblance of substitution): since women are substitutes for men in testimony (as per the verse), and true substitutes are not used when the original is available, the semblance of substitution creates enough doubt to exclude them in hudud. The text also answers an objection that the verse is about debts by stating that legal consideration is for the general wording, not the specific occasion. Additionally, it clarifies that matters like the Islam of a disbeliever and apostasy are included under 'hudud' for this purpose, even if not explicitly stated in earlier texts.

Key Terms
القود (al-qawad): Retaliation for homicide or bodily injury (qisas) in the law of talion.
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed punishments for crimes like theft, robbery, slander, drinking, and zina. Here it refers to all such punishments except zina.
شبهة البدلية (shubha al-badaliyya): The legal semblance that women's testimony is a substitute for men's, since in financial transactions two women substitute for one man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Women's testimony is categorically invalid in qisas and all hudud except zina, because of the general Quranic command, the sunnah, and the principle that hudud are averted by the slightest doubt.

Women's Testimony in Exclusive Matters: A Hanafi Analysis
Inter-madhhab dispute on number of women witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts one woman's testimony for virginity, childbirth, and female defects, and evaluate the Shafi'i and Ibn Abi Layla positions.

Core Idea
One woman's testimony suffices where men cannot see: necessity drops both masculinity and number.

This passage tackles an important exception in the law of testimony: matters that men cannot normally observe, such as virginity, childbirth, and certain female defects. The Hanafi school argues that a single woman's testimony is sufficient, while other schools require two or four. Let's explore the proofs and reasoning behind this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: one woman's testimony suffices for virginity, childbirth, and defects that men cannot see. Two are recommended for caution.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing views
Note the Shafi'i view (four women) and Ibn Abi Layla's view (two women). Understand their proofs: analogy to the general rule where two women equal one man.
Ata also follows the Shafi'i view; Malik and al-Thawri reportedly require two.
3
Analyse the Hanafi dalil
Examine the hadith of al-Zuhri and Hudhayfa. Understand how the definite plural (al-nisa') indicates the minimum (one).
The linguistic argument: 'al-nisa' without a known referent covers the genus, hence one.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response to opponents
The dropping of masculinity is due to necessity (men cannot access this knowledge). By the same reasoning, the number is dropped because one woman's testimony is easier to obtain than two.
This is an argument from the same cause (illa): difficulty of looking.
5
Determine the practical consequence
State the thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi practice, one woman's testimony is enough; in Shafi'i, four; in Ibn Abi Layla's view, two.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللبكارة، والولادة، وعيوب النساء فيما لا يطلع عليه الرجال
[۱] قوله : وللبكارة...الخ ؛ لما روى عبد الرزاق في مصنفه»: عن ابن شهاب الزُّهْرِي قال : مضت السنة أن تجوز شهادة النساء فيما لا يطلع عليه غيرهن من ولادات النساء وعيوبهن) ، ووجه الاستدلال بهذا الحديث : إِنَّ الجمع المحلى بالألف واللام إذا لم يكن ثمة معهود ، ويراد به الجنس، فيتناول الأقل.
وقال حذيفة ه: «أجاز رسول الله الله شهادة القابلة على الولادة»(۳)، وقال الشَّافِعِيُّ : يشترط الأربع وهو قول عطاء الله ؛ لأنَّ كل امرأتين مقام رجل واحدٍ في الشهادة، وقال ابن أبي ليلى الله : يشترط اثنتان ؛ لما أنه لما سقط اعتبار الذكورة بقي العدد معتبراً، ونسبه الشُّمُنِّي إلى مالك والثووي .
والحجة [على] الشافعي له وابن أبي ليلى له ما روينا من حديث ابن شهاب الزهري له ؛ ولأنه إنَّما سقطت الذكورة اليف النظرا ؛ لأنَّ نظر الجنس أخف، فكذا يسقط العدد ؛ لأنَّ نظر الواحدة أخف من نظر الإثنتين إلا أن الإثنتين أحوط ، لما فيه من معنى الإلزام.
And for virginity, childbirth, and defects of women in what men do not have knowledge of.
[1] His saying: 'And for virginity...etc.' because Abd al-Razzaq narrated in his Musannaf from Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri who said: 'The sunnah passed that the testimony of women is permitted in matters that no one else but they see, such as the childbirths of women and their defects.' And the point of inference from this hadith is that the definite plural when there is no specified referent and is intended for the genus includes the minimum.
And Hudhayfa said: 'The Messenger of Allah permitted the testimony of the midwife concerning childbirth.' And al-Shafi'i said: 'Four [women] are required,' and that is the saying of Ata, because every two women stand in the place of one man in testimony. And Ibn Abi Layla said: 'Two [women] are required,' because when the consideration of masculinity is dropped, the number remains considered. And al-Shumunni attributed [this view] to Malik and al-Thawri.
And the proof against al-Shafi'i and Ibn Abi Layli is what we narrated from the hadith of Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri. And because masculinity is dropped due to the difficulty of looking because looking at the [opposite] sex is more severe, so likewise the number is dropped because the look of one woman is less severe than the look of two. However, two are more cautious because there is an element of enforcement.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of women witnesses required in matters that men cannot normally see, such as virginity, childbirth, and female defects. The Hanafi position, based on the hadith of al-Zuhri and the hadith of Hudhayfa about the midwife, is that one woman's testimony is sufficient. The hadith's wording 'women' in the indefinite plural indicates the minimum of one. Imam al-Shafi'i and Ata require four women, analogizing that every two women equal one man, so four women equal two men. Ibn Abi Layla requires two women, arguing that since the requirement of masculinity is dropped, the original number (two) remains. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the dropping of masculinity is due to necessity (men cannot access this knowledge), and by the same reasoning the number is also dropped because the lesser difficulty of one woman's testimony compared to two. However, two women are recommended for caution. The Hanafi position is that one woman's testimony is sufficient, though two are more cautious (ahwat).

Key Terms
البكارة (al-bakara): Virginity; a female's condition of being a virgin. Testimony regarding loss of virginity due to defloration or other causes.
الولادة (al-wilada): Childbirth; the act of giving birth. Testimony about the birth of a child, e.g., for establishing lineage.
عيوب النساء (uyub al-nisa'): Physical defects specific to women, such as vaginal abnormalities, that are not normally seen by men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many women witnesses are required to establish a claim of virginity loss or childbirth?
A) Four women
B) Two women
C) One woman
D) No women are allowed

Key Takeaway
One woman's testimony suffices for matters men cannot see, because necessity drops both the requirement of masculinity and the number.

Witnesses for Non-Financial Matters: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
States the required number of witnesses for non-financial matters like marriage and divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for witnesses in non-financial matters and explain the ikhtilaf with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
For non-financial matters like marriage, Hanafi law accepts one man and two women as witnesses.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the required number of witnesses for matters that are not purely financial, such as marriage, divorce, and agency. The text explicitly states that either two men or one man and two women suffice. However, this ruling is contested by Imam al-Shafi'i, who restricts the one-man-two-women combination to financial matters only. We will unpack the dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Read the passage carefully: for non-financial matters (ghayr māl) like marriage, fosterage, divorce, agency, and will, the required witnesses are either two men or one man and two women.
Note that the text also mentions an exception: if defects of women are visible to men (e.g., an extra finger), a single woman's testimony is insufficient.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
The commentator explicitly mentions that there is a dispute with al-Shafi'i. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one man and two women are only accepted in financial matters, not in non-financial matters.
The text does not provide al-Shafi'i's dalil, but the disagreement is noted.
3
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, a marriage contract witnessed by one man and two women is valid; under Shafi'i law, it would be invalid unless two men are present.
This affects not only marriage but also divorce, agency, etc.
4
Identify the mufta bihi and nuance
The text upholds the Hanafi position as the relied-upon view. Additionally, the footnote adds an intra-Hanafi nuance: the wording of shahada (testimony) is required by Khurasani scholars but not by Iraqi scholars.
This shows that even within the Hanafi school, there can be differences on procedural details.

Source Text

امرأة ، ولغيرها : مالاً أو غير مال : كنكاح ، ورضاع، وطلاق، ووكالة، ووصية، رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان
امرأة ، إنما قال هذا؛ لأنَّ عيوب النساء إذا كانت مما يطلع عليه الرجال : كالإصبع الزائدة مثلاً لا يكفي شهادة امرأة.
(ولغيرها : مالاً أو غير مال : كنكاح ، ورضاع، وطلاق، ووكالة، ووصية، رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان) : إنما قال : مالاً أو غير مال ؛ لأنَّ فيه خلاف الشَّافِعِي ، فإنَّ غير المال لا يُقْبَلُ فيه شهادة رجل وامرأتين عنده، بل هذا مخصوص بالمَال.
[1] قوله : امرأة ؛ واحدة بشرط الحريَّةِ والعقل والإسلام والبلوغ، والأحوط امرأتان، والأحب ثلاث، والمخرج عن الخلاف الطبع، ولفظ الشهادة يشترط عند مشایخ خراسان، لا عند مشايخ العراق.
A woman, and for other than it [financial matters]: property or non-property: like marriage, fosterage, divorce, agency, will, two men or one man and two women. A woman, he only said this because if the defects of women are such that men can see them: like an extra finger for example, the testimony of one woman is not sufficient. (And for other than it: property or non-property: like marriage, fosterage, divorce, agency, will, two men or one man and two women): he only said property or non-property because there is a dispute with al-Shafi'i, for indeed non-property does not accept the testimony of one man and two women according to him, rather this is specific to property. [1] His saying: 'a woman' refers to one, with the condition of freedom, sanity, Islam, and majority; the most precautionary is two women, the most beloved is three, and the way out of the dispute is nature (i.e., reliance on natural disposition), and the wording of testimony is required according to the scholars of Khurasan, not according to the scholars of Iraq.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling from the matn of Al-Wiqaya, which the commentator is expanding. The ruling states that for matters other than financial—such as marriage, fosterage, divorce, agency, and wills—the required number of witnesses is either two men or one man and two women. The commentator clarifies that the mention of 'property or non-property' is to highlight a difference with Imam al-Shafi'i, who only accepts the testimony of one man and two women in financial matters, not in non-financial ones. The commentator then notes an exception: if the defects of women are visible to men (e.g., an extra finger), then the testimony of a single woman is insufficient. In the footnote, it adds that the one woman must be free, sane, Muslim, and adult; it is recommended to have two or three women. There is also a scholarly difference on whether the word 'shahada' (testimony) must be explicitly uttered: Khurasani scholars require it, while Iraqi scholars do not.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony given in court; in this context, the number and qualification of witnesses required for different types of claims.
غير مال (ghayr māl): Matters that are not purely financial, such as marriage, divorce, lineage, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One man and two women
C) Either two men or one man and two women
D) Three women

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows one man and two women as witnesses for non-financial matters, contrary to the Shafi'i position which restricts this to financial matters.

Women's Testimony on a Newborn's Cry for Inheritance: Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on women's testimony on the newborn's cry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on accepting women's testimony on istihlal for inheritance, and explain the reasoning (qiyas and istihsan) behind each position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa rejects women's testimony on a newborn's cry for inheritance because it is audible to men, but his companions accept it due to customary male absence.

This passage presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute on whether women's testimony on a newborn's first cry (istihlal) can establish the child's right to inherit. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between the cry—which is theoretically audible to men—and the birth itself, which is hidden. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, along with the other three Sunni schools, argue that since men are not customarily present at childbirth, necessity requires accepting women's testimony. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school balances textual analogy (qiyas) with practical custom (urf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage discusses two distinct testimonies: (1) a man testifying to seeing a birth, and (2) women testifying to the newborn's cry. Focus on the latter. Note that the cry (istihlal) is used as evidence of live birth for inheritance.
The man's testimony part is peripheral; the core is the women's testimony on the cry.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Abu Hanifa says women's testimony on istihlal is NOT accepted for inheritance. His reason: the cry is a sound hearable by men, so it is not exclusively a female domain. He analogizes it to wounds in bathhouses (where women's testimony is accepted because men cannot see), but distinguishes it because men could in principle be present to hear the cry.
The same testimony is accepted for prayer because prayer is a religious matter where even a single woman’s report suffices (like crescent sighting).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its basis
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept women's testimony on istihlal for inheritance. Their reason: men are not ordinarily present at childbirth, so in practice the cry is only heard by women. Hence necessity (darura) requires acceptance, analogous to birth itself.
This view aligns with the majority of schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali).
4
Analyze the qiyas and istihsan
Identify the qiyas (analogy) used by Abu Hanifa: cry is like wounds in bathhouses—both are potentially accessible to men, so women's testimony is not accepted. The Sahibayn use istihsan (juristic preference) based on custom: since men are absent, the rule should be like birth. Note that the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn is not given in the text; the dispute is presented as unresolved.
Later Hanafi fatwa often adopts the Sahibayn's view due to practical necessity.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa's view, if only women testify to the cry, the child does not inherit. Under the Sahibayn's view, the child inherits based on that testimony. This affects inheritance distribution in cases where the only evidence of live birth is women's testimony.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is not stated here; later authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الشُّمُنِّي : لو شهد بالولادة رجل بأن قال فأجابها فاتفق نظري إليها تقبل إذا كان ولو قال : تعمدت النظر لا تقبل ، وبه قال بعض أصحاب الشافعي له، وقال عدلاً، بعض مشايخنا : تقبل أيضاً، وبه قال بعض أصحاب الشافعي . ولا تقبل شهادة النساء على استهلال الصبي عند أبي حنيفة له في حق الإرث ، ويقبل في حق الصلاة ؛ لأنَّ الاستهلال صوت مسموع، والرجال والنساء فيه سواء ، فكان مما يطلع عليه الرجال ، وإن لم يحضروا صار شهادتهن عليه كشهادتهن على جراحات النساء في الحمامات، بخلاف الولادة، فإنّها انفصال الولد من الأم فلا يطلعُ عليه الرجال، والصلاة من أمور الدين، وخبر المرأة الواحدة حجّةٌ في ذلك، كشهادتها على هلال رمضان. وقال أبو يوسف الله و محمد الله : تقبل في حق الإرث أيضاً، وبه قال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد الله ؛ لأنَّ الرجال في العادة لا يحضرون في ذلك الموضع ؛ ليسمعوا صوته، فصارت كشهادتهن على الولادة (" ). [1] قوله : امرأة؛ [بالنسبة للحديث السابق]... [2] قوله : لا يقبل فيه...الخ ; الأصل : عدم قبول شهادتهن ; لنقصان العقل، واختلاط الضبط، وقصور الولاية، فإنّها لا تصلح للخلافة؛ ولهذا لا تقبل شهادتهن وحدهن وإن كثرن، ولا مع الرجال في الحدود والقصاص.
And al-Shumunni mentioned: If a man testifies to a birth by saying 'he answered her, so my sight fell upon her' it is accepted if he was [just?]... and if he said 'I deliberately looked' it is not accepted, and some of al-Shafi'i's companions said the same. Some of our scholars said: it is also accepted, and some of al-Shafi'i's companions said the same. And the testimony of women on the cry of a newborn is not accepted according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, regarding inheritance, but it is accepted regarding prayer because the cry is a sound that is heard, and men and women are equal in that, so it is something that men can know about, and even if they are not present, their testimony becomes like their testimony on women's wounds in bathhouses, contrary to birth, for it is the separation of the child from the mother which men cannot know about, and prayer is a matter of religion, and the report of one woman is a proof in that, like her testimony on the crescent of Ramadan. And Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: it is accepted regarding inheritance as well, and al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, may Allah have mercy on them, said the same, because men are not ordinarily present in that place to hear his cry, so it becomes like their testimony on birth. [2] His saying: 'it is not accepted in it...' the principle is non-acceptance of their testimony due to deficiency of intellect, mixture of inaccuracy, and deficiency of authority, for they are not fit for leadership; hence their testimony alone is not accepted even if many, nor with men in hadd and qisas.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute specifically regarding the acceptance of women's testimony on the cry of a newborn (istihlal) for determining inheritance rights. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such testimony is not accepted for inheritance because the cry is a sound that men could potentially hear if present; thus it is not exclusively women's domain. However, he accepts it for prayer (e.g., to confirm live birth for funeral prayer) because prayer is a religious matter where a single woman's report is sufficient, analogous to her testimony on the crescent of Ramadan. The two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, along with the other three Sunni imams, accept women's testimony on istihlal for inheritance as well, reasoning that men are not customarily present at childbirth to hear the cry, so necessity dictates acceptance. The footnote explains the general principle of non-acceptance of women's testimony alone due to their perceived deficiencies, but exceptions are made in certain cases.

Key Terms
استهلال (istihlāl): The cry of a newborn immediately after birth; used as evidence of live birth.
جراحات النساء في الحمامات (jirāḥāt al-nisā' fī al-ḥammāmāt): Wounds of women in bathhouses; an example where women's testimony alone is accepted because men cannot see.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because men are not ordinarily present at childbirth to hear the cry, so it is like birth itself.
C) Because inheritance matters require two women witnesses by default.
D) Because prayer is a religious matter and they extend that analogy.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of women's testimony on a newborn's cry for inheritance is disputed in the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa rejects it based on the cry's theoretical audibility to men, while the Sahibayn and other schools accept it based on the customary absence of men at childbirth.

Requirement of 'Adala and Acceptance of Women's Testimony
Explains the requirement of 'adala and the acceptance of women's testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of 'adala for witnesses and explain the Hanafi rationale for accepting women's testimony in financial and family matters.

Core Idea
Witness testimony requires 'adala; women's testimony is accepted in financial and family matters due to necessity and compensated forgetfulness.

This lesson examines the requirement of uprightness ('adala) for all witnesses, as derived from the Quran, and the specific reasoning behind the Hanafi acceptance of women's testimony in certain cases. The commentator explains that while 'adala is a universal condition, women's testimony is limited to financial matters and related rights due to a natural deficiency in retention that is compensated by pairing them. The passage also clarifies that testimony is an original proof, and the only obstacle is doubt (shubha), which does not bar rights like property and marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its proof
Recognize that 'adala is a condition for accepting testimony from all witnesses, as established by the Quranic verses Al-Talaq 65:2 and Al-Baqarah 2:282.
The phrase 'ذَوَى عَدْلٍ' directly indicates the need for 'adala.
2
Understand the scope of women's testimony
Note that women's testimony is accepted in financial matters and their adjuncts (e.g., lending, hiring) due to necessity and frequent occurrence.
The rationale includes low risk and high frequency.
3
Analyze the compensatory mechanism
Recognize that women's deficiency in retention is compensated by requiring two women to testify together, as opposed to one man.
This is based on the verse 'two women from those you approve of the witnesses'.
4
Contrast with areas of exclusion
Understand that women's testimony is not accepted in hadd penalties and qisas because these are not established with any doubt (shubha).
The text argues that rights like marriage, divorce, and property are established despite doubt, even stronger than jest.
5
Trace the proof from caliphic practice
Note that the commentator cites 'Umar and 'Ali's acceptance of women's testimony in marriage and divorce as additional evidence.
This shows that women's testimony is not limited to financial matters alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط للكل العدالة (1)
[1] قوله : وشرط للكلّ أي لوجوب قبول شهادة الرجال والنساء في الحدود وغيرها من الحقوق العدالة، وإنما شرطت لقوله : وَأَشْهِدُوا ذَوَى عَدْلٍ مِنكُمْ ( الطلاق: 2 ) وهو ظاهر ؛ لقوله تعالى: مِمَّن تَرْضَوْنَ مِنَ الشُّهَدَاء ( البقرة: 282 ). والمرضي من الشاهد هو العدل؛ ولأنَّ مَن يباشر غير الكذب من الموصي قد يباشر الكذب؛ وهذا لأنَّ الخبر محتمل للصدق والكذب، ويترجح جانب الصدق بالعدالة .
وإنّما قبلت في الأموال وتوابعها كالإعارة والإجارة والكفالة والأجل وشرط الخيار؛ للضرورة؛ لكثرة وقوعها، وقلّة خطرها.
ولنا : ما روي أنَّ عمر وعليّاً له أجازا بشهادة النساء مع الرجال في النكاح والفرقة، وهذا نص على أن تقبل شهادتهن مع الرجال غير الأموال أيضاً؛ ولأن الشهادة حجَّة أصلية لا ضروريّة، والأصل فيها القبول بوجود ما يبتنى عليه أهلية الشهادة، وهي الولاية، وهي تبتنى على الحرية والإرث؛ ولوجودِ أهلية القبول. وهي تتبنى على انتفاء التهمة بالكذب والغلط، فالكذب ينتفي بالعدالة، والغلط ينتفي باتقان المعاينة والضبط والأداء؛ لأنَّ بالأوَّل يحصل العلم، وبالثاني يحصل البقاء والدوام، وبالثالث يحصل العلم للقاضي؛ ولهذا تقبل روايتها في الأخبار. وكان ينبغي أن تقبل شهادتهنَّ مطلقاً كالرجال، ولكـن جـاءَ النص بخلافه، ونقصان الضبط بزيادة النسيان ينجبر بضم الأخرى إليها، فلم يبق بعد ذلك إلا الشبهة، وهذه الحقوق تثبت مع الشبهة كالمال بل وفوقه ألا ترى أنَّ النكاح يثبت مع الهزل، وكذا الطلاق والعتاق والمالُ لا يثبت به، وأي شبهة أقوى من الهزل، بخلاف الحدودِ والقصاص؛ لأنها لا تثبت مع الشبهة.
And 'adala is a condition for all. [1] His saying: 'and a condition for all' i.e., for the obligation of accepting the testimony of men and women in hadd penalties and other rights, 'adala is a condition. It is conditioned because of His saying: 'And bring to witness two witnesses from among your men, and if not two men, then one man and two women from those you approve of the witnesses' (Al-Baqarah: 282). And the one approved of among witnesses is the 'adl; and because the one who avoids lying in his recommendation may still lie; this is because a report is susceptible to truth and falsehood, and the side of truth is strengthened by 'adala. And it is only accepted in financial matters and their adjuncts like lending, hiring, guarantee, term, and stipulation of option, due to necessity because of their frequent occurrence and low risk. And our proof: what is narrated that 'Umar and 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with them, allowed the testimony of women with men in marriage and separation, and this is explicit that their testimony with men is accepted in non-financial matters as well. And because testimony is an original proof, not a necessary one, and the principle is acceptance upon the existence of what the eligibility for testimony is based upon, which is authority (wilaya), and it is based on freedom and inheritance; and due to the existence of eligibility for acceptance. And it is based on the absence of suspicion of lying and error; lying is negated by 'adala, and error is negated by precision of observation, retention, and performance; because by the first, knowledge is obtained, by the second, permanence and continuity, by the third, knowledge is obtained for the judge; hence their narration is accepted in reports. It would have been appropriate that their testimony be accepted absolutely like men, but the text came contrary to that, and the deficiency of retention due to increased forgetfulness is compensated by adding another woman to her, so after that nothing remains except doubt, and these rights are established despite doubt like property and even more; don't you see that marriage is established despite jest, and similarly divorce and manumission, while property is not established by it, and what doubt is stronger than jest? Contrary to hadd penalties and qisas, because they are not established with doubt.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage addresses the requirement of 'adala (uprightness) for all witnesses. The commentator explains that 'adala is necessary based on Quranic verses (Al-Baqarah: 282 and Al-Talaq: 2) which require 'righteous' witnesses. The testimony of women is accepted in financial matters and their adjuncts due to necessity, as these transactions occur frequently and involve low risk. The commentator then provides proof from the practice of Caliphs 'Umar and 'Ali, who accepted women's testimony with men in marriage and divorce, indicating acceptance in non-financial matters as well. The reasoning is that testimony is an original proof; women have the capacity for testimony based on eligibility (wilaya), and their deficiency in retention is compensated by having two women. The only remaining issue is doubt (shubha), but rights like marriage, divorce, and property are established despite doubt—even stronger, as marriage is valid even if uttered in jest, which is the strongest doubt. However, hadd penalties and qisas are not established with doubt.

Key Terms
عدالة (ʻadāla): The quality of being upright, just, and avoiding major sins and minor sins consistently; a necessary condition for a witness's testimony to be accepted.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that can prevent the application of hadd penalties; in this context, it refers to the doubt that might arise from women's testimony, which is tolerated in financial and family matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Quranic evidence cited for the requirement of 'adala in witnesses?
A) Al-Baqarah 282: 'And bring to witness two witnesses from among your men'
B) Al-Talaq 2: 'And bring to witness two witnesses of 'adl'
C) Al-Nisa 15: 'And those who commit immorality among your women'
D) Al-Maida 106: 'O you who have believed, testimony among you'

Key Takeaway
The condition of 'adala is universal for all witnesses, and women's testimony is accepted in financial and family matters due to necessity and compensated forgetfulness, but not in hadd penalties due to the presence of doubt.

The Condition of 'Adalah for Testimony
Ruling with proof on the condition of ‘adalah for testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of 'adalah (righteousness) for witnesses and identify the Quranic proofs that establish it.

Core Idea
‘Adalah is a Quranic condition for all testimony, ensuring the witness’s truthfulness.

This passage opens by asserting that ‘adalah (righteousness) is a condition for accepting any testimony. It then cites Quranic verses to ground this rule. In this lesson, we examine the textual basis and the Hanafi interpretation of ‘adalah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving testimony (shahadah). The ruling is that it is valid only if the witness possesses ‘adalah. Without ‘adalah, the testimony is not accepted.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites two Quranic verses: 'Wa ash'hidu dhaway 'adlin minkum' (65:2) and 'mimman tardawna mina al-shuhada'' (2:282). Identify that these are the primary textual evidence.
The first verse commands calling two just witnesses; the second speaks of witnesses you approve.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command to call witnesses who are ‘adl indicates that ‘adalah is a condition for the testimony to be valid. The term ‘adl is interpreted as having religious rectitude.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub, so the command implies obligation of condition.
4
Note the definition of ‘adalah
The passage explains that the approved witness is the ‘adl, and that ‘adalah negates lying and strengthens truthfulness. In Hanafi fiqh, ‘adalah means avoiding major sins and not persisting on minor sins.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab aspect
The condition of ‘adalah is agreed upon, but definitions vary slightly. This passage focuses on the Hanafi view.

Key Terms

Women's Testimony: Scope and Rationale in Hanafi Law
Ruling with proof on the scope of women's testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on women's testimony, identify the cases where it is accepted, and state the rationale based on necessity and shubhah.

Core Idea
Women's testimony is accepted with men in all non-hudud/qisas cases, including marriage and divorce, due to necessity and the principle that rights are established despite shubhah.

The passage continues by specifying the scope of women's testimony. It acknowledges the general rule that women's testimony alone is not accepted, but it is accepted with men in financial matters and their derivatives. Moreover, based on the practice of 'Umar and 'Ali, it extends to marriage and divorce. This lesson explores the rationale, including the concept of shubhah and compensation for forgetfulness.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for women's testimony
Women's testimony alone is not accepted, nor with men in hudud and qisas. It is accepted in financial matters and their follow-ups (like lending, hiring, guarantee) due to necessity.
2
Identify the proof for extension beyond financial matters
The passage cites the practice of 'Umar and 'Ali who accepted women's testimony with men in marriage and divorce (nikah and firqah). This is considered a clear text (nass) that extends beyond financial matters.
This is the Hanafi proof for including marriage and divorce.
3
Analyze the rationale: testimony as original proof
Testimony is an original proof (hujjah asliyyah) not based on necessity. The capacity for testimony (ahliyyah al-shahadah) is based on authority (wilayah), which is present in women (based on freedom and inheritance). Lying is negated by 'adalah; error is compensated by having two women.
4
Discuss the role of shubhah (doubt)
After compensating for forgetfulness by pairing women, only shubhah remains. Rights like financial and marriage are established despite shubhah, as seen with marriage being valid despite jest (hazl). Hudud and qisas are not established with shubhah.
This is the key distinction.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school restricts women's testimony to financial matters only, not accepting it in marriage and divorce. The Hanafi school relies on the practice of the Companions.

Defining 'Adalah: The Hanafi Standard
Defining 'adalah via multiple scholarly opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'adalah as given in al-Tanqih and distinguish it from other definitions mentioned.

Core Idea
'Adalah is abstention from religious prohibitions, a condition for valid testimony.

This passage from ‘Umdat al-Ri‘ayah presents multiple definitions of ‘adalah (righteousness/justice) as discussed in the Hanafi school. The author settles on the definition from al-Tanqih: abstention from religious prohibitions. Understanding these definitions is essential because ‘adalah is a key condition for the validity of testimony (shahadah) in Islamic courts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary definition
The text first quotes al-Tanqih: 'al-‘adalah hiya al-inzajar ‘an al-mahzurat al-diniyyah' (abstention from religious prohibitions). This is the relied-upon definition.
2
Examine the additional definitions
The text then lists other definitions: avoiding major sins, not persisting on minor sins, truthfulness, etc. Note the common themes of avoiding wrongdoing and maintaining integrity.
3
Understand the exclusionary effect
The third definition explicitly excludes the disbeliever, the immoral, and the innovator from being considered 'adil.
4
Relate ‘adalah to testimony
Recognize that ‘adalah is a condition for the witness's acceptability. The witness must be 'adil in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالعدالة والعدالة على ما قال المصنف الله في «التنقيح»: «هي الانزجار من المحظورات الدينية».
وقيل : أن يجتنب عن الكبائر، ولا يصر على الصغائر، ويكون صلاحه أكثر من
فساده، وأن يستعمل الصدق، ويجتنب عن الكذب ديانة ومروءة.

محافظة دينيَّةٌ تحملُ صاحبها على ملازمة التقوي والمروءة من غير
بدعة، فخرج به الكافر والفاسق والمبتدع.
وقيل : هي هيأة راسخة في النفس من الدين، تحمل صاحبها على ملازمة التقوى
والمروءة، وتقرب منهما.
وقيل : هي ملكة في النفس تمنعها عن اقتراف الكبائر، والإصرار على الصغائر،
وعن الرذائل المباحة.
ويقرب منه أيضاً ما قال الحكماء : هي التوسط بين بين الإفراط والتفريط، وهي مركبة من الحكمة والعفة والشجاعة، فاختلفت العبارات في التعبير عنها ، ذكرنا بالاختصار، والتفصيل في مبسوطات الأعلام الأخيار.

قال الله : وَأَقِيمُوا الشَّهَادَةَ لِلَّهِ ) ، وقال له : وَأَشْهِدُوا إِذَا تَبَايَعْتُمْ ) ومثل ذلك ، وقال ل له : «إذا علمت مثل الشمس فأشهد»(4).

(٤) أخرجه الحاكم وصححه والبيهقي وضعفه والعقيلي (٤) : (٦٩) ، وأعله بمحمد بن سليمان ، ولفظه : عن ابن عباس أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سئل عن الشهادة ، فقال : رأيت الشمس فاشهد على مثلها أو دع ولا يعرف إلا به، ينظر: «التخليص»(٤ : ٦٩٨)، و(خلاصة البدر(٢ : ٤٣٩) ، ونصب الراية (٤ : ٨٢).
By righteousness, and righteousness according to what the author said in al-Tanqih: 'It is abstention from religious prohibitions.' And it was said: That he avoids major sins, does not persist on minor sins, and his good deeds are more than his bad deeds, and he uses truthfulness and avoids lies out of religion and manliness. And it was said: It is a religious preservation that carries its possessor to adhere to piety and manliness without innovation; thus the disbeliever, the immoral, and the innovator are excluded. And it was said: It is a deep-seated disposition in the soul from religion that carries its possessor to adhere to piety and manliness and brings them close. And it was said: It is a faculty in the soul that prevents it from committing major sins, persisting on minor sins, and from permissible base habits. And close to that is what the philosophers said: It is the median between excess and deficiency, and it is composed of wisdom, chastity, and courage. So the expressions differed in describing it; we have mentioned it briefly, and the details are in the extensive works of the great scholars. [1] His statement: 'And the wording of testimony' because the textual evidence regarding it has only come with the word 'shahadah'. Allah said: 'And establish the testimony for Allah' (Quran 65:2), and He said: 'And take witnesses when you transact' (Quran 2:282), and similar. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If you know it like the sun, then testify.' And because it contains increased emphasis; for the word 'ashhadu' is from the expressions of oath, so the meaning of oath is observed in it, and his abstention from lying by this word 'ashhadu' is because this meaning is not found in other words.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage presents multiple definitions of 'adalah (righteousness/justice) from the Hanafi perspective, culminating in the definition from al-Tanqih: abstention from religious prohibitions. It emphasizes that 'adalah requires avoiding major sins and not persisting on minor sins, truthfulness, and pious conduct. The second part discusses the requirement that testimony be pronounced with the specific wording 'ashhadu' (I testify). It cites Quranic verses and a hadith where the Prophet instructed to testify only when certain. The word 'ashhadu' is considered an oath, reinforcing the witness's commitment to truth.

Key Terms
العدالة (al-‘adalah): Defined in the text as abstention from religious prohibitions, avoidance of major sins, non-persistence on minor sins, truthfulness, and pious conduct.
لفظ الشهادة (lafz al-shahadah): The specific wording used when giving testimony, which must be 'ashhadu' (I testify).
أشهد (ashhadu): Arabic word meaning 'I testify', considered a form of oath that reinforces truthfulness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which definition of 'adalah is attributed to the author of al-Tanqih?
A) Avoiding major sins and not persisting on minor sins
B) Abstention from religious prohibitions
C) Being a median between excess and deficiency
D) A deep-seated disposition in the soul

Key Takeaway
‘Adalah in the Hanafi school is primarily defined as abstention from religious prohibitions, and it is a fundamental condition for the acceptability of testimony.

The Wording of Testimony: Why 'Ashhadu' is Required
Ruling on the wording of testimony with textual and rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi requirement that testimony be pronounced with the word 'ashhadu' and identify the dalil for this ruling.

Core Idea
Testimony must be given with 'ashhadu' because it is an oath, reinforcing truthfulness.

This passage from ‘Umdat al-Ri‘ayah explains the rationale behind the Hanafi ruling that the word 'ashhadu' (I testify) is a required wording for testimony in court. It cites Quranic verses and a hadith to support this position, and argues that 'ashhadu' contains an element of oath, which deters false testimony.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The Hanafi school requires the witness to say 'ashhadu' (I testify) when giving testimony. Other expressions like 'I know' are not sufficient.
2
Identify the textual evidence
The passage cites Quran 65:2 'And establish the testimony for Allah' and Quran 2:282 'And take witnesses when you transact', as well as the hadith 'If you know it like the sun, then testify' (فأشهد).
The hadith uses the word 'fashhad' which is from the same root as 'ashhadu'.
3
Analyze the linguistic implication
The command 'fashhad' implies the use of the word 'ashhad' as the proper wording. The mere fact of knowing is not enough; one must actively testify using the specific word.
4
Understand the rationale
The word 'ashhadu' is an expression of oath (yamin). This adds emphasis and deters perjury. The meaning of oath is not present in other words like 'a'lam' (I know).
This rational argument (dalil 'aqli) supports the textual evidence.

Judge's Inquiry into Witness Integrity: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on judge's inquiry into witness justice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the judge's duty to investigate witness justice, identify the evidence for each view, and explain why the Sahibayn's view is the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A judge may rely on a Muslim's apparent justice unless the opponent objects, except in hudud and qisas—but later corruption shifts the rule.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah addresses a key procedural question: Must a judge actively investigate the character of witnesses before accepting their testimony? The answer reveals a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage also clarifies the distinction between justice as a condition for the obligation of acceptance versus the validity of testimony itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core disagreement
State Abu Hanifa's position and the position of the Sahibayn. Abu Hanifa says the judge does not inquire unless the opponent objects, except in hudud and qisas. The Sahibayn say the judge must inquire in all cases, with or without objection.
The disagreement hinges on whether apparent justice (zahir) suffices as proof.
2
Locate Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith: 'Muslims are just against one another, except one who has been punished for slander.' He also uses the principle that the apparent state of a Muslim (his intellect and religion) deters him from false testimony. In the absence of an contestant, this apparent is sufficient.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is qat'i here.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's counter-argument
The Sahibayn argue that judgment must be based on proof (hujja), and apparent justice is not a sufficient proof for entitlement. Moreover, the prevalence of corruption in later times renders the apparent unreliable. Therefore, the judge must investigate to avoid nullity.
Their view is considered a response to changed social conditions.
4
Note the exception for hudud and qisas
Even Abu Hanifa requires inquiry in hudud and qisas because these are averted by doubts. The judge must actively seek reasons to drop such severe punishments. This exception shows that the principle of caution overrides the default reliance on apparent justice.
This exception aligns with the broader principle of 'daf' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and rationale
The passage states that fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn's view due to widespread corruption (kathrat al-fasad) in the presenter time. This is a clear example of tarjih based on changing circumstances (taghayyur al-zaman).
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah; the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter of testimony and retraction thereof / Its definition, number, and what the witness bears. So it is not accepted if he says: 'I know' or 'I am certain', and a judge does not inquire about a witness without the opponent's objection, that justice is a condition for us for obligation of acceptance, not for validity of acceptance. So for the non-just, it is not obligatory upon the judge to accept his testimony, but if he accepts and judges by it, his judgment is valid. So it is not accepted if he says: 'I know' or 'I am certain', and a judge does not inquire about a witness without the opponent's objection. And the scholars of Iraq said: The wording of testimony is not required in the testimony of women in matters that men do not see, because it is a report not a testimony, so it becomes like the testimony for the crescent of Ramadan. The first is correct because it is testimony due to its containing the meaning of obligation, so it is specific to the court, and freedom and Islam are required in it. [1] His saying: 'Know...etc.'; Know that the author (may Allah have mercy on him) equated justice and the wording of testimony in being conditions, following the author of al-Hidayah, but it is not so, because the wording of testimony is a pillar like the validity of performance, and justice is not a condition for the validity of performance, but its manifestation is a condition for the obligation of judgment upon the judge. Hence he said in al-Tanwir: Justice is for its obligation, not for its validity. So if he judges by the testimony of a wrongdoer (fasiq), it is executed. End. And he said in al-Hidayah: If he judges by the testimony of a wrongdoer, it is valid according to us. End. And he added in al-Fath: And the judge would be sinful. End. So the commentator wanted to clarify what is correct, so he said: 'Know...etc.' (2) His saying: 'His judgment is valid'; because the wrongdoer is qualified for the office of judgment and authority, so he is qualified for testimony. And from Abu Yusuf: If the wrongdoer is prominent among people and possesses manliness, his testimony is accepted, due to the absence of suspicion of lying in his testimony. The first is more correct, as they have stated. (3) His saying: 'So it is not accepted'; because the texts speak of bearing witness (al-ishhad) as previously mentioned, so nothing else takes its place. (1) Al-Hidayah (3:118). (2) Tanwir al-Absar (p. 151). (3) Al-Hidayah (3:118). (4) Fath al-Qadir (6:456). [PAGE 532] Zubdat al-Nihayah li-`Umdat al-Ri`ayah. Except in a hadd punishment or qisas, and they (the two companions) said: He inquires in all cases. [1] Meaning: The judge does not inquire nor investigate whether the witness is just or unjust if the opponent does not object to him, except in a hadd punishment or qisas, and they (the two companions) said: He inquires in all cases. [1] His saying: 'He does not inquire...etc.'; So the judge relies on the apparent justice of a Muslim, and does not inquire about him until the opponent objects, except in hudud and qisas; due to what Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated in his Musannaf: 'From Abd al-Rahman ibn Sulayman ibn Hajjaj, from Amr ibn Shu`ayb, from his father, from his grandfather, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Muslims are just against one another, except one who has been punished for slander.' And because the apparent state is deterrence; because his intellect and religion prevent him from committing evil, so the apparent is relied upon in the absence of a contestant, contrary to hudud and qisas; because they are averted by doubts, and caution is taken to drop them in each case initially without objection from an opponent, hoping they may be dropped. [2] His saying: 'If the opponent does not object to him'; But if he objects, then the judge inquires, because he would not object falsely apparently, so the two apparents conflict, so weighing by investigation becomes necessary. [3] His saying: 'And they (the two companions) said: He inquires in all cases'; i.e., in all other rights and claims, whether the opponent objects or not; because judgment is based on proof, which is the testimony of just persons, and justice before inquiry is established by apparent, and it is not suitable as proof for entitlement, so it became necessary to inquire about them to guard against nullity. And according to their view, fatwa is given. Thus in al-Hidayah and others, due to widespread corruption in judgments in this time. (1) In Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah (5:76) and others. (2) Al-Hidayah (3:118). (3) Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (7:63). (4) Multaqat al-Fatawa (p. 382).
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah deals with the rules of testimony (shahada), specifically the judge's duty to inquire into the justice (adala) of witnesses. The passage opens by clarifying that justice is a condition for the obligation of acceptance, not for the validity of the testimony itself – meaning a judge may accept the testimony of a fasiq (wrongdoer), though he would be sinful. The wording of testimony (lafz al-shahada) is a pillar, not a condition. The main ruling is that a judge does not investigate the character of a witness unless the opponent raises an objection (ta'n), except in cases of hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). This is based on the hadith that Muslims are just except those punished for slander, and on the principle that the apparent state of a Muslim is sufficient. However, the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the judge must inquire in all cases, because corruption has become widespread and apparent justice is not a sufficient basis for proof. The passage concludes that the view of Sahibayn is the relied-upon position for fatwa (mufta bihi) due to the prevalence of moral decay in later times. The commentator also notes that some scholars of Iraq do not require the word 'ashhadu' in women's testimony on matters men cannot see, but the correct view is that it is required because testimony carries the meaning of obligation. The passage thus covers both intra-Hanafi differences and practical judicial procedure.

Key Terms
عدالة (ʻadālah): Justice; a quality in a witness that makes his testimony acceptable. Here it is a condition for obligation of acceptance, not validity.
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony; a statement made in court to establish a right. It requires the wording 'ashhadu' (I testify) as a pillar.
طعن (ṭaʻn): Objection; a challenge by the opponent against the witness's integrity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in this passage, when must the judge inquire into the justice of a witness?
A) Only when the opponent objects in hudud and qisas.
B) In all cases, whether the opponent objects or not.
C) Only in hudud and qisas, with or without objection.
D) Only if the witness is a fasiq known to the judge.

Key Takeaway
In contemporary Hanafi practice, due to widespread corruption, judges must investigate witness integrity in all cases, following the Sahibayn's view.
