Judge's Reliance on His Written Record of Testimony
Intra-Hanafi dispute on judge's written testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a judge's reliance on his written testimony and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A judge may rule from his sealed register when memory fails; the seal provides certainty that private documents lack.

This passage addresses a practical problem: when a judge forgets the testimony but has it recorded in his official register, can he still issue a ruling? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa insists on direct recollection, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, allow reliance on the register due to necessity. Later authorities have settled on the position of the Sahibayn as the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue and scenario
The passage deals with a judge who recorded testimony in his official register (dīwān/kharīṭa) under his seal, then forgot the case. Can he rule based on that record?
The dispute is limited to this exact scenario, not to private documents (ṣakk).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the judge cannot rule without recalling the testimony because handwriting resembles handwriting (al-khaṭṭ yushbihu al-khaṭṭ), so certainty is not achieved.
His argument is based on the possibility of forgery and lack of certainty.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the judge may rule because his register is under his seal, protecting it from tampering, and due to the judge's heavy workload, forgetfulness is inevitable. The seal provides sufficient certainty.
They distinguish between the sealed register and a private document (ṣakk) in the litigant's hand.
4
Explain the distinction between register and private document
The judge's register is under his seal, ensuring integrity; a private document (ṣakk) is in the hand of a litigant and vulnerable to alteration, so a witness cannot rely on it.
This distinction is key to the Sahibayn's reasoning.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and later authorities
Later scholars like al-Khalwani, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and al-Taqwim preferred the Sahibayn's position, making it the relied-upon fatwa.
The operative ruling is that the judge may rely on his sealed register.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما الخلاف فيما إذا وَجَدَ القاضي شهادتَهُ في ديوانه؛ لأنَّ ما يكون تحت ختمِهِ يؤمن عليه التغيير بخلاف الصَّكَ فإنَّه في يد الخصم. وقال شمس الأئمة الخَلْوَانِي : ينبغي أن يفتى بقول محمد الله، وهكذا في «الأجناس». كذا في «الخلاصة»، وجزم في «البَزَّازيّة» بأنه يفتى بقول محمد، وفي «البحر» معزياً إلى «المبتغى»: من وجد خطه وعرفه ونسي الشهادة وسعه أن يشهد إذا كان في حوزه، وبه نأخذ. انتهى. وفي «السراج الوهاج» : و ما قاله أبو يوسف له هو المعمول به، وقال في «التقويم»: قولهما هو الصحيح. انتهى. فعلى هذا ينبغي للشارح له أن يُفصل المسألة. [١] قوله : وجد القاضي شهادته ؛ بأن شهدَ الشهود عند القاضي فأثبت في خريطة، وجاء المشهود له يطلبُ الحكم، ولم يحفظه القاضي فعلى قول أبي حنيفة له لا يحكم القاضي بدون الذكر ؛ لأنَّ الخطّ يشبه الخط، فلم يحصل العلم. وعندهما يحكم ؛ لأنَّ القاضي لكثرة أشغالِهِ يعجز عن حفظ كل حادثة ؛ ولهذا يكتب، وإنما يحصل المقصود بالكتاب إذا جاز له الاعتماد عليه عند النسيان الذي لا يمكن التحرز عنه ، وما يكون في خريطته يكون تحت ختمِهِ فيؤمن من الزيادة والنقصانِ فحصل له العلم بذلك. بخلاف الصك، فإنَّ الشاهد إذا وجد شهادته من الصك ، وعَلِمَ أنه خطه لا يحلُّ له أن يشهد بمجرد وجدان الشهادة في الصك ؛ لأنَّ الصك في يد غير القاضي فلا يكون تحت ختمه ليؤمن عليه من الزيادة والنقصان ، فلا يحصل العلم بذلك.
The difference of opinion is only when the judge finds his testimony in his register; because what is under his seal is safe from alteration, unlike the document which is in the hand of the opponent. Shams al-A'imma al-Khalwani said: It is appropriate to give fatwa according to the saying of Muhammad, and thus in al-Ajnas. Likewise in al-Khulasa, and al-Bazzaziyya affirmed that fatwa is given by Muhammad's saying, and in al-Bahr quoting al-Mubtagha: Whoever finds his writing and recognizes it but forgot the testimony, it is permissible for him to testify if it is in his possession, and we take this. End. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: What Abu Yusuf said is the operative rule, and in al-Taqwim: Their saying is correct. End. So on this basis, it is appropriate for the commentator to detail the issue. [1] His saying: the judge found his testimony; that is, when witnesses testified before the judge and he recorded it in his register, and the beneficiary comes seeking judgment, and the judge does not remember it; according to Abu Hanifa, the judge does not judge without recall because handwriting resembles handwriting, so certainty is not achieved. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he judges because the judge, due to his many occupations, is unable to remember every incident; therefore he writes, and the purpose is achieved by writing if he is allowed to rely on it when forgetfulness occurs, which cannot be avoided. What is in his register is under his seal, so it is safe from increase and decrease, and thus certainty is achieved. Unlike the document, when a witness finds his testimony in a document and knows it is his handwriting, it is not permissible for him to testify merely by finding the testimony in the document because the document is in the hand of someone other than the judge and is not under his seal to be safe from increase and decrease, so certainty is not achieved.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific issue within the broader topic of testimony: whether a judge may rely on his own written record of testimony when he has forgotten the case. The text begins by stating that the disagreement among the Hanafi imams is limited to this scenario. The matn establishes that testimony based on hearsay is generally not accepted, but an exception is made for the judge's own register. The commentary explains the rationale: the judge's register is under his seal, ensuring its integrity, unlike a private document (sakk) which is in the hands of the litigant and susceptible to tampering. Abu Hanifa holds that the judge cannot rule without direct recollection, as handwriting may be similar and does not produce certainty. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that due to the judge's heavy workload, forgetfulness is inevitable, and the sealed register provides sufficient certainty for him to rely on it. Later authorities discuss which position is preferred for fatwa: al-Khalwani and al-Bazzaziyya favor Muhammad's view, while al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Taqwim favor Abu Yusuf's or both. The commentator suggests that the issue should be detailed further. This intra-Hanafi dispute is resolved by later scholars in favor of the Sahibayn's position, which is the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
ديوان (dīwān): The judge's official register where he records testimony.
خريطة (kharīṭa): A record or register specifically belonging to the judge.
صك (ṣakk): A private document in the hand of a litigant, not under the judge's seal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), why may a judge rule based on his written record without remembering the testimony?
A) Because handwriting offers absolute certainty.
B) Because the register is under his seal and safe from tampering, and forgetfulness is inevitable.
C) Because the litigant confirms the testimony.
D) Because the judge is infallible in his memory.

Key Takeaway
The judge may rely on his sealed official register; this is the operative position in the Hanafi school.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Testimony by Hearsay: Qiyas versus Istihsan
Inter-madhhab dispute on hearsay testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi exceptions to the rule against hearsay testimony and explain the istihsan reasoning that overrides the qiyas.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is accepted where direct observation is impossible and public indicators create certainty.

The general rule in Islamic law is that testimony requires direct observation or tawatur. However, for certain matters that are inherently private yet have widespread legal consequences, Hanafi jurists make an exception by istihsan. This lesson examines the qiyas that would reject hearsay and the istihsan that accepts it for six specific categories, highlighting the inter-madhhab dispute over entry (dukhūl).

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The default ruling: no testimony by hearsay without direct sight. This is the baseline from which exceptions are carved.
The matn states: 'ولا يشهد بالتسامع' – He does not testify by hearsay.
2
List the six exceptions
Hanafis allow hearsay for lineage (nasab), death (mawt), marriage (nikāḥ), entry (dukhūl), appointment of a judge (wilāyat al-qāḍī), and the original establishment of a waqf (aṣl al-waqf).
Conditions of waqf are excluded because they are not widely known.
3
Understand the qiyas argument
The strict analogy (qiyas) would reject hearsay for these matters because testimony requires knowledge, and knowledge comes only from direct observation or tawatur. This would make hearsay like sale and lease, where it is not accepted.
The text says: 'والقياس أن لا تجوز' – The analogy is that it is not permissible.
4
Understand the istihsan argument
Istihsan overrides the qiyas because: (1) these matters are witnessed only by a few, yet their rulings persist; (2) requiring direct testimony would cause hardship (ḥaraj) and suspend rulings; (3) public notoriety (shuhra) substitutes for direct sight.
Circumstantial evidence (e.g., living as spouses) suffices due to necessity.
5
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Shāfiʿī, Mālik, and Aḥmad reject hearsay for entry specifically, analogizing to zinā which requires direct observation. The Hanafi response: entry has public consequences (linesage, mahr, ʿiddah, ihṣān) that make it distinct.
This is a legitimate ikhtilāf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بالتسامع بلا عيان
[٢] قوله : ولا يشهد بالتسامع ؛ أي بسبب التسامع بلا عيان، أي بشيء لم يعاينه إلا أن يشهد في النسب بأنَّ فلاناً ابن فلان أو أخوه ، والموت بأن فلانـاً قـد مـات ، والنكاح : بأن فلاناً قد تزوج فلانةً، والدخول : بأنَّ فلاناً تزوج فلانة ودخل بها ، وولاية القاضي بأنَّ فلاناً قد تولّي القضاء من جانب فلان الإمام. وأصل الوقف بأنَّ فلاناً وقف هذه الضيعة مثلاً، واحترز به عن شرائطه ؛ لأن أصل الوقف هو الذي يشتهر دون شرائطه فلا يقبل فيها بالتسامع، كما سيصرح الشارح إليه.
والقياس أن لا تجوز؛ لأنَّ الشهادة لا تجوز إلا بالعلم، ولا يتحقق العلم إلا بالمشاهدة والعيان أو بالخبر المتواتر، ولم يوجد ذلك، فصار كالبيع والإجارة، بل أولى ؛ لأنَّ حكم المال أخف من حكم النكاح ؛ ولهذا لا يجوز للقاضي أن يحكم بالتسامع، والحكم يجب بما تجب به الشهادة، ولهذا لو فسر للقاضي لا يقبله. ووجه الاستحسان : إنَّ هذه الأمور تختص بمعاينة أسبابها خواص من الناس ، ويتعلق بها أحكام تبقى على انقضاء القرون، وانقراض الأعصار، فلو لم تقبل فيها بالتسامع أدى إلى الحرج وتعطيل الأحكام ؛ ولأنَّ الأسباب يقترن بها ما تشتهر به. فإنَّ النسب : يشتهر بالتهنئة وإبنسبة كلّ واحدٍ إلى آخر عند المخاطبات ، والمنادات، والموت بالتعزية، وقسمة التركات، واندراس الآثار، والنكاح بالشهود، والولائم، والدخول : يتعلق أحكام مشهورة من النسب، والمهر، والعدة، وثبوتِ الإحصان، والقضاء : بقراءة المنشور ، واختلافُ الخصوم إليه، وازدحامهم عليه، فنزلت الشهرة منزلة العيان، فلا يشترط فيها المشاهدة.
بخلافِ البيع والهبة والإجارة وأمثالها ؛ لأنها لا تختص بشهادةِ أسبابها خواص من الناس، بل بحضرة الخاص والعام، وبه جرت العادة. ولأنَّ الناس قاطبةً مجمعون على أنهم يشهدون بهذه الأشياء بالشهرة، ألا ترى أنا نشهدُ أنَّ علياً تزوّج فاطمة رضي الله عنها ودخل بها، وشريحاً له كـان قاضياً، وعمر بن الخطاب له تزوج بنت علي له ، ولو تعلقت بحقيقة علم النسب أدّى إلى عدم الشهادة بها أصلاً ؛ لأنَّ سببَ النَّسب العلوق ، ولا علم للبشر فيه، وسبب القضاء والتولية ما لا يحضره إلا الوزير وأمثاله، وكذا الدخول لا يعرفه إلا الزوجان، فاكتفى في الكل بالدليل الظاهر. ثمَّ إنّما يجوز له أن يشهد بهذه بالتواتر، وبإخبار من يثق به، وإذا رأى امرأةً يدخل بها رجل وينبسطان انبساط الأزواج، وسمعَ من الناس أنها زوجته جاز له أن يشهد به، وإن لم يعاين عقد النكاح ، وكذا شخصاً إذا رأى جالساً مجلس القضاء يفصل، جاز له أن يشهد أنه قاض بكذا قالوا ، وقال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد ه : لا تقبل الشهادة بالتسامع في الدخول ؛ لأنه ما يعاين، كما في الشهادة على الزنا.
And not by hearsay without direct sight. [2] His saying: He does not testify by hearsay; that is, by way of hearsay without direct sight, meaning something he has not witnessed, except that he may testify concerning lineage that so-and-so is the son of so-and-so or his brother; death that so-and-so has died; marriage that so-and-so has married such-and-such woman; entry (dukhul) that so-and-so married such-and-such and consummated the marriage; appointment of a judge that so-and-so has been appointed judge by such-and-such imam; and the original establishment of a waqf that so-and-so endowed this estate, for example. He excludes the conditions of waqf because the original establishment is what is widely known, not its conditions, so hearsay is not accepted for them, as the commentator will clarify. The analogy (qiyas) dictates that it is not permissible because testimony is not permissible except with knowledge, and knowledge is only achieved by direct observation or tawatur, and that is not present. So it becomes like sale and lease, or even more so because the ruling concerning property is lighter than the ruling concerning marriage. Therefore, the judge may not judge by hearsay, and a ruling must be based on what testimony is based on. For this reason, if the judge is told directly, he does not accept it. The basis of istihsan is that these matters are such that only specific people witness their causes, yet rulings related to them persist across generations and eras. If hearsay were not accepted for them, it would lead to hardship and suspension of rulings. Also, these causes are associated with things that make them well-known. Lineage becomes known through congratulations and addressing each person as another's son; death through condolences, division of inheritance, and disappearance of traces; marriage through witnesses and wedding feasts; entry is associated with well-known rulings concerning lineage, dower, waiting period, and confirmation of ihsan; and the appointment of a judge through the reading of the decree and litigants coming to him and crowding around him. Thus, widespread reputation takes the place of direct sight, so direct observation is not required. This is unlike sale, gift, lease, and the like, because their causes are not witnessed only by specific people but in the presence of both the elite and the public, and this is the custom. Moreover, all people agree that they testify to these matters based on reputation. Do you not see that we testify that Ali married Fatimah (may Allah be pleased with them) and consummated the marriage, that Shurayh was a judge, and that Umar ibn al-Khattab married Umm Kulthum bint Ali? If testimony depended on the actual knowledge of lineage, it would lead to no testimony at all because the cause of lineage is conception, which no human knows. The cause of a judge's appointment is something that only the vizier and his like witness. Likewise, entry is only known by the spouses. Therefore, in all of these, circumstantial evidence suffices. Then, it is only permissible for him to testify to these through tawatur or through the report of someone he trusts. If he sees a woman entering with a man and they are relaxed like spouses, and hears from people that she is his wife, it is permissible for him to testify, even if he did not witness the marriage contract. Similarly, if he sees a person sitting in the judge's seat resolving disputes, it is permissible for him to testify that he is a judge. Thus they said. And al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad said: Testimony by hearsay is not accepted concerning entry because it is not witnessed, like testimony concerning zina.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on testimony based on hearsay (samāʿ/tawātuʿ). The matn states that hearsay without direct sight is generally not accepted for testimony. The commentary expands, explaining that the qiyas (analogical reasoning) would reject hearsay altogether because testimony requires certainty, which only comes from direct observation or tawātur. However, by istihsān (juristic preference), hearsay is accepted for specific matters that are inherently public and necessary for the functioning of society: lineage (nasab), death (mawt), marriage (nikāḥ), consummation (dukhūl), appointment of a judge (wilāyat al-qāḍī), and the original establishment of a waqf (aṣl al-waqf). Conditions of waqf are excluded because they are not widely known. The reasoning is that only specific individuals witness the actual causes of these matters, yet their rulings persist across generations. Accepting only direct testimony would lead to hardship (ḥaraj) and suspension of rulings. Public notoriety (shuhra) substitutes for direct sight. The text distinguishes these from transactions like sale, gift, and lease, which are customarily witnessed by the public. The passage then provides examples of widely accepted hearsay testimonies, such as the marriage of Ali and Fatima (RA) and the judgeship of Shurayh. Finally, it notes that Imams al-Shāfiʿī, Mālik, and Aḥmad disagree specifically regarding entry (dukhūl), requiring direct observation, similar to zinā. The Hanafi position is that entry can be testified based on hearsay due to its public indicators (e.g., living as spouses, public knowledge). This inter-madhhab dispute centers on the extent of istihsān and the analogy to zinā.

Key Terms
تسامع (tawātuʿ): Hearsay or widespread report that conveys general knowledge, often synonymous with tawātur in this context.
شهرة (shuhra): Public notoriety or widespread renown that substitutes for direct observation in legal testimony.
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas to avoid hardship and achieve a more equitable result.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is testimony by hearsay accepted for entry (dukhūl) in marriage but not for sale?
A) Because sale is more important than marriage.
B) Because entry is private and only known to the spouses, so hearsay is necessary, while sale is typically public.
C) Because the Quran explicitly allows hearsay for marriage.
D) Because there is a consensus of all schools on this point.

Key Takeaway
Hearsay testimony is a valid exception to the general rule, limited to six categories, justified by istihsan to avoid hardship.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony by Hearsay: The Hanafi Exception in Six Matters
Ruling on accepting testimony based on hearsay/reputation in specific matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six matters where hearsay testimony is accepted in the Hanafi school and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is valid in six matters because reputation (shuhra) is treated as equivalent to direct observation to prevent hardship.

Testimony in Islamic law generally requires direct knowledge. However, the Hanafi school recognizes an exception based on widespread reputation (tasammua) for six specific matters: lineage, death, marriage, consummation, judgeship, and the origin of an endowment. This lesson explains the legal reasoning: while qiyas would reject such testimony, istihsan (juristic preference) permits it due to necessity and the practical impossibility of direct knowledge in these matters.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the default rule
Identify that qiyas (analogy) rejects hearsay testimony because knowledge requires direct observation or mutawatir report.
2
Identify the exceptional matters
List the six matters: lineage, death, marriage, consummation, judgeship, and waqf origin.
3
Understand the basis of istihsan
Istihsan relies on the need to avoid hardship (haraj) and the fact that these matters are associated with widespread signs that create common knowledge.
4
Note the contrast with other transactions
Contracts like sale and lease are not exceptional because they are typically conducted in public and require direct witnesses.
5
Apply the rule to practical scenarios
See why matters like wala' and emancipation are not included (except Abu Yusuf's view).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقياس أن لا تجوز؛ لأنَّ الشهادة لا تجوز إلا بالعلم، ولا يتحقق العلم إلا بالمشاهدة والعيان أو بالخبر المتواتر، ولم يوجد ذلك، فصار كالبيع والإجارة، بل أولى؛ لأنَّ حكم المال أخف من حكم النكاح؛ ولهذا لا يجوز للقاضي أن يحكم بالتسامع، والحكم يجب بما تجب به الشهادة، ولهذا لو فسر للقاضي لا يقبله. ووجه الاستحسان: إنَّ هذه الأمور تختص بمعاينة أسبابها خواص من الناس، ويتعلق بها أحكام تبقى على انقضاء القرون، وانقراض الأعصار، فلو لم تقبل فيها بالتسامع أدى إلى الحرج وتعطيل الأحكام؛ ولأنَّ الأسباب يقترن بها ما تشتهر به. فإنَّ النسب: يشتهر بالتهنئة وإبنسبة كلّ واحدٍ إلى آخر عند المخاطبات، والمنادات، والموت بالتعزية، وقسمة التركات، واندراس الآثار، والنكاح بالشهود، والولائم، والدخول: يتعلق أحكام مشهورة من النسب، والمهر، والعدة، وثبوتِ الإحصان، والقضاء: بقراءة المنشور، واختلافُ الخصوم إليه، وازدحامهم عليه، فنزلت الشهرة منزلة العيان، فلا يشترط فيها المشاهدة. بخلافِ البيع والهبة والإجارة وأمثالها؛ لأنها لا تختص بشهادةِ أسبابها خواص من الناس، بل بحضرة الخاص والعام، وبه جرت العادة. ولأنَّ الناس قاطبةً مجمعون على أنهم يشهدون بهذه الأشياء بالشهرة، ألا ترى أنا نشهدُ أنَّ علياً تزوّج فاطمة رضي الله عنها ودخل بها، وشريحاً له كان قاضياً، وعمر بن الخطاب له تزوج بنت علي له، ولو تعلقت بحقيقة علم النسب أدّى إلى عدم الشهادة بها أصلاً؛ لأنَّ سببَ النَّسب العلوق، ولا علم للبشر فيه، وسبب القضاء والتولية ما لا يحضره إلا الوزير وأمثاله، وكذا الدخول لا يعرفه إلا الزوجان، فاكتفى في الكل بالدليل الظاهر. ثمَّ إنّما يجوز له أن يشهد بهذه بالتواتر، وبإخبار من يثق به، وإذا رأى امرأةً يدخل بها رجل وينبسطان انبساط الأزواج، وسمعَ من الناس أنها زوجته جاز له أن يشهد به، وإن لم يعاين عقد النكاح، وكذا شخصاً إذا رأى جالساً مجلس القضاء يفصل، جاز له أن يشهد أنه قاض بكذا قالوا، وقال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد: لا تقبل الشهادة بالتسامع في الدخول؛ لأنه ما يعاين، كما في الشهادة على الزنا. كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها تعريفها ونصابها وما يتحمله الشاهد إلا في النسب، والموت، والنكاح والدخول، وولاية القضاء القاضي، وأصل الوقف إذا أخبره به عدلان أو رجل وامرأتان (۱) وقيل: إن الزنا فاحشة، فلا يحتالُ في إثباتها بخلاف الدخول(۲)، ذكره العلامة الشُّمُنِي. [١] قوله: إلا في النسب....الخ؛ قصر الاستثناء على هذه الأشياء ينفي اعتبار التسامع في الولاء، وعن أبي يوسف: إنّه يجوز؛ لأنه بمنزلة النسب؛ لقوله: «الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب (۳)، فلو لم يجر بالتسامع لتعطلت الأحكام. ولهما: إنَّ العتق يبتني على زوال الملك، ولا بد فيه من المعاينة، فكذا ما يبتني عليه، وذكر شمس الأئمة السَّرَخْسِي: إنَّ الشهادة بالعتق لا تقبل بالإجماع. وذكر الحَلْوَانِيُّ: إِنَّ الخلاف ثابت فيه أيضاً، ثم ينبغي أن لا يفسر أنه يشهد بالتسامع، فلو فسر لا يقبله كمعاينة شيء في يد إنسان يطلق له الشهادة، فإذا فسَّرَ لا تقبل، كذا في «التبيين»، وغيره. (۳) قوله: إذا أخبر به؛ ليحصل له نوع علم، وهذا يدلُّ على أن لفظة الشهادة ليست بشرط في الكل، أما الذي يشهد عند القاضي فلا بُدَّ له من لفظة الشهادة. لكن قال العلامة الأكمل في «العناية»: يشترط أن يكون الإخبار بلفظ الشهادة على ما قالوا؛ لأنها توجب زيادة علم شرعاً لا يوجبها لفظ الخبر. انتهى. وقال الزَّيْلَعِي في «شرح الكنز»: ويشترط [في] الإخبار لفظ الشهادة في غير الموت، وفي الموت لا يشترط؛ لأنه لا يشترط فيه العدد، فكذا لفظ الشهادة لا يشترط. انتهى. (٤) قوله: عدلان أو رجل وامرأتان؛ وقيل: يكفي في الموت أن يخبره واحد
The analogy (qiyas) would dictate that it is not permissible, because testimony is only permissible based on knowledge, and knowledge is only achieved through direct observation or mutawatir report, and that is not present here, so it would be like sale and lease—rather even more so, because the ruling concerning property is lighter than the ruling concerning marriage. For this reason, a judge may not rule based on hearsay, and a ruling must be based on what testimony is required for, and therefore if he explains to the judge, he does not accept it. The basis of istihsan: these matters are such that only specific people observe their causes, and rulings related to them persist over generations and centuries, so if hearsay were not accepted in them, it would lead to hardship and suspension of rulings; also, these causes are associated with things that make them well-known. So lineage is known by congratulations and by one being attributed to another in addresses and calls, death by condolences, division of estates, and obliteration of traces, marriage by witnesses and feasts, consummation is associated with well-known rulings like lineage, dower, 'iddah, and establishing ihsan, judgeship by reading the appointment document, the parties coming to him, and crowding around him. Thus, widespread reputation is treated as equivalent to direct sight, so direct observation is not required. Contrary to sale, gift, lease, and the like, because their causes are not observed only by specific people, but rather in the presence of both specific and general public, and custom has so proceeded. And because all people are unanimous that they testify to these things based on reputation—do you not see that we testify that 'Ali married Fatima (may Allah be pleased with them) and consummated with her, that Shurayh was a judge, and that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab married 'Ali's daughter? If testimony were tied to the actual knowledge of lineage, it would lead to no testimony at all, because the cause of lineage is the conception, which humans have no knowledge of, and the cause of judgeship and appointment is not witnessed except by the minister and his likes, and similarly consummation is not known except by the spouses. So they sufficed in all with the apparent evidence. Then, he may testify to these based on tawatur or by informing from someone he trusts, and if he sees a woman entered by a man and they are comfortable as spouses, and hears from people that she is his wife, it is permissible for him to testify to that, even if he did not witness the marriage contract. Similarly, if he sees a person sitting in the judge's seat rendering decisions, it is permissible for him to testify that he is a judge. And al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad said: testimony based on hearsay is not accepted regarding consummation, because it is not directly observed, as in testimony for adultery. Book of Testimony and Retraction: its definition, its minimum number, and what the witness bears. Except in lineage, death, marriage, consummation, the office of the judge, and the origin of the endowment if two just men or one man and two women inform him. (1) It was said: indeed zina is an abomination, so it is not to be circumvented in establishing it, unlike consummation (2), mentioned by al-'Allama al-Shumunni. [1] His statement: 'except in lineage...etc.' confines the exception to these matters, negating the consideration of hearsay in wala'. From Abu Yusuf: it is permissible, because it is like lineage, due to his saying: 'Wala' is a relationship like that of lineage' (3), so if hearsay were not accepted, rulings would be suspended. For them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): indeed emancipation is based on the removal of ownership, and requires direct observation, so too what is based on it. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned: testimony for emancipation is not accepted by consensus. Al-Halwani mentioned: the difference of opinion is also established there, then he should not explain that he testifies based on hearsay; if he explains, it is not accepted, like seeing something in someone's hand that allows testimony; if he explains, it is not accepted. Thus in al-Tabyin and others. (3) His statement: 'if he informs him' to obtain some knowledge, and this indicates that the word 'shahadah' is not a condition in all cases. As for the one who testifies before the judge, he must use the word 'shahadah'. But al-'Allama al-Akmal said in al-'Inayah: it is a condition that the informing be with the word 'shahadah' according to what they said, because it creates additional knowledge legally that the word 'khabar' does not. End. Al-Zayla'i said in Sharh al-Kanz: the word 'shahadah' is required in the informing except for death, where it is not required, because the number is not required there, so likewise the word 'shahadah' is not required. End. (4) His statement: 'two just men or one man and two women'; and it is said: in death, it suffices that one person informs him.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion of the ruling on testimony based on hearsay (shahada bil tasammua) within the Hanafi school. It begins by stating the qiyas (analogy) that would reject such testimony because it lacks direct knowledge, as in contracts like sale and lease. However, the Hanafi school accepts it through istihsan (juristic preference) due to necessity: matters like lineage, death, marriage, consummation, judgeship, and the origin of waqf are often only known through widespread reputation because their causes are not directly observable by everyone. The text explains that these matters have associated signs and practices that make them well-known—like congratulations for lineage, condolences for death, feasts for marriage, etc.—so reputation is treated as equivalent to direct observation. The Hanafi position is contrasted with that of al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, who only accept hearsay in lineage, death, and marriage? Actually they accept in the same except? The text says they reject hearsay in consummation but accept in other things? The text says 'لا تقبل الشهادة بالتسامع في الدخول' meaning they reject in consummation. So the dispute is specifically about consummation. Later, the commentary addresses subsidiary issues: whether hearsay is accepted in wala' (clientage) and emancipation (there is a difference between Abu Yusuf and the others), and the conditions for the informants (two just men or one man and two women for waqf, and for death one person suffices according to some). The passage also discusses whether the word 'shahadah' must be used when informing; the Hanafi position is that it is not necessary outside court, but when testifying in court, the lafz is needed. The overall ruling is that hearsay testimony is a valid exception in the specific matters listed, based on the principle of removing hardship.

Key Terms
التسامع (al-tasāmmu’): Testimony based on widespread reputation or hearsay, where the witness does not have direct knowledge but relies on common knowledge and continuous reports.
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to necessity, custom, or public interest.
الشهرة (al-shuhra): Widespread reputation or custom that is treated as evidence in the absence of direct knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis (dalil) for accepting hearsay testimony in the six matters?
A) Qiyas on sale contracts.
B) Istihsan to avoid hardship.
C) A direct Quranic verse.
D) Ijma of all madhahib.

Key Takeaway
Hearsay testimony is accepted in Hanafi fiqh for six specific matters due to istihsan, overriding qiyas.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
7 min
The Hanafi Position on Hearsay Testimony for Consummation (Dukhul)
Inter-madhhab dispute on hearsay testimony for consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts hearsay testimony for consummation while the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools do not.

Core Idea
Consummation is lawful and its effects must be established, unlike zina which is a sin requiring strict proof; thus hearsay suffices.

While the Hanafi school accepts hearsay testimony for consummation (dukhul) as part of the six exceptions, the other three major schools reject it. This lesson dives into the specific dispute: the opponents analogize consummation to zina, which also occurs in private, but the Hanafi school distinguishes based on the nature of the act—zina is a sin (fahisha) requiring strict evidence to avoid scandal, while consummation is lawful and its consequences (lineage, mahr, iddah, ihsan) must be provable to avoid hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of disagreement
The Hanafi school includes dukhul in the six matters; the other schools exclude it.
2
State the opponent's proof
They analogize to zina: both are private acts, so hearsay is insufficient.
3
Analyze the Hanafi distinction
The passage states that zina is a fahisha, so strict proof is needed; dukhul is lawful and necessary for practical rulings.
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah)
Hanafis can prove consummation through reputation; others need direct witnesses, which is almost impossible.
5
Consider the reliance on istihsan
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to override qiyas due to hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقياس أن لا تجوز؛ لأنَّ الشهادة لا تجوز إلا بالعلم، ولا يتحقق العلم إلا بالمشاهدة والعيان أو بالخبر المتواتر، ولم يوجد ذلك، فصار كالبيع والإجارة، بل أولى؛ لأنَّ حكم المال أخف من حكم النكاح؛ ولهذا لا يجوز للقاضي أن يحكم بالتسامع، والحكم يجب بما تجب به الشهادة، ولهذا لو فسر للقاضي لا يقبله. ووجه الاستحسان: إنَّ هذه الأمور تختص بمعاينة أسبابها خواص من الناس، ويتعلق بها أحكام تبقى على انقضاء القرون، وانقراض الأعصار، فلو لم تقبل فيها بالتسامع أدى إلى الحرج وتعطيل الأحكام؛ ولأنَّ الأسباب يقترن بها ما تشتهر به. فإنَّ النسب: يشتهر بالتهنئة وإبنسبة كلّ واحدٍ إلى آخر عند المخاطبات، والمنادات، والموت بالتعزية، وقسمة التركات، واندراس الآثار، والنكاح بالشهود، والولائم، والدخول: يتعلق أحكام مشهورة من النسب، والمهر، والعدة، وثبوتِ الإحصان، والقضاء: بقراءة المنشور، واختلافُ الخصوم إليه، وازدحامهم عليه، فنزلت الشهرة منزلة العيان، فلا يشترط فيها المشاهدة. بخلافِ البيع والهبة والإجارة وأمثالها؛ لأنها لا تختص بشهادةِ أسبابها خواص من الناس، بل بحضرة الخاص والعام، وبه جرت العادة. ولأنَّ الناس قاطبةً مجمعون على أنهم يشهدون بهذه الأشياء بالشهرة، ألا ترى أنا نشهدُ أنَّ علياً تزوّج فاطمة رضي الله عنها ودخل بها، وشريحاً له كان قاضياً، وعمر بن الخطاب له تزوج بنت علي له، ولو تعلقت بحقيقة علم النسب أدّى إلى عدم الشهادة بها أصلاً؛ لأنَّ سببَ النَّسب العلوق، ولا علم للبشر فيه، وسبب القضاء والتولية ما لا يحضره إلا الوزير وأمثاله، وكذا الدخول لا يعرفه إلا الزوجان، فاكتفى في الكل بالدليل الظاهر. ثمَّ إنّما يجوز له أن يشهد بهذه بالتواتر، وبإخبار من يثق به، وإذا رأى امرأةً يدخل بها رجل وينبسطان انبساط الأزواج، وسمعَ من الناس أنها زوجته جاز له أن يشهد به، وإن لم يعاين عقد النكاح، وكذا شخصاً إذا رأى جالساً مجلس القضاء يفصل، جاز له أن يشهد أنه قاض بكذا قالوا، وقال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد: لا تقبل الشهادة بالتسامع في الدخول؛ لأنه ما يعاين، كما في الشهادة على الزنا. كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها تعريفها ونصابها وما يتحمله الشاهد إلا في النسب، والموت، والنكاح والدخول، وولاية القضاء القاضي، وأصل الوقف إذا أخبره به عدلان أو رجل وامرأتان (۱) وقيل: إن الزنا فاحشة، فلا يحتالُ في إثباتها بخلاف الدخول(۲)، ذكره العلامة الشُّمُنِي. Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion of the ruling on testimony based on hearsay (shahada bil tasammua) within the Hanafi school. It begins by stating the qiyas (analogy) that would reject such testimony because it lacks direct knowledge, as in contracts like sale and lease. The Hanafi position is contrasted with that of al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, who only accept hearsay in lineage, death, and marriage? Actually they accept in the same except? The text says they reject hearsay in consummation but accept in other things? The text says 'لا تقبل الشهادة بالتسامع في الدخول' meaning they reject in consummation. So the dispute is specifically about consummation. Later, the commentary addresses subsidiary issues: whether hearsay is accepted in wala' (clientage) and emancipation (there is a difference between Abu Yusuf and the others), and the conditions for the informants (two just men or one man and two women for waqf, and for death one person suffices according to some). The passage also discusses whether the word 'shahadah' must be used when informing; the Hanafi position is that it is not necessary outside court, but when testifying in court, the lafz is needed. The overall ruling is that hearsay testimony is a valid exception in the specific matters listed, based on the principle of removing hardship.

Key Terms
التسامع (al-tasāmmu’): Testimony based on widespread reputation or hearsay.
الدخول (al-dukhūl): Consummation of marriage.
الفاحشة (al-fāḥisha): Abomination, specifically zina.

Key Takeaway

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Hearsay for Wala' and Emancipation, and Conditions for Informing
Intra-Hanafi dispute and procedural details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the position of Abu Yusuf on hearsay testimony for wala' and explain why the majority rejects it, and state the conditions for informing (number of witnesses and lafz al-shahada).

Core Idea
Wala' is like lineage to Abu Yusuf but not to the majority; hearsay for emancipation is even more contested, and the informant must use the word 'shahadah' except in death.

The passage also addresses subsidiary issues: whether hearsay testimony is accepted for wala' (clientage) and emancipation. Abu Yusuf analogized wala' to lineage, but most Hanafi scholars require direct evidence. Additionally, the conditions for the informant are discussed: the number required and whether the word 'shahadah' must be used. This lesson unpacks these intra-madhhab differences and procedural details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception list
The six matters are exclusive; wala' and emancipation are not included.
2
Abu Yusuf's argument for wala'
He cites the hadith 'al-wala'u luhmatun ka-luhmati al-nasab' and fears suspension of rulings.
3
Majority's response
Emancipation requires proof of removal of ownership, which cannot be based on hearsay.
4
Sarakhsi vs Halwani on emancipation
Sarakhsi claims consensus, Halwani says ikhtilaf remains.
5
Procedural conditions
For waqf, two just men or one man and two women; for death, one person suffices. The word 'shahadah' is required in court but not necessarily outside.

والقياس أن لا تجوز؛ لأنَّ الشهادة لا تجوز إلا بالعلم، ولا يتحقق العلم إلا بالمشاهدة والعيان أو بالخبر المتواتر، ولم يوجد ذلك، فصار كالبيع والإجارة، بل أولى؛ لأنَّ حكم المال أخف من حكم النكاح؛ ولهذا لا يجوز للقاضي أن يحكم بالتسامع، والحكم يجب بما تجب به الشهادة، ولهذا لو فسر للقاضي لا يقبله. ووجه الاستحسان: إنَّ هذه الأمور تختص بمعاينة أسبابها خواص من الناس، ويتعلق بها أحكام تبقى على انقضاء القرون، وانقراض الأعصار، فلو لم تقبل فيها بالتسامع أدى إلى الحرج وتعطيل الأحكام؛ ولأنَّ الأسباب يقترن بها ما تشتهر به. فإنَّ النسب: يشتهر بالتهنئة وإبنسبة كلّ واحدٍ إلى آخر عند المخاطبات، والمنادات، والموت بالتعزية، وقسمة التركات، واندراس الآثار، والنكاح بالشهود، والولائم، والدخول: يتعلق أحكام مشهورة من النسب، والمهر، والعدة، وثبوتِ الإحصان، والقضاء: بقراءة المنشور، واختلافُ الخصوم إليه، وازدحامهم عليه، فنزلت الشهرة منزلة العيان، فلا يشترط فيها المشاهدة. بخلافِ البيع والهبة والإجارة وأمثالها؛ لأنها لا تختص بشهادةِ أسبابها خواص من الناس، بل بحضرة الخاص والعام، وبه جرت العادة. ولأنَّ الناس قاطبةً مجمعون على أنهم يشهدون بهذه الأشياء بالشهرة، ألا ترى أنا نشهدُ أنَّ علياً تزوّج فاطمة رضي الله عنها ودخل بها، وشريحاً له كان قاضياً، وعمر بن الخطاب له تزوج بنت علي له، ولو تعلقت بحقيقة علم النسب أدّى إلى عدم الشهادة بها أصلاً؛ لأنَّ سببَ النَّسب العلوق، ولا علم للبشر فيه، وسبب القضاء والتولية ما لا يحضره إلا الوزير وأمثاله، وكذا الدخول لا يعرفه إلا الزوجان، فاكتفى في الكل بالدليل الظاهر. ثمَّ إنّما يجوز له أن يشهد بهذه بالتواتر، وبإخبار من يثق به، وإذا رأى امرأةً يدخل بها رجل وينبسطان انبساط الأزواج، وسمعَ من الناس أنها زوجته جاز له أن يشهد به، وإن لم يعاين عقد النكاح، وكذا شخصاً إذا رأى جالساً مجلس القضاء يفصل، جاز له أن يشهد أنه قاض بكذا قالوا، وقال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد: لا تقبل الشهادة بالتسامع في الدخول؛ لأنه ما يعاين، كما في الشهادة على الزنا. كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها تعريفها ونصابها وما يتحمله الشاهد إلا في النسب، والموت، والنكاح والدخول، وولاية القضاء القاضي، وأصل الوقف إذا أخبره به عدلان أو رجل وامرأتان (۱) وقيل: إن الزنا فاحشة، فلا يحتالُ في إثباتها بخلاف الدخول(۲)، ذكره العلامة الشُّمُنِي. [١] قوله: إلا في النسب....الخ؛ قصر الاستثناء على هذه الأشياء ينفي اعتبار التسامع في الولاء، وعن أبي يوسف: إنّه يجوز؛ لأنه بمنزلة النسب؛ لقوله: «الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب (۳)، فلو لم يجر بالتسامع لتعطلت الأحكام. ولهما: إنَّ العتق يبتني على زوال الملك، ولا بد فيه من المعاينة، فكذا ما يبتني عليه، وذكر شمس الأئمة السَّرَخْسِي: إنَّ الشهادة بالعتق لا تقبل بالإجماع. وذكر الحَلْوَانِيُّ: إِنَّ الخلاف ثابت فيه أيضاً، ثم ينبغي أن لا يفسر أنه يشهد بالتسامع، فلو فسر لا يقبله كمعاينة شيء في يد إنسان يطلق له الشهادة، فإذا فسَّرَ لا تقبل، كذا في «التبيين»، وغيره. (۳) قوله: إذا أخبر به؛ ليحصل له نوع علم، وهذا يدلُّ على أن لفظة الشهادة ليست بشرط في الكل، أما الذي يشهد عند القاضي فلا بُدَّ له من لفظة الشهادة. لكن قال العلامة الأكمل في «العناية»: يشترط أن يكون الإخبار بلفظ الشهادة على ما قالوا؛ لأنها توجب زيادة علم شرعاً لا يوجبها لفظ الخبر. انتهى. وقال الزَّيْلَعِي في «شرح الكنز»: ويشترط [في] الإخبار لفظ الشهادة في غير الموت، وفي الموت لا يشترط؛ لأنه لا يشترط فيه العدد، فكذا لفظ الشهادة لا يشترط. انتهى. (٤) قوله: عدلان أو رجل وامرأتان؛ وقيل: يكفي في الموت أن يخبره واحد
The analogy (qiyas) would dictate that it is not permissible, because testimony is only permissible based on knowledge, and knowledge is only achieved through direct observation or mutawatir report, and that is not present here, so it would be like sale and lease—rather even more so, because the ruling concerning property is lighter than the ruling concerning marriage. For this reason, a judge may not rule based on hearsay, and a ruling must be based on what testimony is required for, and therefore if he explains to the judge, he does not accept it. The basis of istihsan: these matters are such that only specific people observe their causes, and rulings related to them persist over generations and centuries, so if hearsay were not accepted in them, it would lead to hardship and suspension of rulings; also, these causes are associated with things that make them well-known. So lineage is known by congratulations and by one being attributed to another in addresses and calls, death by condolences, division of estates, and obliteration of traces, marriage by witnesses and feasts, consummation is associated with well-known rulings like lineage, dower, 'iddah, and establishing ihsan, judgeship by reading the appointment document, the parties coming to him, and crowding around him. Thus, widespread reputation is treated as equivalent to direct sight, so direct observation is not required. Contrary to sale, gift, lease, and the like, because their causes are not observed only by specific people, but rather in the presence of both specific and general public, and custom has so proceeded. And because all people are unanimous that they testify to these things based on reputation—do you not see that we testify that 'Ali married Fatima (may Allah be pleased with them) and consummated with her, that Shurayh was a judge, and that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab married 'Ali's daughter? If testimony were tied to the actual knowledge of lineage, it would lead to no testimony at all, because the cause of lineage is the conception, which humans have no knowledge of, and the cause of judgeship and appointment is not witnessed except by the minister and his likes, and similarly consummation is not known except by the spouses. So they sufficed in all with the apparent evidence. Then, he may testify to these based on tawatur or by informing from someone he trusts, and if he sees a woman entered by a man and they are comfortable as spouses, and hears from people that she is his wife, it is permissible for him to testify to that, even if he did not witness the marriage contract. Similarly, if he sees a person sitting in the judge's seat rendering decisions, it is permissible for him to testify that he is a judge. And al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad said: testimony based on hearsay is not accepted regarding consummation, because it is not directly observed, as in testimony for adultery. Book of Testimony and Retraction: its definition, its minimum number, and what the witness bears. Except in lineage, death, marriage, consummation, the office of the judge, and the origin of the endowment if two just men or one man and two women inform him. (1) It was said: indeed zina is an abomination, so it is not to be circumvented in establishing it, unlike consummation (2), mentioned by al-'Allama al-Shumunni. [1] His statement: 'except in lineage...etc.' confines the exception to these matters, negating the consideration of hearsay in wala'. From Abu Yusuf: it is permissible, because it is like lineage, due to his saying: 'Wala' is a relationship like that of lineage' (3), so if hearsay were not accepted, rulings would be suspended. For them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): indeed emancipation is based on the removal of ownership, and requires direct observation, so too what is based on it. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned: testimony for emancipation is not accepted by consensus. Al-Halwani mentioned: the difference of opinion is also established there, then he should not explain that he testifies based on hearsay; if he explains, it is not accepted, like seeing something in someone's hand that allows testimony; if he explains, it is not accepted. Thus in al-Tabyin and others. (3) His statement: 'if he informs him' to obtain some knowledge, and this indicates that the word 'shahadah' is not a condition in all cases. As for the one who testifies before the judge, he must use the word 'shahadah'. But al-'Allama al-Akmal said in al-'Inayah: it is a condition that the informing be with the word 'shahadah' according to what they said, because it creates additional knowledge legally that the word 'khabar' does not. End. Al-Zayla'i said in Sharh al-Kanz: the word 'shahadah' is required in the informing except for death, where it is not required, because the number is not required there, so likewise the word 'shahadah' is not required. End. (4) His statement: 'two just men or one man and two women'; and it is said: in death, it suffices that one person informs him.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion of the ruling on testimony based on hearsay (shahada bil tasammua) within the Hanafi school. It begins by stating the qiyas (analogy) that would reject such testimony because it lacks direct knowledge, as in contracts like sale and lease. However, the Hanafi school accepts it through istihsan (juristic preference) due to necessity: matters like lineage, death, marriage, consummation, judgeship, and the origin of waqf are often only known through widespread reputation because their causes are not directly observable by everyone. The text explains that these matters have associated signs and practices that make them well-known—like congratulations for lineage, condolences for death, feasts for marriage, etc.—so reputation is treated as equivalent to direct observation. The Hanafi position is contrasted with that of al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, who only accept hearsay in lineage, death, and marriage? Actually they accept in the same except? The text says they reject hearsay in consummation but accept in other things? The text says 'لا تقبل الشهادة بالتسامع في الدخول' meaning they reject in consummation. So the dispute is specifically about consummation. Later, the commentary addresses subsidiary issues: whether hearsay is accepted in wala' (clientage) and emancipation (there is a difference between Abu Yusuf and the others), and the conditions for the informants (two just men or one man and two women for waqf, and for death one person suffices according to some). The passage also discusses whether the word 'shahadah' must be used when informing; the Hanafi position is that it is not necessary outside court, but when testifying in court, the lafz is needed. The overall ruling is that hearsay testimony is a valid exception in the specific matters listed, based on the principle of removing hardship.

Key Terms
الولاء (al-walā’): Clientage, the relationship between a freed slave and the emancipator, which entails inheritance rights.
العتق (al-‘itq): Emancipation of a slave.
لفظة الشهادة (lafẓat al-shahāda): The word 'ashhadu' (I testify) used when giving testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sarakhsi, what is the ruling on hearsay testimony for emancipation?
A) Accepted by consensus.
B) Rejected by consensus.
C) There is ikhtilaf.
D) Only Abu Yusuf accepts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits hearsay testimony to six specific matters; wala' and emancipation are not included by the majority, and conditions for informants vary.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
The Six Exceptions: Hearsay Testimony in Hanafi Law
Explaining exceptions to the requirement of direct eyewitness testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six exceptions to the requirement of direct testimony in Hanafi law, explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding clientage, and apply the conditions required for hearsay testimony.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is accepted in six specific matters due to necessity, but each exception has its own conditions and intra-madhhab variations.

In Islamic court proceedings, testimony is generally required to be based on direct eyewitness observation. However, certain matters such as lineage, death, and marriage are often impossible to witness directly by multiple people. The Hanafi school, recognizing this difficulty, allows hearsay testimony (الشهادة بالتسامع) in six specific cases as a relaxation (rukhsah). This lesson examines the passage from the book of testimony that delineates these exceptions, the conditions attached to them, and the internal scholarly differences within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six exceptions
From the matn, list the six matters where hearsay testimony is permitted: lineage, death, marriage, entering (consummation), jurisdiction of a judge, and original endowment.
2
Examine the scope of the exceptions
Note that clientage (الولاء) is deliberately excluded by the Sahibayn, despite Abu Yusuf's opposing view. Understand the reasoning: emancipation requires eyewitness to removal of ownership.
The hadith 'الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب' is cited but considered insufficient by the majority.
3
Analyze the conditions on the informant
The passage specifies that the informant must be two just men or one man and two women, except for death where one just person may suffice. Also, the wording of testimony is required for court witnesses, but for mere informants it is not necessary except by some opinions.
For death, al-Zayla'i and al-Fath relax both number and wording due to hardship.
4
Distinguish Imam Abu Hanifa's stricter position
Imam Abu Hanifa requires that the hearsay be so widespread that it settles in the heart (tawatur), effectively requiring mass transmission. The matn follows the Sahibayn's more lenient position.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
The passage provides examples: seeing a judge in session, seeing a couple living together, and seeing possession of property. These are not hearsay but circumstantial evidence used to testify to underlying facts.
These examples demonstrate the Hanafi reliance on customary signs (qarā'in) in evidentiary law.

كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها تعريفها ونصابها وما يتحمله الشاهد
إلا في النسب، والموت، والنكاح والدخول، وولاية القضاء القاضي، وأصل الوقف إذا أخبره به عدلان أو رجل وامرأتان
وقلنا : إن الزنا فاحشة، فلا يحتالُ في إثباتها بخلاف الدخول، ذكره العلامة الشُّمُنِي. قوله : إلا في النسب....الخ ؛ قصر الاستثناء على هذه الأشياء ينفي اعتبار التسامع في الولاء، وعن أبي يوسف : إنّه يجوز؛ لأنه بمنزلة النسب ؛ لقوله : «الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب»، فلو لم يجر بالتسامع لتعطلت الأحكام. ولهما : إنَّ العتق يبتني على زوال الملك ، ولا بد فيه من المعاينة، فكذا ما يبتني عليه، وذكر شمس الأئمة السَّرَخْسِي له : إنَّ الشهادة بالعتق لا تقبل بالإجماع. وذكر الحَلْوَانِيُّ : إِنَّ الخلاف ثابت فيه أيضاً ، ثم ينبغي أن لا يفسر أنه يشهد بالتسامع، فلو فسر لا يقبله كمعاينة شيء في يد إنسان يطلق له الشهادة ، فإذا فسَّرَ لا تقبل، كذا في «التبيين» ، وغيره. قوله : إذا أخبر به ؛ ليحصل له نوع علم، وهذا يدلُّ على أن لفظة الشهادة ليست بشرط في الكل، أما الذي يشهد عند القاضي فلا بُدَّ له من لفظة الشهادة. لكن قال العلامة الأكمل في «العناية» : يشترط أن يكون الإخبار بلفظ الشهادة على ما قالوا ؛ لأنها توجب زيادة علم شرعاً لا يوجبها لفظ الخبر. انتهى. وقال الزَّيْلَعِي في «شرح الكنز» : ويشترط [في] الإخبار لفظ الشهادة في غير الموت، وفي الموت لا يشترط ؛ لأنه لا يشترط فيه العدد، فكذا لفظ الشهادة لا يشترط. انتهى. قوله : عدلان أو رجل وامرأتان ؛ وقيل : يكفي في الموت أن يخبره واحد عدل، أو واحدة ؛ لأن الموت قد يتفق في موضع لا يحضره إلا واحد، وإذا وقع في موضع يحضره قوم فقلما يشاهده واحد، فاشتراط العدد فيه يؤدي إلى بعض الحرج ، وصحح في الظهيرية»: إن الموت كغيره. وقال في «الفتح»: المختار الاكتفاء بالواحد في الموت، والعدالة إنما تشترط في المخبر في غير المتواتر، أما في المتواتر فلا يشترط العدالة، ولا لفظ الشهادة. كما في «الخلاصة»، واعلم أنَّ قول المتن على طبق ما قال الصاحبان، أما عند الإمام فلا تجوز الشهادة ما لم يسمع ذلك من العامة بحيث يقع في قلبه صدق الخبر.
قوله : فبيان المصرف.. الخ ؛ ذكر المرغيناني له : إنه لا بُدَّ من بيان الجهة بأن يشهدوا أنه وقف على هذا المسجد أو الفقر أو ما أشبهه ، حتى لو لم يذكروا في شهادتهم الجهة لا تقبل شهادتهم. قوله : ويشهد...الخ ؛ يعني مَن رأى شخصاً جالساً مجلس القضاء يدخل عليه الخصوم جاز له أن يشهد أن ذلك الشخص قاض، وإن لم يعاين تقليد الإمام إياه ، وكذا من رأى رجلاً وامرأة يسكنان معاً في بيت وبينهما انبساط الأزواج جاز له أن يشهد على أنها زوجة ذلك الرجل وإن لم يعاين عقد النكاح. وقيل : لا بد من الإخبار بأنها زوجته وكذا من رأى شيئاً سوى الآدمي في يدِ رجل يتصرف فيه تصرُّف الملاك جاز له أن يشهد أنَّ ذلك الشيء للرَّجل المتصرف وإن لم يعاين أسباب الملك ؛ لأنَّ اليد أقصى ما يستدل به على الملك، إذ هي مرجع الدلالة في الأسباب كلّها فيكتفي بها، وعن أبي يوسف له : إنه يشترط مع ذلك أن يقع في قلبه أنه له. كذا في «الهداية».
Book of testimony and retraction from it: its definition, its number (of witnesses), and what the witness bears. Except in lineage, death, marriage and entering, and the jurisdiction of a judge's judgment, and the original endowment, if two just men or one man and two women inform him of it. And we said: Fornication is an abomination, so there is no recourse to proving it by hearsay, unlike entering. Mentioned by Allama al-Shumunni. His saying: 'Except in lineage...etc.' confining the exception to these things negates considering hearsay in clientage. And from Abu Yusuf: it is permissible because it is like lineage due to his saying: 'Clientage is a bond like the bond of lineage.' So if it were not accepted by hearsay, rulings would become invalid. And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): indeed emancipation is based on the removal of ownership, and it requires eyewitness, so likewise what is based upon it. And Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned that testimony regarding emancipation is not accepted by consensus. And al-Halwani mentioned that disagreement also exists about it, then he should not explain that he testifies by hearsay; if he explains, it is not accepted. Like seeing something in the hand of a person that allows him to testify; if he explains, it is not accepted. As in 'al-Tabyin' and others. His saying: 'When he is informed by him' so that he obtains some knowledge. This indicates that the wording of testimony is not a condition in all cases. As for one who testifies before a judge, the wording of testimony is necessary for him. But Allama al-Akmal said in 'al-Inaya': it is a condition that the information be with the wording of testimony, as they said, because it brings about an increase of knowledge legally that the wording of news does not. End quote. And al-Zayla'i said in 'Sharh al-Kanz': wording of testimony is required for information in other than death, but in death it is not required because number is not required in it, so likewise wording of testimony is not required. End quote. His saying: 'Two just men or one man and two women' and it is said: it suffices in death that one just man or one woman inform him, because death may occur in a place where only one is present, and if it occurs in a place where people are present, rarely does one witness it alone, so stipulating number leads to hardship. And it was corrected in al-Zahiriyya that death is like others. And he said in 'al-Fath': the chosen is sufficiency of one in death, and justice is only required in the informant in non-mutawatir matters, but in mutawatir matters, neither justice nor the wording of testimony are required. As in 'al-Khulasa'. And know that the statement of the text is in accordance with what the two companions said; as for Imam Abu Hanifa, testimony is not valid unless he hears it from the public such that the truthfulness of the report settles in his heart. His saying: 'Explanation of the disbursement...etc.' al-Marghinani mentioned that it is necessary to specify the destination by witnessing that it is an endowment for this mosque or the poor or similar, so if they do not mention the destination in their testimony, their testimony is not accepted. His saying: 'And one testifies...etc.' means whoever saw a person sitting in the judge's seat with litigants entering upon him, it is permissible for him to testify that that person is a judge, even if he did not witness the caliph's appointment. Likewise, whoever saw a man and woman living together in a house with marital intimacy, it is permissible for him to testify that she is the wife of that man, even if he did not witness the marriage contract. And it is said: there must be a statement that she is his wife. Likewise, whoever saw something other than a human in the hand of a man who disposes of it as owners dispose, it is permissible for him to testify that that thing belongs to the disposing man, even if he did not witness the causes of ownership, because possession is the ultimate way to infer ownership, as it is the source of indication in all causes, so it suffices. And from Abu Yusuf: it is required with that that it settle in his heart that it is his. As in 'al-Hidaya'.
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage from the book of testimony discusses the exceptions to the general rule that testimony must be based on direct eyewitness observation. The matn states that hearsay testimony (الشهادة بالتسامع) is accepted in six specific matters: lineage (النسب), death (الموت), marriage (النكاح), entering (الدخول) which refers to marital consummation, the jurisdiction of a judge (ولاية القضاء القاضي), and the original endowment (أصل الوقف) when the witness is informed by two just men or one man and two women. The commentator expands on each exception.

The first point concerns the exclusion of other matters, such as clientage (الولاء). Imam Abu Yusuf holds that hearsay should also be accepted for clientage because a hadith equates it to lineage, but Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, reasoning that emancipation is based on removal of ownership which requires eyewitness. Al-Sarakhsi notes consensus against hearsay testimony for emancipation. Al-Halwani mentions there is disagreement, but any witness must not explain that they are testifying by hearsay.

Regarding the wording of testimony, the commentator clarifies that when testifying before a judge, the witness must use the specific wording of testimony (أشهد). However, for the exceptions listed, the informant who does not appear in court need not use that wording. Al-Zayla'i specifies that for death, even the wording of testimony is not required because the number of witnesses is also relaxed.

The number of witnesses required for the information is also discussed. For death, some say one just man or one woman suffices due to necessity and to avoid hardship, though the Zahiriyya considers death like other matters requiring two. The preferred view (al-mukhtar) in al-Fath is that one is sufficient for death.

Imam Abu Hanifa's position is stricter: he requires that the information be so widespread that it settles in the heart with certainty, effectively requiring tawatur. The matn's statement follows the Sahibayn's view.

The passage also covers witnessing a judge based on seeing him in the judge's seat with litigants, and witnessing a marriage based on seeing a couple living together with marital intimacy. Similarly, possession is sufficient to testify ownership unless one explains otherwise, according to Abu Yusuf. These rulings demonstrate the Hanafi approach of practical evidentiary inference based on common custom and necessity.

Key Terms
الشهادة بالتسامع (al-shahāda bi al-tasāmu‘): Testimony based on widespread hearsay rather than direct eyewitness observation.
الولاء (al-walā’): Clientage bond between a freed slave and the emancipator, considered analogous to lineage in some rulings.
العدلان (al-‘adlān): Two just witnesses whose testimony is acceptable in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which of the following matters is hearsay testimony (الشهادة بالتسامع) NOT permitted?
A) Lineage (النسب)
B) Clientage (الولاء)
C) Death (الموت)
D) Marriage (النكاح)

Key Takeaway
Hearsay testimony is accepted only in six specific matters, with conditions varying by matter and intra-madhhab differences mainly concerning clientage and the number of informants for death.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
Testimony Based on Outward Indications: Hearsay, Possession, and Inner Presumption
Explaining permissible testimony based on hearsay and possession with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for permissible testimony based on outward signs (tawatur, yad) and apply the requirement of inner presumption (zann) to the case of possession.

Core Idea
Testimony from outward signs is permissible, but mere possession is insufficient without an inner presumption of ownership.

In Islamic legal procedure, witnesses must testify from certain knowledge. However, the Hanafi school recognizes that absolute certainty is often impossible, so the law permits testimony based on widespread reports (tawatur) and dominant outward indications such as possession (yad). This passage from Umdat al-Riaya explains three such scenarios (judgeship, marriage, ownership) and delves into the conditions under which possession alone can ground testimony. A key nuance is the requirement that the witness have an inner presumption (zann) that the fact is true—a condition that distinguishes the Hanafi view from more lenient or stricter positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
State the three examples given where testimony based on outward signs is permitted: seeing a person in a judge's court with litigants (testify he is a judge), seeing a man and woman cohabiting with marital intimacy (testify she is his wife), and seeing a person in possession of an item and disposing of it like an owner (testify it is his). Note the outward indication that permits testimony in each.
These are applications of the principle of relying on dominant outward signs (al-ghalba).
2
Understand the death exception
The passage discusses the number of witnesses for death: the relied-upon view is that one witness suffices. This is because insisting on two would cause hardship (haraj) since death may occur in remote places where only one is present. Also, note that tawatur (widespread report) does not require the 'adala of the source, nor the wording of testimony.
The example of death illustrates the principle of raf' al-haraj.
3
Distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa requires that the witness hear the testimony from the general public such that the truthfulness settles in his heart. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow testimony based on possession alone, but with the condition that the witness have an inner presumption (zann) that it belongs to the possessor. The mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf resolved in favor of the Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the condition of inner presumption (zann)
The passage explains that even if the witness sees an item in someone's hand, if the circumstance (e.g., a precious pearl in a garbage collector's hand) does not produce a genuine presumption, he should not testify. Also, if two just witnesses inform him that it belongs to another, he cannot testify; if only one witness contradicts, he may continue unless his heart settles on the truthfulness of that single witness.
This shows that the condition is not merely possession but the subjective state of the witness's heart.
5
Compare with other schools
Al-Khassaf, al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad require both possession and disposition (tasarruf) as evidence of ownership. The Hanafi school (Sahibayn) does not require disposition; possession is sufficient if accompanied by inner presumption. Abu Hanifa and a narration from the Sahibayn also allow testimony for slaves based on possession alone.
Cross-madhhab difference: the practical consequence is that a Hanafi may testify based on possession alone, while a Shafi'i would not.

Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses when testimony is permissible based on outward indications rather than direct certainty. It begins with three examples where one can testify based on common observation: (1) seeing a person in a judge's court with litigants entering allows one to testify that he is a judge, even without seeing his appointment; (2) seeing a man and woman cohabiting with marital intimacy allows testimony that she is his wife, even without witnessing the marriage contract; (3) seeing a person in possession of an item and disposing of it like an owner allows testimony of ownership, even without witnessing the cause of ownership. The author then addresses the number of witnesses required for death: the relied-upon view (al-mukhtar) is that one witness suffices, due to hardship in obtaining multiple witnesses in remote places. The condition of 'adala (integrity) applies only to reporters of non-mutawatir news; in mutawatir (widespread) reports, neither 'adala nor the wording of testimony is required. The matn (text) follows the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), while Imam Abu Hanifa requires that the testimony be based on hearing from the public such that the heart is convinced of its truth. Regarding possession, the author explains that mere possession (al-yad) is not sufficient; one must also have a presumption (zann) in the heart that the item belongs to the possessor. This is attributed to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and some say it is the consensus of all three imams. The Hanafi position, however, is nuanced: if two just witnesses contradict the possession, testimony is not permissible; but one witness does not remove the presumption. The Hanafi school differs from Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali, who require both possession and disposition as evidence of ownership. According to Abu Hanifa and a narration from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, testimony about a slave is also permissible based on possession alone. The author of al-Hidaya and al-Kanz did not restrict the rule to non-slave items.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony in court; giving evidence based on knowledge, which in this context may be based on outward signs or hearsay when certainty is impossible.
تواتر (tawatur): A report transmitted by such a large number that it is impossible for them to have agreed upon a lie; it yields certainty and does not require the 'adala of each individual.
يد (yad): Possession; physical control over an item. In this context, it serves as the primary indicator (dalil) of ownership.
تصرف (tasarruf): Disposition; acting like an owner by using, selling, leasing, etc. Some scholars require this alongside yad for ownership testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view in this passage, what additional condition is required for a witness to testify about ownership based on possession (yad) of an item?
A) That the witness has seen the owner dispose of the item (tasarruf).
B) That the witness has heard from two just people that it belongs to the possessor.
C) That the witness has an inner presumption (zann) that the item belongs to the possessor.
D) That the witness has seen the purchase contract for the item.

Key Takeaway
When testifying from possession, Hanafi law requires not just outward possession but an inner presumption (zann) that ownership is genuine.
