Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Testimony from Heretical Sects: Hanafi Position and Proof
Ruling rejecting testimony of six heretical sects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on testimony from six major heretical sects and explain why their beliefs remove them from Ahl al-Qibla.

Core Idea
Incorrect creed invalidates testimony: a person is not a Muslim if they hold beliefs like Jabr or Qadr, so their witness is rejected.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah identifies six sects whose testimony is not accepted in Islamic courts. The Hanafi school classifies these sects as outside Ahl al-Qibla due to specific theological errors. Understanding this ruling requires recognizing that legal testimony (shahadah) depends not only on outward piety but also on correct belief ('aqidah). This lesson will unpack each sect's error and the proof used to exclude them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and subject
The passage rules that testimony is not accepted from those whose creed is not Ahl al-Sunnah. Identify the general rule: anyone from the listed sects is not a Muslim, so their testimony is rejected.
The ruling is not about individual sins but about fundamental beliefs that nullify Islam.
2
List the six main sects and their core beliefs
The text names six sects: Jabriyyah, Qadariyyah, Rawafid, Khawarij, Mu'attilah, Mushabbihah. For each, state the defining belief that causes their exclusion.
The passage gives a brief refutation for each, but the key is the belief itself.
3
Understand the criterion for being from Ahl al-Qibla
The passage states that even a lifetime of worship does not count if one holds beliefs like pre-eternity of the world, denial of resurrection, or denial of God's knowledge of particulars. These beliefs remove a person from Ahl al-Qibla.
Ahl al-Qibla are those who pray facing the Kaaba and are considered Muslims.
4
Apply the hadith of the seventy-three sects
The hadith states that all sects except one are in the Fire. The saved sect is the one following the Prophet and his Companions. The Hanafis identify the listed sects as among the 72 erring sects, thus outside the saved group.
This is the proof (dalil) for rejecting their testimony.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools might consider these sects as Muslims if they outwardly profess Islam. The Hanafis are strict: specific beliefs that contradict core tenets remove one from Islam entirely.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that the Hanafi position rejects their testimony, while others may accept it after repentance or if they are ignorant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها / باب القبول وعدمه
الذين لا يكون معتقدهم معتقد أهل السُنَّةِ، وهم الجبرية، والقدرية، والروافض، والخوارج، والمعطلة، والمشبهة، وكل منهم اثنا عشر فرقة، فصاروا اثنين وسبعين.
فمَن واظب طول عمره على الطاعات والعبادات مع اعتقادِ قدم العالم أو نفي الحشر أو نفي علمه سبحانه بالجزئيات لا يكون من أهل القبلة.
قوله: وهم الجبرية؛ وهم الذين قالوا: إن العبد مجبر لا قدرة له أصلاً لا خالقة ولا كاسبة، ويرد عليهم بطلان الثواب والعقاب.
والقدرية: وهم الذين قالوا: إن للعبد قدرة خالقة لأفعاله، ويرد عليهم قوله تعالى: وَاللهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ.
والروافض: وهم الذين رفضوا أكثر الصحابة، وأنكروا إمامة الشيخين، والمسح على الخفين، وسبوا معاوية وأحزابه.
والخوارج: وهم الذين خرجوا عن الطريقة السوية، وحاربوا مع علي، وشتموا أصهار رسول الله.
والمعطلة: وهم الذين قالوا: إن الله تعالى معطل، كما قال الحكماء: إنه صدر منه عقل أول، ثم صدر منه عقل ثان ثم وثم إلى أن صدر العقل العاشر وهو العقل الفعال، وعليه نظام العالم.
والمشبهة: وهم الذين شبهوا الله بالخلق، وأثبتوا له الجسمية، فغلاتهم على الجسم الصرف، وغير الغلاة قالوا: إنه جسم لا كالأجسام من دم ولحم لا كاللحوم.
وكل منهم اثنى عشر فرقة، صرح به في «الدر المختار»، و«منح الغفار»، و«التبيين»، و«الرمز»، وغيرها.
لكن قال البرجندي في «شرح النقاية»: كبار فرقهم سبع على ما في «المواقف»: المعتزلة: وهم عشرون صنفاً، والشيعة: وهم اثنان وعشرون صنفاً، والخوارج: وهم عشرون صنفاً، والمرجئة: وهم خمسة أصناف، والبخارية: وهم ثلاثة أصناف، والجبرية والمشبهة: وهما صنفان، ففرق أهل الأهواء اثنتان وسبعون. انتهى.
فصار الاثنين وسبعين فرقةً كلهم في النار، والفرقة الزائدة على هذا العدد هي الناجية، وهي من كانت على ما كان عليه رسول الله وأصحابه، ففي الحديث: ستفترقُ أمتي على ثلاثة وسبعين فرقة، كلها في النار، إلا ما كان على ما أنا عليه وأصحابي.
Book of Testimony and Retraction from It / Chapter on Acceptance and Non-acceptance. Those whose creed is not the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah: they are the Jabriyyah, Qadariyyah, Rawafid, Khawarij, Mu'attilah, and Mushabbihah, and each of them has twelve sects, so they become seventy-two. So whoever persists his entire life in acts of obedience and worship while believing in the pre-eternity of the world, or denial of the Resurrection, or denial of His knowledge, exalted be He, of particulars, is not from Ahl al-Qibla. His statement: 'and they are the Jabriyyah'; they are those who said that the servant is compelled, having no power at all, neither creative nor acquisitive, and the invalidation of reward and punishment is a refutation against them. The Qadariyyah: they are those who said that the servant has creative power over his actions, and the refutation against them is His statement, exalted: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' The Rawafid: they are those who rejected most of the Companions, denied the caliphate of the two shaykhs, and wiping over the leather socks, and insulted Mu'awiyah and his party. The Khawarij: they are those who departed from the straight path, fought with Ali, and reviled the in-laws of the Messenger of Allah. The Mu'attilah: they are those who said that Allah, exalted, is inactive, as the philosophers said: from Him emanated a first intellect, then from it emanated a second intellect, then so on until there emanated the tenth intellect, which is the active intellect, and upon it depends the system of the world. The Mushabbihah: they are those who likened Allah to creation and affirmed corporeality for Him; their extremists affirm pure body, and the moderates said: He is a body not like bodies, of blood and flesh not like flesh. And each of them has twelve sects, as stated in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Minah al-Ghaffar, al-Tibyan, al-Ramz, and others. However, al-Birjandi said in Sharh al-Nuqayah: their major sects are seven according to al-Mawaqif: the Mu'tazilah: twenty groups, the Shi'ah: twenty-two groups, the Khawarij: twenty groups, the Murji'ah: five groups, the Bakiriyyah: three groups, the Jabriyyah and Mushabbihah: two groups, so the sects of the people of desires are seventy-two. End. So they become seventy-two sects, all in the Fire, and the sect beyond this number is the saved one, and it is the one that was upon what the Messenger of Allah and his Companions were upon, for in the hadith: 'My nation will split into seventy-three sects, all in the Fire except the one that is upon what I and my Companions are upon.'
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement and expansion on the acceptance of testimony. It begins by listing the heretical sects whose testimony is not accepted: the Jabriyyah (fatalists who deny human agency), Qadariyyah (who affirm creative power for humans), Rawafid (rejecters of the majority of Companions, especially Abu Bakr and Umar), Khawarij (those who revolted against Ali), Mu'attilah (those who strip God of attributes, including philosophers who posit emanation of intellects), and Mushabbihah (those who anthropomorphize God). Each sect is said to have twelve subgroups, totaling seventy-two. The core ruling states that even if a person performs acts of worship all their life, if they hold beliefs like the pre-eternity of the world, denial of resurrection, or denial of God's knowledge of particulars, they are not considered from Ahl al-Qibla (i.e., Muslims). Their testimony is therefore rejected. The commentary then expands each sect's definition and their refutation. The Jabriyyah are refuted by the fact that reward and punishment would be meaningless if humans had no choice. The Qadariyyah are refuted by the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' (Surah al-Saffat 96), which attributes all actions to Allah. The Rawafid are noted for rejecting the first two caliphs and the practice of wiping over leather socks, and for cursing Mu'awiyah. The Khawarij are known for their rebellion against Ali and slandering his family. The Mu'attilah are identified with the philosophy of emanation, which denies that God directly creates the world. The Mushabbihah are divided into extremists who believe God is a body and moderates who say He is a body unlike any other. After explaining each sect, the text notes that each has twelve subdivisions, as confirmed in later Hanafi works like al-Durr al-Mukhtar. A secondary opinion from al-Birjandi lists the major sects differently, totaling seventy-two groups. Finally, the hadith of the seventy-three sects is cited: the saved sect is the one that follows the way of the Prophet and his Companions. Thus, testimony from those outside this saved sect is rejected. The Hanafi position is that such beliefs remove a person from the fold of Islam, making their witness invalid.

Key Terms
الجبرية (al-Jabriyyah): Those who claim that the human being is compelled (mujbar) and has no power at all over his actions.
القدرية (al-Qadariyyah): Those who claim that the human being has a creative power (khaliqah) over his actions, independent of Allah.
الروافض (al-Rawafid): Those who rejected the majority of the Companions, denied the caliphate of Abu Bakr and Umar, and reject wiping over leather socks.
الخوارج (al-Khawarij): Those who deviated from the straight path, fought against Ali, and reviled his family.
المعطلة (al-Mu'attilah): Those who strip Allah of attributes; specifically the philosophers who claim emanation of intellects.
المشبهة (al-Mushabbihah): Those who liken Allah to creation and affirm corporeality for Him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the status of a person who performs all acts of worship but believes in the pre-eternity of the world?
A) He is considered a Muslim but his testimony is rejected.
B) He is not from Ahl al-Qibla and his testimony is rejected.
C) He is a fasiq whose testimony is accepted after repentance.
D) He is a true believer because of his devotion.

Key Takeaway
Correct Islamic creed is a fundamental condition for the acceptance of testimony; those who belong to the six listed sects are not considered Muslims, and their testimony is rejected.
